# 玉清无极总真文昌大洞仙经

**Preface and Memorial to the Throne of *The Jade Purity Ultimate Perfection Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture with Commentary***

**Title:** *The Jade Purity Ultimate Perfection Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture with Commentary*. Compiled by Daoist Wei Qi of the Yuan dynasty, completed in the third year of the Zhida era. This work employs the principles of *tushu* divination and Internal Alchemy to annotate *The Great Cavern Scripture*, compiled by a Daoist of the Southern Song. Ten fascicles. Source text: *Daoist Canon of the Zhengtong Era*, *Yujue* category of the *Dongzhen* section.

**Fascicle One: Preface and Memorial Illustrations**

**Memorial Presenting the Scripture**

Your humble subject, Wei Qi, respectfully states:
The celestial nature of life is bestowed by the One Origin at birth. The Dao shapes all forms, and the myriad beings share their essence with the Five Planets. With utmost reverence, we reflect upon Your Imperial Majesty—whose Dao aligns with the vast heavens, whose virtue merges with the divine. You perpetually revive the pristine customs of remote antiquity, far extending the grand legacy of bygone ages. The jade tablets and golden records of scripture are all reverently studied and practiced; those who dwell in mountain caves and wild places are universally elevated and promoted. Thus, moved by the fervor of the rustic and the boundless grace of Your Majesty’s clemency, I humbly present *The Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture*, praying for Your Sacred Person’s eternal longevity. May Your Yao-like benevolence broadly shelter all, Your sagely governance flourish in cultural splendor, Your Shun-like filial piety shine resplendently, and Your glorious era’s fortune be grandly manifest. As the jade candle harmonizes, spring burgeons and autumn sobers; as the celestial pivot turns, clouds nourish and stars gleam. Heaven and Earth assume their rightful places, the myriad beings are nurtured; transformation reaches its utmost bounds. Sun and moon illuminate, the four seasons proceed—sincerity thus aids both the hidden and the manifest.

Your subject, Qi, presumptuously affronts Heaven’s majesty; my humble heart cannot bear the awe of gazing upon Your Sacred Presence. With utmost trepidation and reverence, I bow twice and present this memorial for Your Majesty’s perusal.

Presented on a day in the ninth month of the third year of the Zhida era.
Your subject, Wei Qi, respectfully memorializes.

**Memorial to the Empress Dowager**

Your humble subject, Wei Qi, respectfully states:
The foundation of royal transformation is recorded in the ancient classics, from Tairen to Taisi. The origins of the *Guofeng* lie in the reverence for You Song and the esteem for the women of Jie and Xin. With utmost reverence, we reflect upon Her Imperial Highness the Empress Dowager—whose virtuous model is gentle and harmonious, whose graceful demeanor is pure and refined. Her aspirations, serene, align with the workings of Heaven; her virtue, upright, accords with Earth’s pattern. She stirs the awe of the hundred clans, guiding all to the realm of longevity. I, Qi, have long concealed my traces on Penglai, drifting like duckweed or tumbleweed in humble existence. Knowing well the Empress’s reception of Heaven’s blessings, I dare present *The Wenchang Scripture* in prayer and praise. May the moon’s radiance shimmer in splendor, emulating Heaven’s image to govern the Six Palaces; may the teachings of Yin flourish in clarity, embodying Earth’s origin to nurture the myriad beings. May the people, as children, universally bask in Her compassionate shade; may Hua and Yi alike be enveloped in Her singular grace.

Your subject, Qi, presumptuously affronts Her august kindness; my humble heart cannot bear the terror of hoping for Her favor. With utmost reverence and awe, I bow twice and respectfully submit this memorial.

Presented on a day in the ninth month of the third year of the Zhida era.
Your subject, Wei Qi, respectfully memorializes.

**Preface**

The Scripture is the guiding principle of the Dao. How could the Dao be contained in words? Yet the supreme sages, through words, composed texts, and through texts, expounded teachings—thereby ordering the world’s Way in ways beyond mortal comprehension. Thus, all scriptures possess ineffable subtleties. In recent times, scholars have parsed their phrases and annotated their chapters, often grasping the intent of the celestial and human in their explanations. Such is the case with the *Great Cavern Scripture*. Originating from the Primordial Beginning, its words plumb the profound and embrace the numinous, transcending truth through kalpas—truly what is called "wondrous."

Now, Master Wei of Zhongyang has ventured to compose new annotations for it, carving them for circulation. Having met me in the capital, he sought a preface. Upon examining his work, I found its depths unfathomable—truly beyond mortal comprehension. Yet I have heard that the purpose of expounding scripture lies in its myriad recitations, and those who embody the Dao savor it profoundly. In this, the Master has surely attained insight. If one grasps the meaning beyond the savor, then from myriad recitations one arrives at wordlessness, and the path to the Primordial Beginning’s revealed realm is without duality.

Composed in the fifth month of summer, the *renzi* year of the Huangqing era.
By special grace, the Perfected of Great Simplicity, Concentrated Spirit, Vast Dao, and Illuminated Virtue; the Thirty-Eighth Celestial Master of the Han Succession; Grand Master for Glorious Happiness; and Duke of Liu, Zhang Yucai.

---

The *Great Cavern Immortal Scripture* originated in Western Shu, and the Central Plains had not yet seen it. Master Wei of Zhongyang, arriving in the capital from Pengshan, presented me with a volume and requested a preface. Upon careful examination, I found it to expound teachings beyond the mundane. The Master has interwoven annotations from the Three Teachings’ sages, their purport profound and far-reaching. Without a thorough understanding of the Three Teachings’ texts, it would be difficult to grasp. Yet one phrase—*"the jade chamber where yin and yang merge as one"*—and its annotation on the union of yin and yang verge on the carnal. Could Master Wei have tailored this for the present age? Still, one must be wary of "explaining dreams to a fool."

Moreover, the Western Sage once said: *"From the Deer Park to the River of Crossing, not a single word was spoken in between."* Our Master Confucius also declared: *"What does Heaven say? The four seasons proceed, and the myriad things are born."* The Old Sage likewise taught: *"Excessive speech leads to exhaustion; better to abide in the center."* Thus, language and writing are but expedients by which sages reveal the Dao when unavoidable. If one attains the Dao, what need remains for words or writing? What does the Master of Zhongyang make of this view?

Respectfully inscribed on the full moon of the *Qinghe* month, the fourth year of the Zhida era.
By Hanlin Academician, Grand Master for Thorough Counsel, Drafter of Edicts, and Compiler of the National History, Zhang Zhongshou of Chouzai Studio.

---

Before the tortoise and horse [emblems of the Han] appeared, the Five Scripts had already manifested in the *Lingbao* texts. The flourishing of the celestial Way and this culture is like nurturing primordial qi—vast and self-subsistent. The more it is muddied, the clearer it becomes; the more it is obscured, the brighter it shines. It knows no interruption, no existence or extinction. The fires of kalpas cannot burn it; the vicissitudes of ages cannot alter it. Lofty and abiding above, were it not for the unyielding integrity, purity, and essence of its nature, its mechanism would cease. Thus, the ceaseless operation of form and nature is governed by what may be called the Emperor.

The Old Immortal of Sevenfold Curves, through meritorious conduct and virtue, has illuminated the warp and weft of scripture with divine clarity. How vast is the Emperor’s power! Holding this register of scripture, he awakens all beings, for it is the pivot of creation, the source of nature and life. The Governor resides herein—from before the first form arose to the boundless reaches beyond the four directions. Vast and empty! The ten thousand differences share one root; a thousand kalpas follow one path. Viewed through the Dharma-eye, it is utterly unobstructed.

What I call the *Great Simplicity*, *Great Beginning*, *Great Origin*, *Great Primal*, and *Great Ultimate* is none other than the *Wenchang Great Cavern* transmitted by the Primordial Beginning. Master Wei of Zhongyang has plumbed its mysteries, parsing its phrases and explicating its characters. Grounded in the learning of the Dao, the principles of nature, the alchemical formulas, and the mechanisms of Chan, he has thoroughly revealed the heart-mind methods of sages across the ages, leaving no residue. Lofty and abiding above, it is overseen by the divine. Readers, take heed!

Respectfully inscribed on an early summer day, the *xinhai* year of the Zhida era.
By Expectant Academician of the Jixian Institute and Grand Master for Palace Attendance, Zhao Jiong of Shu, with bowed hands.

---

**Preface to the Annotated *Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture***

I have heard that the jade of the Mystic Garden, the gold of Kunwu, the luminous pearl of Zhao, and the jade disk of Liancheng—whether dredged from Hepu, mined from Kunlun, or bearing names like "Bright Moon" or "Radiant Raiment"—were treasured by Bian He and cherished by the Marquis of Sui. Though the world may have heard of them, few have seen them, yet all revere and long to behold them. How much more so for the *Dark Pearl*, the *Grain of Millet*, the *Canghu Jiemo Pearl*—treasures prized by gods and humans? Such is the *Wenchang Great Cavern*.

It resides within all yet remains unseen and unvalued by its bearers, who discard and scorn it. Thus, the sages expounded it to awaken beings, employing metaphors drawn from dharmic forms—not as tangible traces, but as radiant qi transformed into sound, not as written words. The supreme Dao is wordless; the supreme truth is imageless. Since the division of the undifferentiated, the principles of the Three Powers have become manifest, and the body of primordial transformation has returned to unity. One knows not whether the Dao is me or I am the Dao. Yet after the Five Phases fell into disorder and qi’s movements shifted, the root of life became constrained by governance. Thus, the Three Treasures Lord once again revealed the original cause to gods and humans: *"The qi of your bodies is my qi; the spirit of your beings is my truth."* He desired that all people awaken to this, seeing that they might return to me and no longer be bound by qi’s movements, thereby attaining the natural effortlessly.

For this reason, the Primordial Beginning re-expounded the thirty-six chapters’ secrets, comprising 3,188 words, and entrusted them to the Jade Emperor Dao Lord. He composed a preface recounting their origins, totaling 908 words, and bestowed it upon the Great Mystery Dao Father. The two sages’ dharma-words together number 4,096.

Thus, though the Perfect Truth bears no form, the traces of the sages grew ever more manifest; though the True Lord spoke no words, the mysterious scriptures flourished in abundance. Embracing heaven and earth, shaping the myriad things with subtle art—how vast is this supreme treasure! Truly it is said: *"Only the Creative Beginning can bestow the finest blessings upon the world."*

Now, the thirty-six chapters correspond to the four nines of the Metal tally, embodying the Way of the Golden Elixir within oneself. The upper scroll contains ten chapters, the middle scroll ten, and the lower scroll sixteen—all three scrolls composed in five-character lines, totaling thirty-six chapters. Above these chapters stands the *"Great Cavern Sovereign of the Imperial Honored One,"* a single chapter in four-character lines, distinct in form and placed at the head of the entire scripture.

Each of the three scrolls is prefaced by an introductory sutra, and the lower scroll concludes with a closing sutra—all expounded by the Jade Emperor Dao Lord—thus revealing the full scope of the text from beginning to end. In the early Zhou dynasty, the Celestial Emperor commanded the Three Perfected Ones to transmit it to Master Zhang Tongzhen of the Grand Assembly. This is that very scripture. By reckoning the time, more than twenty-five hundred years have passed since then.

There exists a version by Wei Yuanjun of Maoshan, titled *The Supreme Clarity Great Cavern Jade Scripture*, said to have been transmitted by the Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy. Compared to this text, it lacks two chapters and contains eighty additional characters. Another version, from the time of Emperor Ming of the Liu Song, by Lu Xiujing, appends the *"First of the Emperor,"* *"Feminine One,"* and *"Masculine One"* scriptures—some in three-character lines, others in four, with irregular meter—to the respective chapters, resulting in a greater number of verses, though the main text remains the same.

Examining the records, it is written: During the Tang dynasty, the Perfected Wang Baohe of Zizhou, by imperial command, collated *The Thirty-Nine Chapters Great Cavern Scripture* and transmitted it to his successor. In the reign of Emperor Zhenzong of the Song, Master Zhu Ziying of the Observing Mystery wrote a commentary, and in the first year of the Zhenghe era, Zhang Shangying presented a memorial to the throne—both largely in accord with this text. Originally comprising one hundred and twenty scrolls, the Jade Emperor Dao Lord and Niu Ziming, the Great Mystery Dao Father, distilled its essentials, divided its chapters and verses, and arranged the thirty-six chapters into three scrolls for ease of cultivation.

Above, it stabilizes the thirty-six heavens; below, it governs the thirty-six earths; and within, it connects the qi of the thirty-six palaces of the human body. Is this not what is meant by *"thirty-six above in heaven, thirty-six below on earth, boundless the Great Mystery—how wondrous the* Great Cavern Scripture!"* The scripture records the hidden names and taboo titles of celestial perfected beings, linking them to the qi and spirits within the human body. Thus, it stands above the *"Salvation of Humanity,"* *"Birth of the Divine,"* and *"Yellow Court"* scriptures. For this reason, inner and outer illuminate each other, above and below intertwine—all drawn from the microcosm of the human body as a small heaven and earth.

If one can nurture their own spirit and qi, chanting the precious chapters, then the celestial perfected will descend and merge with the qi and spirits within one’s body. This is called *"returning wind and blending harmoniously,"* where form and spirit attain perfection, uniting with the Dao in truth. Thus, the Way of longevity is achieved, enabling one to grasp heaven and earth, seize yin and yang, command wind and thunder, and dispatch gods and ghosts. One may recline in the carriage of flowing clouds, gazing upon the Terrace of Literary Florescence.

Yet people merely know that reciting the scripture leads to death, and not reciting it also leads to death—how can there be a principle of longevity? They fail to realize that reciting the scripture allows one to shed the illusory body and attain the true form, called *"liberation from the corpse."* Those who do not recite it perish along with their illusory body and true form alike. The sharpest of roots understand without being told, while the foolish and unworthy, though admonished repeatedly, remain utterly oblivious. Moreover, the chapters, verses, and meanings are profound and obscure—who but a heavenly being reborn could comprehend them?

In my youth, I was instructed in proper conduct and studied the various masters and hundred schools without exception. In the *yisi-mao* year of the Zhiyuan era, at the age of twenty, I received and recited this scripture. Now, thirty years have passed, and I have only lamented the corruption of the text—nine out of ten copies diverge, leaving no standard to follow. I often recalled that in my childhood, I had read the Three Treasuries and remembered a character or two, yet dared not presume to correct the errors myself. Moreover, after the great refining furnace of the world’s teachings, the true scriptures have all but vanished.

In recent years, while holding minor office in the southwest, I urged others to study this text, visiting every household. Many took to reading it, but I, having transmitted errors in turn, found little peace in my heart. Recently, wandering by rivers and lakes, I sat in quietude at an inn and gained sudden insight. I then reviewed my former annotations, comparing them with the Three Teachings’ scriptures I had once memorized, and where their meanings aligned, I provided explanations verse by verse. Following the *Great Change*’s principles of the Limitless, the Yellow River and Luo River diagrams, the pre- and post-heaven trigrams, the firing times of the Golden Elixir, and the celestial qi of the Imperial Honored One, I arranged thirteen illustrations to precede the scripture, so that one might grasp its meaning at a glance.

Yet my humble insights are shallow and crude, and I fear incurring the censure of heaven and the ridicule of the learned. Only after respectfully presenting this to the Investigating Commissioner of the Perfected Lord of Life and receiving his unseen approval did I dare share it with like-minded seekers. This is not to glorify the great scripture but merely to illuminate it for those of modest capacity. Written in the *jiyou* year of the Zhida era, in the eastern mountains of Shu, by Zhongyangzi Wei Qi of Penglai Mountain, who bows in reverence and respectfully presents this preface.

The *Illustration of the Ultimateless*
Zhou Dunyi created the *Taiji* to encompass the *Book of Changes*; I expound the Ultimateless to summarize the *Great Cavern*. For the *Taiji* already embodies the forms and qi, while the Ultimateless is without sound, without scent, without image, without name—only principle remains.

Zhou Dunyi also said: "The Ultimateless and yet the Supreme Ultimate." When the Ultimateless moves, it becomes yang and generates primordial qi, which pertains to water—thus called *Taiyi* (Great Simplicity), giving rise to primordial light. When it stills, it becomes yin and generates original qi, which pertains to fire—thus called *Yuanming* (Original Destiny), giving rise to *Taichu* (Great Beginning). When stillness reaches its extreme and reverts to movement, it becomes yang and generates inceptional qi, which pertains to wood—thus called *Taishi* (Great Inception). When the three qi cycle, the primordial, original, and inceptional qi are complete, and qi, form, and substance are fully possessed yet never separate—this is called *Taisu* (Great Simplicity). When it stills, it becomes yin and pertains to metal—thus called *Taisu*. The initial three qi of the Brahma-conduct form the root of heaven and earth, and all things attain their proper positions—this is called *Taiji* (Supreme Ultimate). When it moves, it becomes yang and pertains to earth, governing the Four Images—thus called *Taiji Wuling Chong* (Supreme Ultimate of Five Spirits in Harmony). Movement and stillness alternate as each other’s root; therefore, the Five Ultimates and Five Phases are called the Five Elders. The *Five Talismans Jade Scripture* states they were born before the Original Beginning.

The Heavenly King further unfolded the primordial qi of *Taiyi*, condensing it into a single ○ precious pearl—this is the Five Phases as one yin-yang, yin-yang as one *Taiji*, and the *Taiji* as fundamentally the Ultimateless. Thus it is said: "The Ultimateless governs the true script of the Wenchang Great Cavern."

I take this ○ precious light and condense it into the myriad qi, which transform and give birth to the various heavens. Again, I distribute its light into hundreds, thousands, and myriads of billions, forming the *Great Cavern Immortal Scripture*—the Jade Scripture that establishes heaven and earth and enlightens the divine spirits. It is also said: "The Five Qi knit the ten directions; the myriad qi generate the myriad spirits"—this is the Five Phases unfolding in sequence, with the four seasons proceeding accordingly. The *Scripture of Salvation* states: "The Five Scripts open the expanse, universally planting divine spirits. Without script, there is no light—equal to the myriad spirits and myriad qi of immortals." This is the true essence of the Ultimateless, the essence of the Two and Five, where the two qi interact and transform to generate the myriad things. Thus, Wenchang is the ancestor of heaven and earth, the mother of the myriad things. Therefore, every person possesses a Wenchang, and every thing possesses a *Taiji*.

If one can diligently cultivate and refine the Way of the Wenchang Great Cavern, one will ultimately return to the midst of the Ultimateless—emptiness and spontaneity. Human life naturally arises from nothingness, and in old age, returns to nothingness. By examining the *Illustration of the Ultimateless*, one knows that the two qi and Five Phases originate from the two qi—yin and yang—and the Five Phases are water, fire, wood, metal, and earth. Principle gives rise to qi, and qi gives rise to script. Script refers to the Heavenly Stems and Earthly Branches.

Yang moves and generates *renzi* (Yang Water), the first number; yin stills and generates *dingsi* (Yin Fire), the second number; it moves again and generates *jia-yin* (Yang Wood), the third number; it stills again and generates *xinyou* (Yin Metal), the fourth number; it moves and generates *wuchen-xu* (Yang Earth), the fifth number; it stills and forms *guihai* (Yin Water), the sixth number; it moves and forms *bingwu* (Yang Fire), the seventh number; it stills and forms *yimao* (Yin Wood), the eighth number; it moves and forms *gengshen* (Yang Metal), the ninth number; it stills and forms *chou-wei* (Yin Earth), the tenth number.

Though called Heavenly Stems, they also possess yin and yang: *jia, bing, geng, ren, wu* are yang stems, belonging to yang and necessarily moving to form script; *yi, ding, xin, gui, ji* belong to yin and necessarily still to form script. The Earthly Branches also possess yin and yang: *zi, wu, yin, shen, chen, xu* are yang branches; *si, hai, mao, you, chou, wei* are yin branches.

When the Five Scripts are complete, their names are the Five Ultimates. Yet the scripture further speaks of Five Ultimates, making Ten Ultimates—would this not invite the scorn of the discerning? They do not know that each of the Five Phases possesses two qi, which interact to generate the Five Phases. Yang generates as one Ultimate, yin completes as one Ultimate, mutually engendering and transforming to form the script of heaven and earth. The scripture states: "The true script commences with illumination; a spark ignites the true script. The Ten Virtues proclaim the true script; the horizontal script welcomes the Emperor’s sons. The Ten Transcendents knit the human script"—all unfold through the Five Scripts. Thus, heaven, earth, and the myriad things all grow and flourish by means of them.

Some may ask: "The Yellow Emperor commanded Da Nao to explore the essence of the Five Phases and create the *Jiazi* cycle—how could it exist before heaven and earth?" They do not know that the *Jiazi* was born before heaven and earth; this is merely its manifestation through humanity. The Heavenly Sovereign’s *Jiazi* cycle of Ten Stems and Twelve Branches originally began with *Sheti* above *yin*; this is recorded in the *Erya*. Later, Fuxi began from *jia*, saying: "The east’s *jia* is the flourishing virtue of wood, where the myriad things begin to grow"—thus starting the Ten Stems with *jia*. The two qi of yin and yang transform to generate the Heavenly Stems and Earthly Branches. In heaven, they are the celestial patterns; on earth, they are the terrestrial principles. By gazing upward and examining below, exploring the profound and seeking the hidden, and investigating the sources and flows, the sixty *Jiazi* cycles correspond to the sixty stellar positions in the heavens. The qi of the Five Phases transform into the Eight Trigrams, which settle the eight directions. Now, the sixty *Jiazi* and sixty-four hexagrams are distributed throughout the *Cavern Chapters*, all harmonizing with the wondrous Dao.

The qi of the Nine August Upper Perfected is *renzi*, generating the Heavenly One’s water—this is *Taiyi* (Great Simplicity). The pure qi of the Supreme Center’s Six Qi is *guihai*, forming the Earthly Six’s water—this is *Taizhong* (Supreme Center). The qi of the Heavenly August Upper Perfected is *dingsi*, generating the Earthly Two’s fire—this is *Taichu* (Great Beginning). The Yellow Radiance qi of the Morning Center is *bingwu*, forming the Heavenly Seven’s fire—this is *Taihe* (Great Harmony). The qi of the Supreme One’s Upper Prime is *jia-yin*, generating the Heavenly Three’s wood—this is *Taishi* (Great Inception).

The qi of the Golden Watchtower’s Upper Radiance is *yi-mao*, forming the Earthly Eight’s wood—this is *Taiqing* (Great Purity). The Primordial Simplicity’s initial ascetic practice is *xin-you*, generating the Earthly Four’s metal—this is *Taisu* (Primordial Simplicity). The Supreme Perfected’s Ninefold Light Wheel is *geng-shen*, forming the Heavenly Nine’s metal—this is *Taizhen* (Supreme Perfection). The Fivefold Numinous Surge of the Great Ultimate is *wu-chen-xu*, generating the Heavenly Five’s earth—this is *Taiji* (Great Ultimate). The Tenfold Brilliance of the Primordial Mystery is *ji-chou-wei*, forming the Earthly Ten’s earth—this is *Taixuan* (Primordial Mystery).

The classics are the embodiment of numbers; numbers are the function of the classics. Those who cultivate the Way of Wenchang cannot be ignorant of numbers. For heaven and earth operate through numbers, and the myriad things come into being through numbers. Numbers are precisely the movement and stillness of yin and yang within the Great Ultimate.

The *Book of Changes* states: "The numbers of heaven are five; the numbers of earth are five. The five positions interact and each has its correspondence. The numbers of heaven total twenty-five; the numbers of earth total thirty. Together, the numbers of heaven and earth total fifty-five." The *Elixir Classic* says: "East three and south two together make five; north one and west four share the same. *Wu-si* returns to follow the generative number of wood. When the three families meet, they form the infant." This is what is meant by Wenchang.

The Dao is the classic and the *Book of Changes*; the *Book of Changes* is numbers and images. The classic states: "With the qi of the Mysterious One, the sound of the Great Mystery, and the true Way of the August One," and also: "From the wondrous One of the Dao, the root of life-bestowing goodness is conceived. The Mysterious divides the origin, the Beginning transmits the true, and the myriad heavens are transformed and born." Tracing their origins, all arise from the number one.

For when the Mysterious qi moves, it first generates water, then earth and wood; when still, it generates metal and fire. From one to five, the Five Phases are sequentially arrayed. Then six is paired with one to form water; seven with two to form fire; eight with three to form wood; nine with four to form metal; and ten with five to form earth. Thus transformations are accomplished, and the spirits and gods are set in motion.

Before the Great Ultimate divided, these numbers were already latent within the Ultimate of Non-being. Therefore, the generation and completion of heaven, earth, and humanity depend on numbers, and their decay and ruin also depend on numbers—yet the common people use them daily without awareness. When the sage Fuxi emerged, moved by the dragon-horse bearing the River Chart, he followed its patterns to draw the eight trigrams.

Those who understand these numbers find the Way of nature and life within them, and thus Wenchang is fully encompassed. Therefore, the lower scroll speaks of the Five Greatnesses, Five Phases, Five Elders, and Five Talismans—all that generates heaven, establishes earth, and nurtures humanity—none of which do not originate from the Nine Palaces and Eight Trigrams. For the palaces and trigrams arise from the two qi and the Five Phases, and these two and five in turn emerge from the Great Ultimate and the Ultimate of Non-being.

Fuxi was a great sage who meditated deeply on the supreme Way, his spirit moving heaven. Tracing the origins of heaven and earth and following the transformations of Pangu, he took his own body’s hair and skin as the images of the trigrams. When Jizi composed the *Hongfan*, the nine and five blessings were: first, longevity; second, wealth; third, health and peace; fourth, the love of virtue; fifth, a natural end to life. These five blessings are what all people in the world desire, yet they do not know the Way by which to cultivate and advance toward them. This begins with the Luo Diagram. The Nine Palaces of the Luo Diagram are the "use of nine" in the *Book of Changes* and the "demonstration of nine" in *Wenchang*. Those who apply their minds to this will find the *Book of Changes*’ pure *Qian* and *Wenchang*’s pure yang converging without prior agreement. Thus it is said: "The noble person works unceasingly all day, striving to improve without rest," and also: "Continuous as if existing"—this is what is meant by seeking blessings without deviation.

The Luo Diagram is: wearing nine on the head and treading one underfoot, three on the left and seven on the right, two and four as the shoulders, six and eight as the feet. By regulating the qi’s flow in both forward and reverse, traversing the Nine Palaces, the sums of the vertical and horizontal lines are all fifteen. Interwoven with the River Chart, they form the Way of the Three Powers—truly the numbers that warp heaven and weft earth.

After the undifferentiated chaos divided, the myriad things relied on it to come into being. When the Luo tortoise emerged bearing its patterns in the time of Great Yu, the images and numbers first became efficacious. Yu used them to regulate the waters and arrange the Nine Categories. Jizi followed them to compose the *Hongfan*, King Wen followed them to rearrange the positions of the trigrams—these were the numbers of the Great Ultimate. Thus *Wenchang* states: "Demonstrating the methods of the nine governances, transmitting the talismans of the nine lights"—all employing nine, for nine is the number of pure yang. Therefore, the classic has thirty-six chapters, just as *Qian*’s "use of nine" is no different. This is the root of nature and life within the Three Powers, the Way of simplicity spoken of in the *Taiyi*—yet people are unaware of it, and some drift into the schools of yin-yang and geomancy.

Those who seek the five blessings of the *Hongfan* must thoroughly investigate the nine numbers of *Wenchang* before they can succeed. Above are the Nine Heavens, and the human head also has nine palaces to correspond to them. The earth has nine provinces, and the human body has nine orifices to correspond to them. The Dipper has nine origins, and the human heart has nine apertures to correspond to them. Water has nine rivers, and the human intestines have nine curves to correspond to them.

Nine is the number of yang, and humanity cannot live without yang. Yu grieved over Gun’s execution and meditated in profound resonance, desiring to restore the great work. Thus heaven bestowed upon him the governance of the waters, all in accord with the substance and function of heaven and earth’s great transformations.

The River Chart emerged thousands of years before the Luo Diagram, which is why Fuxi was able to draw the Former Heaven Eight Trigrams—these were the fifty-five numbers contained within the Great Ultimate. In drawing the trigrams, there seemed to be an order, yet many predecessors took the nine numbers of the Luo Diagram to be the River Chart. Liu Mu followed this transmission, and it has persisted to this day. Here, through exploration within *Wenchang*, it is found that the River Chart corresponds to ten, while the Luo Diagram corresponds to nine. Thus their sequence is set forth: within the Ultimate of Non-being, this structure was already present, though its secrets remained hidden. Only when the dragon-horse bore the chart in Fuxi’s time did it emerge, and he drew the eight trigrams accordingly. Taking the odd, light, and pure numbers one, five, and seven as yang, he placed them above to form *Qian* heaven. Taking the even, heavy, and turbid numbers two, six, and ten as yin, he placed them below to form *Kun* earth. This is called "the positions of heaven and earth are fixed"—it is the Great Ultimate generating the Two Modes.

Taking the five numbers and pairing them with one, two, three, and four to form Old Yin, Old Yang, Young Yin, and Young Yang—this is the Two Modes generating the Four Images. By interweaving the numbers six, seven, eight, nine, and ten, the eight trigrams are formed: one *Qian*, two *Dui*, three *Li*, four *Zhen*, five *Xun*, six *Kan*, seven *Gen*, and eight *Kun*. Their symbolic correspondences are taken in opposition: thunder and wind press upon each other, mountains and marshes exchange qi, water and fire do not repel—whether arranged vertically or horizontally, the total is nine. This is called the Four Images generating the eight trigrams.

Thus, the roundness of a person’s head resembles *Qian* heaven, the squareness of the feet resembles *Kun* earth, the body resembles *Gen* mountain, the bodily fluids resemble *Dui* marsh, the voice resembles *Zhen* thunder, the breath resembles *Xun* wind, the blood and nourishment resemble *Kan* water, and the defensive qi resembles *Li* fire—are not the eight trigrams all present within us?

Therefore, in aligning the *Yi* with the principles of the *Cantong Qi*, the teachings of *Wenchang* and the *Dadong* are especially profound and obscure. Some find them difficult to comprehend and are unwilling to recite them. Thus, I have now drawn from the more accessible meanings in various scriptures to synthesize them, so that devout men and women, regardless of wisdom or folly, may all attain understanding.

Before heaven and earth were separated, their form was like a hen’s egg. Within it was Hundun, who took the clear as heaven and the turbid as earth. Hundun grew one *zhang* each day, and heaven and earth opened by one *zhang* each day. His eyes became the sun and moon, his body the mountains, his hair the grasses and trees, and his bodily fluids the waters—this was Pangu.

The Luo Diagram emerged thousands of years after the River Chart. Yu the Great obtained it to regulate the waters—this too is the Five Agents within the Great Ultimate.

Is the purpose of the charts and diagrams merely to draw trigrams and regulate waters? No—it is truly the substance and function of nature and destiny. Without the pre- and post-heavenly charts, their essence could not be revealed, and without the pre- and post-heavenly *Yi* and *Wenchang*, their function could not be manifested. Thus, essence and function are mutually inclusive, nature and destiny illuminate each other—neither can be lacking. I respectfully record both to share with like-minded seekers.

The scripture states: "The Eight Sovereigns govern the Nine Heavens"—these are the eight trigrams and the nine palaces. The eight numbers and nine chapters form an outer and inner correspondence, so the River Chart and Luo Diagram serve as warp and weft. They existed already in the pre-heavenly and pre-earthly state. King Wen later took the River and Luo, carefully examined them, and rearranged the eight trigrams. Thus, *Qian* and *Kun*, as Old Yang and Old Yin, already contained the three sons and three daughters, and so they were retired to the positions of non-use. Therefore, in the *Yi*, *Qian* is placed in the northwest, *Kun* is moved to the southwest, *Kan* and *Li* (yin and yang) properly intersect at the central palace, occupying the due north and south positions. *Zhen*, as the initial intersection of yang, is placed in the east; *Dui*, as the beginning of yin’s intersection, is established in the due west. *Gen* and *Xun*, being mixed yin and yang without mutual resonance, are positioned in the outlying corners.

The post-heavenly eight trigrams circulate among the nine palaces, with five residing at the center and lodging its position in two—this is called "two and five share the same function." The *Yi* states: "The Lord emerges from *Zhen*, aligns with *Xun*, appears in *Li*, labors in *Kun*, delights in speech in *Dui*, battles in *Qian*, toils in *Kan*, and completes speech in *Gen.*" Thus the four seasons proceed, the myriad things are born, and the *Yi* operates throughout heaven and earth.

How could *Wenchang* and the *Yi* be unrelated? For the human body is a small heaven and earth, and *Wenchang* weaves its warp and weft within it. If one can preserve wholeness and return to this, one does not betray the transformative nurturing of the sages, and this scripture is not mere empty text.

The Nine Radiance Talisman is the congealed script of the Primordial Chaos Red Writ and the Nine Yang Brahman qi. First, the initial green radiance begins the Green Heaven, condensing the Great Empyrean Palace in the northeast. Next, the Great Green radiance opens the Great Green Heaven, condensing the Azure Empyrean Palace in the east. Then, the initial cinnabar radiance begins the Cinnabar Heaven, condensing the Bluegreen Empyrean Palace in the southeast. Next, the Great Cinnabar radiance opens the Great Cinnabar Heaven, condensing the Crimson Empyrean Palace in the south. Then, the initial white radiance begins the White Heaven, condensing the Scenic Empyrean Palace in the southwest. Next, the Great White radiance opens the Great White Heaven, condensing the Jade Empyrean Palace in the west. Then, the initial black radiance begins the Black Heaven, condensing the Jadeite Empyrean Palace in the northwest. Next, the Great Black radiance opens the Great Black Heaven, condensing the Purple Empyrean Palace in the north. Finally, the Great Brahman radiance opens the Great Brahman Heaven, condensing the Divine Empyrean Palace at the center.

The Nine Governances: one emperor governs the affairs of all heavens, hence it is called the method of demonstrating the Nine Governances. The Nine Radiance Talisman is transmitted to assemble the spirits. When a person is first born, they receive the qi of the Nine Heavens and thus possess form and spirit. The cultivator completes nine months of practice, and in the tenth month, the sacred embryo is formed—only then can it be nurtured. The perfected ones condense the nine qi into script, calling it the Nine Radiance Talisman, to deliver beings in heaven and earth. This is fully recorded in the registers of the methods.

Here, the Divine Empyrean generates the spirits of the Nine Heavens: above, it governs the thirty-six stellar luminaries of the heavens; below, it governs the thirty-six earthly sovereigns of the fortresses; and in the middle, it governs the thirty-six palaces within the human body. These thirty-six palaces are all infused by the true qi distributed from the upper heavens, irrigating the chambers—only then is a person formed. The *Lesser Scripture of Salvation from Suffering* states: "Return the qi of the upper heavens to control the souls of the Nine Heavens."

The thirty-six heavens and thirty-six earths are detailed in their respective chapters. Now, the thirty-six palaces of the human body are divided into the upper, middle, and lower sections for distribution. When reciting this scripture, one must calm the mind, sit in silence, and visualize the thirty-six palaces within one’s own heart shining brilliantly. Within each palace resides a perfected one, emitting five-colored radiance—above connecting to the thirty-six heavens, below connecting to the thirty-six earths—so that spirit and qi congeal and communicate between above and below. This is what is meant by "the method of the Nine Governances to assemble the emperor, the Nine Radiance Talisman to gather the spirits."

When the radiance and qi have congealed and stabilized, then regulate the voice and rectify the qi, chanting the cavernous chapters. Nine recitations constitute one cycle. After each recitation, dedicate the merit to the perfected ones above, the ghosts and spirits of the middle and lower realms, and the consciousness of one’s own ancestors—bestowing blessings upon each as desired. Sit briefly to allow the spirit and qi to disperse slightly, then rise from the seat unhurriedly. Do not act abruptly, lest the divine radiance be disturbed and the ghosts and spirits rebuke. During scripture recitation, one must not speak. The following is now revealed:

The Golden Elixir is the single point of true yang within the human body, co-emergent with Heaven and Earth, co-luminous with the sun and moon. When it scatters, it becomes a person; when it gathers, it forms the Elixir. The scripture calls it the "Mother of the Elixir," the perfection of true yang.

True yang is lead, born in Kun, which is Earth—termed the "Mysterious Fire of the Dark King." The seed of mercury resides in Qian, which is Heaven, thus enabling the seizure of Heaven and Earth as the crucible and cauldron. It is called "the King of the Dipper in the sun’s embrace, the Feathered One in the moon’s dawn," hence the ability to gather the sun and moon as medicinal substances. It is termed "the dark transformation of Kan’s fusion, the union of yin and yang in the Jade Chamber," where the Yellow Dame serves as the matchmaker, uniting Wood Lord and Metal Mother in harmonious resonance. It is called "the Purple Flower nurturing the embryo," signifying the completion of the sacred fetus in ten months. It is called "the Infant as the Crimson Child," when the yang spirit suddenly manifests in form. The "fusion of the Three and Five Palaces" refers to pursuing the two qi along the Yellow Path and uniting the three natures in the Primordial Palace. The "five qi binding the ten directions and clustering the five phases" denotes the convergence of the five agents. The "Supreme Ultimate governing the Four Perfected" signifies the harmonization of the four images. The "Yellow Court traversing the Northern Primordial" describes true yang ascending to the heart’s palace. The "nine cycles returning to seven" refers to the advancing and retreating, drawing and adding of the *Yi* hexagrams as the fire-timing of the celestial revolution. The "embodiment of the precious pearl illuminating the Mysterious Azure and the Barbarian Pearl" signifies the instantaneous completion of the Golden Elixir with a moment’s effort. The "nurturing and refining of the Five Sprouts Pearl" means that by ingesting this Golden Elixir, one attains the rank of Great Cavern Heaven’s Imperial Perfected.

The scripture’s discourse on the Golden Elixir is manifold; here, only its essentials are briefly outlined.

The "Center" is the center within the center—neither above nor below, neither edge nor side. The Buddhists say: "Neither thinking of good nor evil, in this very moment, one sees the original face." The Confucians call it "tranquil and unmoving," while the Daoists term it the "thought-moment." It cannot be sought through sound or scent, nor grasped through form or appearance. It is perpetually empty, numinous, and unwavering. If one threads through it, this aperture will not shine.

Formerly, when Xue Youqi annotated the *Lingbao Scripture*, he was visited by two immortals, the Twin Boys and Master Ban Bai. In their discourse on the Dao, they spoke of the wonders of the Five Perfected roaming the spirit, which refers precisely to this.

The Five Spirits reside in Heaven, in humans, and in things, all governing the affairs of generation and transformation. Without this spirit to preside over the ceaseless movement of life, the mechanism would cease. Thus, the *Scripture of Salvation* states: "Grasping talismans and holding registers, one preserves life and roots existence, moving in and out of the Flowery Chambers, within the eight obscurities and the subtlest realms, descending to guard the Mud Pill Palace and Crimson Palace of the human body." Therefore, scriptures such as the *Wenchang*, *Lingbao*, *Yellow Court*, and *Engendering the Spirit* all expound upon this.

The Five Spirits disperse into the myriad spirits, but when gathered, they revert to the single Infant. The names of the myriad spirits cannot be exhaustively recorded; here, only the essentials are briefly presented to facilitate contemplation. Through concentrated thought and profound visualization, they will naturally resonate and manifest within one’s own body. The following is now revealed:

The human body is formed by the congealing of the myriad qi, and life begins when the myriad spirits are complete. At birth, one is an infant, purely harmonious and serene, with the heavenly principle undifferentiated—this is the original body of the Great Cavern’s Imperial Perfected. If one cultivates the *Wenchang* scripture to return to the infant, it is called "the wondrous union of form and spirit."

Once the infant is formed, it transforms into the mysterious qi, termed "ascending into formlessness, merging with the Dao, and returning to the Ultimate Nonbeing." Only then does one realize that the root-source arises and concludes here.

The *Great Penetration Scripture* states: "True emptiness, without form, is utterly perfect and complete."

*Preface and Charts to the Jade Purity, Ultimate Nonbeing, All-True Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture, Fascicle One*

*(Note: "吏" is likely a scribal error for "史." The phrase "四数" should read "四数也." "炁清" should be "清炁." Two characters in the original text are illegible.)*

*Jade Purity, Ultimate Nonbeing, All-True Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture, Fascicle Two*
*Annotated by Zhongyangzi Wei Qi of Mount Penglai in Eastern Shu*

**Explication of the Scripture’s Title**

**Jade Purity (Yu Qing):** Within Jade Purity already exists the qi of Grand Simplicity (Tai Yi), Grand Beginning (Tai Chu), Grand Commencement (Tai Shi), and Grand Prime (Tai Su). Though form and essence are not yet distinct, there arises the qi of the Great Cavern (Da Dong), the Lofty and Primordial (Gao Shang), the Vast Nonbeing (Hun Dong Tai Wu), the Original Heavenly Treasure (Yuan Tian Bao), and the Jade Sovereign (Yu Huang), from which the Primordial Beginning (Yuan Shi) is born. At that time, it was named the Lofty and Vast Jade Purity Palace (Gao Shang Da You Yu Qing Guan). Thus, the Great Cavern is none other than the Supreme Ultimate (Tai Ji). This era was called the Dragon Han Upper Kalpa (*Long Han Shang Jie*), the time from which the *Wenchang Scripture* emerged.

**Ultimate Nonbeing (Wu Ji):** "Ultimate Nonbeing and yet the Supreme Ultimate—the Supreme Ultimate is fundamentally Ultimate Nonbeing." Prior to the Five Primes (Wu Tai), there was only the profound and formless, beyond all description; hence, it is called Ultimate Nonbeing.

**All-True (Zong Zhen):** This encompasses the names of the celestial perfected, earthly sages, human spirits, and the essences of the six wefts (*liu wei*). Where there is form, there must be qi; where there is qi, there must be principle (*li*). Principle is the heavenly principle (*tian li*), pure and unadulterated, sincere and without falsehood. In Buddhism, it is called *actuality*; in Daoism, *the Real*; in Confucianism, *sincerity*—yet in truth, they are one. Sincerity is the Way of Heaven, fully expounded by Zisi and Mencius. Since this sincere principle exists, there must be that which governs it: the true of Ultimate Nonbeing (*Wu Ji zhi zhen*) spoken of by Master Zhou, the essence of the Two and Five (*er wu zhi jing*). The Dao calls it the profound and obscure essence (*yao ming zhi jing*), most truly real. It is also said, "Within the true there is spirit." Thus, within the Three Powers (*san cai*), each possesses this principle and this spirit to give life.

The *Zhuangzi* states: "Do heaven and earth coexist with me? Do the myriad things and I share the same body?" This scripture encompasses heaven and earth, enfolds the Three Powers, and leaves no place unreal; hence, it is called *All-True*.

**Wenchang:** *Wen* means principle (*li*), like the veins within wood, their patterns interwoven. In ancient times, Cang Jie created characters by modeling forms after categories. *Chang* means flourishing, great—referring to the vast and abundant principles of heaven and earth. For instance, Fu Xi drew the eight trigrams based on the patterns of the River Chart (*He Tu*), establishing the Way of the Three Ultimates (*san ji*). This scripture thoroughly investigates the principles of pattern, nature, and destiny within the Three Powers, all of which emerge from the Two Qi (*er qi*) and Five Phases (*wu xing*). Thus, the Wenchang star is transformed from the qi of earth. The hexagram *Kun* (Earth) states: "Yellow skirts, supremely auspicious—pattern resides within." The hexagram *Gen* (Mountain) states: "Nothing is more flourishing than *Gen* in generating the myriad things; nothing is more complete than *Gen* in perfecting them." Hence, Master Zhou spoke of "yang transforming and yin uniting, thereby giving rise to the Five Phases." The *Scripture of Salvation* (*Du Ren Jing*) says: "The Five Patterns unfold, universally planting spiritual beings." In the southern realm of literary splendor, radiance shines brilliantly. Chapter Fourteen states: "Southern Prosperity (*Nan Chang*) emits jade-like brilliance." This refers to the Southern Prosperity Palace (*Nan Chang Gong*), governed by the Perfected of Refined Souls (*Lian Hun Zhen Ren*), where the Southern Culmen Emperor of Vermilion Numinosity (*Zhu Ling Di Jun*) resides. There, the Eight-Cornered Jade Seal of the Life-Registering Perfected Lord (*Zhu Sheng Zhen Jun*) is bestowed—what is commonly called the Southern Dipper’s life-registering, though here termed *Southern Prosperity* rather than *Wenchang*. This is the realm of literary brilliance in the Cinnabar Heavenly World (*Dan Tian Shi Jie*), transformed by Brahma-qi (*fan qi*), known as the Southern Prosperity Upper Palace (*Nan Chang Shang Gong*). Today, the Vermilion Numinosity Grotto-Heaven (*Zhu Ling Dong Tian*) of Mount Heng in the Southern Marchmount corresponds to the astral mansions of *Kui* (Straddler) and *Zhen* (Winnowing Basket). Initially, the radiance of *Kui* and *Bi* (Wall) descended, and the Emperor commanded their stewardship over culture. *Bi* resides in the *Hai* (12th Earthly Branch) position, governing charts and books; *Kui* resides in the *Xu* (11th Earthly Branch) position, governing literature. For *Kui* possesses literary splendor, and *Bi* stores books. After the fall of the House of Ying, ancient texts were discovered within a wall—thus, *Bi* has contributed to culture. Hence, the Wenchang Palace includes the Eastern Wall Repository of Charts and Books (*Dong Bi Tu Shu Fu*). Within the Supreme Subtlety Enclosure (*Tai Wei Yuan*), there is the Fifth Star of the Southern Dipper, the Perfected Lord of Refined Souls of Wenchang (*Wen Chang Lian Hun Zhen Jun*), as well as the Palace of the Nine Qi of the Grand Supreme Wenchang (*Tai Shang Jiu Qi Wen Chang Gong*), the stars of the Wenchang Upper Minister (*Wen Chang Shang Xiang*), and the Wenchang Upper General (*Ci Xiang Shang Jiang*). There is also the Wenchang Chart of Flowing Circulation (*Wen Chang Tu Liu Yun*), which generates and transforms cultural artifacts. Thus, within heaven and earth, the Way of generation, completion, and transformation is none greater than this. Hence, it is said: "Opening the Three Luminaries, this is the root of heaven. Without pattern, there is no illumination; without pattern, there is no clarity; without pattern, there is no establishment; without pattern, there is no completion; without pattern, there is no deliverance; without pattern, there is no life." All these statements are founded upon this.

The *Book of Changes* states: "Things intermingle; hence, it is called *pattern* (*wen*)." Thus, this *Wenchang Scripture* is the unifying thread, just as the *Appended Judgments* say: "Transforming and moving without abiding, circulating through the six positions, ascending and descending without constancy, adapting to change alone." It also states: "Alternating and combining to change, interweaving their numbers, penetrating their changes to form the patterns of heaven and earth"—this is the same meaning. Therefore, Wenchang in the world is the root-source of education and transformation.

**Great Cavern (Da Dong):** *Great* means that even the vastness of heaven and earth cannot surpass it. *Cavern* means pervading—all things universally possess this principle, which is the Supreme Ultimate. Once the Supreme Ultimate divides, the Three Powers of heaven, earth, and humanity each attain their proper positions. It is said that each thing possesses a Supreme Ultimate; thus, in general, it is called the Great Cavern. This aligns with the teachings expounded by Master Shao and the principles set forth by Jizi in the *Way of the Royal Ultimate* (*Huang Ji*). Among the scriptures and registers of the Daoist methods, the Three Caverns exist, with the Great Cavern being the highest.

**Immortal Scripture (Xian Jing):** *Scripture* (*jing*) means the path (*you*)—the correct way universally traversed by the myriad things. The Confucian classics—*Book of Songs*, *Book of Documents*, *Book of Changes*, *Book of Rites*, *Analects*, *Mencius*, and *Spring and Autumn Annals*—are all scriptures. Cultivating the Dao is called teaching; hence, it is termed *Immortal Scripture*. The Primordial Beginning (*Yuan Shi*) recognized that each person is endowed with this principle, so he clarified the ranks and precepts to serve as the foundation of education and transformation, enabling ghosts, spirits, and humans alike to return to their root-source. By cultivating and advancing where they are endowed, it becomes the swiftest path to learning the Dao and seeking immortality. If one can trace the origin and grasp the end, returning to seek within oneself, then heaven, earth, and the myriad things are all complete within me.

**Wenchang Aligns with the Changes:** The title *Ultimate Nonbeing, All-True Wenchang Great Cavern* appears inverted and improper. It should follow the order: *Ultimate Nonbeing, Wenchang, All-True, Great Cavern*. *Ultimate Nonbeing* refers to the movement and stillness of yin and yang within the Supreme Ultimate. *Wenchang* refers to the Five Phases. *All-True* refers to the Qian Way (*Qian Dao*) forming the male and the Kun Way (*Kun Dao*) forming the female. *Great Cavern* refers to the transformation and generation of the myriad things.

The Scripture states: "The ten thousand qi give birth to the ten thousand spirits." Thus it is said: The *Taiji* Diagram is the *Book of Changes* in its entirety, while the *Wuji* Diagram is the *Wenchang Great Cavern* in its entirety—this has already been made clear within the diagrams. Yet as time passes, change becomes difficult, and lest it sow doubt among the multitude, we provisionally retain the old conventions.

Moreover, this *Scripture* differs not from the *Changes*: the *Changes* takes Qian and Kun as its gate, while the *Scripture* takes heaven and earth as its foundation. The gate is function; the foundation is substance. Look up to observe the patterns of heaven; look down to examine the principles of earth—principles, too, are patterns. The patterns of heaven are the sixty celestial stems and branches, the sun, moon, and stars arrayed across the thirty-two heavens. The patterns of earth are the sixty-four hexagrams aligned with the thirty-six earthly mounds. The patterns of humanity are the qi of the spirits congealed within the thirty-six palaces and three hundred sixty joints of the body—these correspond to the thirty-two heavens beyond the *Duren Scripture*: the Miro Heaven, Qingwei Heaven, Yuyu Heaven, and Great Red Heaven. The thirty-six earths are the nine earthly mounds, each divided into four earthly sovereigns, totaling thirty-six earthly sovereigns, who collectively govern the expanse of the world. When extended, Qian’s tally is two hundred and sixteen, and Kun’s tally is one hundred and forty-four, their combined tally of three hundred and sixty matching the number of degrees in the celestial circuit of the sun. In smaller measure, the yang lines follow this: each yang line is thirty-six, corresponding to the four nines of the metal tally.

Now, the opening chapter of the *Great Cavern* consists of twenty-two four-character lines, totaling eighty-eight characters, placed above to correspond to the *Wuji*. Beyond this, the main text of the five-character scripture comprises thirty-six chapters, totaling six hundred and twenty lines. Each line corresponds to one line of a hexagram in the *Changes*, and the sixty-four hexagrams yield three hundred and eighty-four lines, which are matched by Qian, Kun, Kan, and Li—twenty-four lines in all. The ancients placed these at the four cardinal directions, but this is incorrect. For Qian and Kun are the great parents, giving birth to the six children, while Kan and Li are the parents of the myriad things, the root of all generation. They should be placed at the center of the *Taiji*. The remaining six hexagrams, with their three hundred and sixty lines, are distributed across the twelve months, corresponding above to the celestial circuit of the fire phases. The remaining two hundred and thirty-six lines are divided: two hundred lines are distributed among the four cardinal directions to correspond to the four images. For *Taiyi*, *Taichu*, *Taishi*, and *Taisu*, fifty lines are assigned to each direction, yielding eight-line hexagrams. Each hexagram has six lines, totaling forty-eight lines. Two additional lines are taken to distinguish the odd and even of yin and yang, thus completing the four images. Another thirty-six lines are placed within the central palace to correspond to the *Taiji*, yielding six hexagrams—this is what is meant by "gold entering the earthen cauldron, the elixir vessel perfected." The scripture totals four thousand and ninety-six characters, which is to say, the *Changes* transforms into four thousand and ninety-six hexagrams.

Through this explanation, it becomes clear that the *Wenchang* is none other than the *Book of Changes*. The *Changes* contains the four ways of the sage; the *Scripture* contains five: to exhaust the origins of heaven and earth, one upholds the *Wuji*; to preserve the integrity of one’s nature and life, one upholds *All-True*; to investigate the principles of yin and yang, one upholds *Wenchang*; to fathom the wonders of spirit and transformation, one upholds the *Great Cavern*; to savor the profundities of its words and flavors, one upholds the *Immortals’ Scripture*. If Qian and Kun are destroyed, the *Changes* cannot be seen; if yin and yang are sundered, the *Wenchang* cannot be seen. The *Scripture*, too, is the Way of simplicity and ease.

The security in which the noble person dwells is the order of the *Scripture*; what delights and inspires him is the diction of its verses. How wondrous! The rest may be extended by analogy, awaiting the scholars of future ages.

Kneeling in reverence, Qi Zai bows.

The Venerable Master Tai Xuan Dao Father Niu Zi initiated the inquiry and compiled the scripture; the Primordial Emperor of the Nine Heavens, Opener of Transformation, revised the *Mysterious Covenant* and composed the preface; the August Personage of Wenchang, the Mystic Sage of the Dao, presides over the *Chart of Wenchang* and oversees the scripture.

The *Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture*, with Tai Xuan Dao Father as its progenitor, is the master of celestial scripture compilation. The Primordial Emperor follows as the first to disseminate this scripture among humanity. The August Personage of Wenchang follows as the progenitor who governs the revolving life-*qi*, presides over culture and education, and assists in the august enterprise of emperors.

According to the *Inner and Outer Biographies of the August Lord*, the *Book of Transformations*, and the scripture’s preface, the August Lord was born in Wu Hui (present-day Pingjiang) in the *yisi* year of King Wu of Zhou’s reign. He received the *Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture* from the Three Perfected Ones. Through diligent recitation, he repeatedly attained spiritual responses, receiving golden icons and ritual registers. His practice of salvation proved efficacious, and he thus realized the sagely fruition of the Great Cavern’s wondrous practice.

Therefore, he composed the preface and *Mysterious Covenant* to enlighten the world. Though the scripture has never been absent from the Four Seas, it has, through repeated wars and fires, at times been lost and left untransmitted. Today, it circulates in Shu, where the people deeply believe in it, for the August Lord is revered as a great deity in Shu. From the Tang dynasty to the present, successive dynasties have honored him, and Wang Jian built a temple in his name. Thus, the August Lord specializes in transforming and saving people through this scripture, and many have attained the Dao by virtue of it.

In essence, this scripture has been transmitted among humanity since the time of King Wu of Zhou, over two thousand years ago. Thus, some characters may contain minor errors, which is hardly surprising. Fortunately, successive generations of perfected beings have verified and arranged it in order. Those who recite it need not doubt one version or be confused by another. With utmost sincerity and single-minded devotion, practicing even a single sentence can elevate one to the rank of highest immortality.

Some say it differs from the *Shangqing Great Cavern Scripture*. I, Qi, reply: The Three Mountains each possess their own scriptures and registers, and their methods are not uniform. Moreover, this is the *Jade Purity Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture*. Those of discernment all recognize the unity of the Dao; only the shallow-minded perceive differences.

**The Wenchang Assembly**
At the Wenchang Assembly, there were the Chan Masters Tongwu and Bolun, along with various Chan masters of Shu—all emanations of Avalokiteśvara Bodhisattva—who together inherited the ritual arena, naming it the *Mind-Pearl Assembly*. They took the August Lord as their leader. Each year, on the birthdays of the masters, Buddhist monks from all mountains would hold grand assemblies, widely propagating incense and fire rituals, offering celebrations and praises. Officials, merchants, scholars, and commoners all revered them in great numbers. Thus, the scriptures and rituals of the two teachings often blended and were used interchangeably.

There were also the Precious Radiance Heavenly Worthy’s *Perfect Penetration Ritual Arena*, where the Dharma seat was shaken, the Emperor’s Bell sounded, and Sanskrit mantras were chanted. Ninefold circumambulations were performed, along with Water and Land Dharma Assemblies and other rites. Some who fail to comprehend may claim the language is impure.

It is not impure. Generally, the character *Dao* adapts only to principle. Where principle resides, the Dao is fundamentally the same. Why distinguish between the two teachings? Only those who cannot fully investigate and exhaust it generate divergent views, leading to doubt and confusion. If one cannot firmly establish this mind, how can one seek the pure and unified principle of the Dao?

Moreover, the Great Emperor was renowned in his time as a great Confucian scholar. He devoted himself to the ancient classics and, during the Tai Kang era of the Jin, led his entire family to ascend as immortals at Fengdong. Successive dynasties honored him as the patriarch of culture. He first encountered the Most High, who bestowed the elixir, enabling him to realize the Dao’s fruition. Later, he met Śākyamuni, who conferred prediction, allowing him to realize the Great Vehicle. Thus, among the three teachings, he upheld the true Dharma.

In the present imperial Yuan dynasty, successive imperial edicts have bestowed praise and honor, renaming the *Lingying Temple* as the *Shrine of Right Culture and Transformation*. This shrine is a state ritual site, distinct from other temples dedicated to deities. He was further enfeoffed as *August Lord of Assisting the Primordial, Opening Transformation, Wenchang, Administering Fortune, and Vast Benevolence*. Among all deities, those granted the title of emperor are exceedingly rare.

I, Qi, am a native of Shu. The temples of Shu need no further proclamation. From my travels across seas and mountains, wherever I go, I seek out numinous traces, and they are found everywhere—Mount Hao being the most prominent. Thus, the flourishing of incense and fire rituals is such that his blessings in safeguarding families and the state, and in aiding both the living and the deceased, are immeasurable.

It is also known that the Wenchang Palace’s officials and subordinates are numerous and well-ordered. Here, I present the sacred taboo names and birthdays of the Wenchang lineage for those who uphold the Wenchang incense fire to know:

The Great Emperor’s taboo names across lifetimes: Shanxun, Zhongsi, Xiaozhong, Ruyi, Xun, Jun.

The above are not to be avoided.

The ancient name was "Evil Child," later omitting the middle and lower characters, leaving only the taboo name "Ya," with the courtesy name "Xianfu." Those who compose documents or memorials must strictly avoid these.

The third day of the second month marks his birth.

Left Minister, the Lady of the Dugu clan, born on the fifteenth day of the seventh month, is the reincarnation of Xu Jingshan. For her merit in slaying the mirage beast of Qiongzhou, she was enfeoffed across dynasties with an eight-character royal title. Now, she presides over the left ranks of Wenchang, commanding an entourage of one thousand two hundred, and is honored as the Broad-Blessing Auspicious Responsive Overflowing Trustworthy Kind King.

Right Minister, Li Fu, born on the fifteenth day of the eighth month, was likewise enfeoffed across dynasties with an eight-character royal title for his merit in breaking the forces of Fu Jian. Now, he presides over the right ranks of Wenchang, commanding an entourage of one thousand two hundred, and is honored as the Heroic Kind Loyal Fierce Winged Aid Right-Assisting King.

The Star Lords of the Wenchang Generals and Chancellors in the Purple Tenuity Enclosure; the Star Lords of the Wenchang Three Dukes’ Inner Seats in the Supreme Subtlety Enclosure; the Star Lords of the Wenchang Recluses and Scholars in the Lesser Subtlety Enclosure; the August King of Civil Rectitude of the Wenchang Upper Palace; the Great Accomplished Ultimate Sage Civil Proclaiming King; the Wenchang Lord of the Nine Qi of the Great Clarity; the Master Lord of the Purple Canopy Palace of the Great Clarity; the Luminous Lord of the Eastern Well; the Clear and Penetrating Decisive Officer; the Lord of the Qi of the Five Classics of the Nine Wonders Palace; the Six Immortals of the Wenchang Inner Attendants; the Four Generals of the White Crane, Penglai, Longevity Cassia, Chrysanthemum, and Cassia Fragrance Outer Halls; the Four Golden Walls of the Wenchang Northern Prefecture—Left and Right Chancellors; the Two Grand Historians, the Two Perfected, Su and Huang; the Censor, the Perfected Lü; the Chief Scribe, the Perfected Zhang; the True Man of the Heavenly Register Conferring Office; the True Man Yao, Who Responds to the Moment; the True Man Qin, Who Proceeds to the Moment; the Sovereign Lord of Primordial Unity; the Marshal of the Northern Prefecture, Duke of Military Classics; the Left Goldbird Envoy, General Hao; the Right Goldbird Envoy, General Di; the General in Charge of the Ruyi, Liu; the Seven Saintly Generals Who Govern the Military Registers; the Generals of the Wooden Horse, Beacon Fire, Swift Advantage, Patrol, Hunting, and Carved Tiger; the one hundred twenty great generals of the Phoenix Prefecture and Terrace; the various spirit officials of the thirty bureaus; the Generals Who Oversee the True Abodes, Thunder, and Frontiers; the Left and Right Announcing Judges and Investigating Patrol Envoys of the Wenchang Prefecture; the True Official of the Dream-Responding Land of Phoenix Mountain.

I, your subordinate of such-and-such rank and surname, reverently kindle heart-incense and humbly offer devotion:

Humbly we pray that your radiance shine upon us, acknowledging our recitations and invocations. Your subordinate’s sincerity is boundless, trembling with reverence. We bow twice to make this known.

They gather and abide in the golden chamber and jade hall of my dwelling, steadfast and undispersed. Swiftly, swiftly, in accordance with the statutes and ordinances!
