The Supreme One resides in the head, which is the Purple Gate. Within the human body are golden towers, jade chambers, purple gates, and jasper palaces. The Purple Gate is a separate chamber of the Muddy Pellet; the Supreme One Lord dwells there, overseeing the registers of immortals who attain the Dao.

The Three Converge at the Earth Gate Below
The Three *qi* unite in virtue; the Three Harmonies form a resonance. The *qi* of arising converges in the Lower Prime Palace. The Earth Gate below is the Gate of Death—*Qian* is the Heavenly Gate, *Xun* is the Earthly Gate, which is the Lower Field, as noted in the commentary on the Earth Gate’s protective guardians.

Uprooting Life to the Jade Emperor’s Palace
One uproots the life-pulse of human arising and elevates it to the Jade Emperor’s Palace, which is in the brain above. The Jade Capital Mountain contains the Jade Emperor’s Palace, presided over by the Upper Prime, where celestial immortals dwell. Only through cultivating the Dao and performing good deeds can one reach this place.

The Maiden Yu Mozi
The true immortal within the Dipper resides in the human heart, governing lifespan, poverty, and wealth. She is also a spirit of the Feminine One, belonging to the ranks of immortal maidens. As primordial true *qi*, she assists heaven and earth in nurturing the myriad beings, embodying the Great Dao to praise the ten thousand transformations.

Wei Zhao Guards the Seven *Qi* Windows
*Wei Zhao* is how Daoists refer to themselves, saying, “This minor servant, so-and-so.” The Seven *Qi* Windows are the seven orifices of the heart, likened to windows for their clarity—this is the meaning of “eight windows, exquisitely wrought,” all elegant metaphors and skillful analogies.

Restraining and Pledging the Blood and Fluids
The True Man of the Nine Primes, named *Juzhi* the Guardian, connects the left ear to the heart. The heart governs the generation of blood and fluids. By restraining and pledging them, one prevents them from being overcome by blood-*qi* or invaded by perverse *qi*, ensuring all returns to correctness and grandeur.

Filling the Five Viscera to Overflowing
If one can refine the utmost truth without being harmed by sensual desires, then the fluids, blood, *qi*, and liquids will fill the five viscera, six bowels, and three hundred sixty joints, accumulating strength. The complexion will be joyful and vigorous, and one’s lifespan will equal the pine and cypress.

The Ten Perfected Ascend to the Purple Chamber
(One version says *Yellow Chamber*, which is incorrect—the Purple Chamber is in the brain.) The Ten Perfected are the Ten Flower Perfected Ones, who ascend from below to the Purple Chamber, which is the Hall of Brightness in the brain, as seen in the *Great Mystery’s Nine Qi’s Upper Mystery Contract*.

The Emperor’s Son Transforms into a Golden Immortal
The *hun* of the August One ascends and is styled the Emperor’s Son. *Gold* refers to the White Tiger of *geng* and *xin*, refined into returning elixir. Ingesting it transforms one’s *qi* and substance into gold and jade, hence a later passage states, “Flesh and bones become gold and jade,” which refers precisely to this.

The White Jade Flying Talisman Summons
The White Jade Flying Talisman of the Jade Capital summons the adept, enabling them to shed the womb and change the cauldron, naturally achieving transcendence. The *Scripture on Generating Spirit* states, “Celebrate this infant’s molting”—this is the way of human birth after ten months in the womb, and the immortal’s shedding of the womb.

Guiding Ascent to the Dragon Terrace Heaven
One is guided upward to the Dragon Terrace Heaven. The Dragon Terrace is the Heaven of Dragon Transformation and Brahma Crossing, referring to the unfathomable transformations. Like the Yellow Emperor of Xuanyuan, who rode a dragon chariot into the sky in broad daylight with a thousand attendants, or the Jin-dynasty figures like Xu Jingshan, who all rode dragons and drove clouds to ascend and pay court to the Jade Clarity—all are recorded in the annals, clearly verifiable. These are transformations of one’s own yin and yang *qi*, becoming clouds and dragons to ride away, not coming from outside. As the *Mystery Contract* says, “Transformations occur naturally.” If one teaches the completion of the sacred embryo in ten months, one can shed the womb and spiritually transform. For those of the Life School, refining the golden elixir and perfecting the ten-month work is the completion. For those of the Nature School, striving to grasp the mechanism, suddenly achieving great enlightenment in a single word, is the completion. For the dull-rooted, who may not awaken to the Dao for twenty or thirty years, there is a distinction between sudden and gradual. Those who aspire to the Dao must not neglect either.

Some say the Dao is not worth studying, but they do not know that the Three Teachings ultimately return to one principle. One must reach the utmost goodness to arrive at the place of rest. The Dao says: “There is a thing, chaotically formed, born before heaven and earth. Silent and void, it stands alone and does not change.” Buddhism says: “The Perfect Awakening and True Suchness are born together with life. If one seeks me through form or pursues me through sound, one walks the wrong path.”

The Confucian says: "Heaven begets the teeming masses; all things have their principles. Look not at what is contrary to propriety; listen not to what is contrary to propriety." These are the embodiments of the sages of the Three Teachings. The Dao says: "In true constancy, one responds to things—constantly responding, constantly quiescent." The Buddhist says: "Perfectly round, radiantly luminous, vividly alive, utterly unobstructed." The Confucian says: "Filled to repletion and thus resplendent is called greatness; great and transformed is called sageliness; sagely yet unfathomable is called spirit." These are the functions of the sages of the Three Teachings.

Buddhism speaks of "no self, no others"; Confucianism speaks of "no obstinacy, no self"—these are all the most fitting and unifying words. Why cling and fail to penetrate? Why remain distant and fail to attain? Those who seek the supreme vehicle must pay heed to this and not rigidly adhere to doctrines that deceive and harm the nature of life.

The above jade inscription in celestial script comprises ninety characters, governing above the Xuanming Gonghua Heaven and ruling below the Third Rampart’s Emperor De Jun.

The *Xuanqi* states: "Recite it ten times, and within the form, the Primordial Destiny of the Original Destiny coalesces into the Perfected One of the Imperial Unity. Nine harmonies and ten unions—embodied, one naturally attains thorough penetration of the true. Able to summon and command the ten directions, to govern the primordial and return the numinous, the myriad qi become perfected, virtue and dark wisdom merge. Profound beyond bounds, transformations arise spontaneously."

At this stage of cultivation, it is called the Mysterious Pass, also known as the Mysterious Assembly. The Six Perfections and Ten Returns—when merit is complete and the Dao is perfected—one ascends to the rank of Immortal Duke. First, the Ten Faiths; next, the Ten Goodnesses; then, the Ten Blossomings; then, the Ten Virtues; gradually advancing to the Ten Immortals; and finally, transforming into the Ten Perfected. Having ascended the six ranks, with wondrous practice fully accomplished, body, spirit, and qi refined, one is titled a Perfected Person.

The Ten Faiths, Ten Goodnesses, Ten Blossomings, Ten Virtues, Ten Immortals, and Ten Perfected are called the Six Ranks Entering the Gate of Myriad Wonders.

*Jade Clarity’s Wondrous Ultimate and Comprehensive Perfected Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture*, Scroll Four
● "Two Qi" should likely read "Three Qi."

*Commentary on Jade Clarity’s Wondrous Ultimate and Comprehensive Perfected Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture*, Scroll Five
Annotated by Zhongyangzi Wei Qi of Mount Penglai in Eastern Shu

The Dao speaks: At that time, this scroll’s wondrous practices are cultivated through the six roots together with nature-and-life, essence-and-blood, fluids-and-saliva, hands-and-feet. If the six roots are pure, one does not fall into the Six Caverns of Fengdu. The Six Caverns are: Zhou’s Cut-Off Yin Heaven, Tai’s Slaying Deceitful Matters Ancestral Heaven, Mingchen’s Enduring Offense Martial City Heaven, Tianzhao’s Sinful Qi Heaven, Zongling’s Seven Transgressions Heaven, and Gansi’s Linked Curved Layers Heaven. If nature-and-life are pure, one does not fall into the Five Marchmounts Hell; if essence-and-blood are pure, one does not fall into the Water Palace Hell; if hands-and-feet are pure, one does not fall into the Nine Darks’ Eighteen Prisons; if fluids-and-saliva are pure, one can generate the five spirits—Wu Ying, Bai Yuan, Tai Yi, Si Ming, and Tao Kang—together attaining the Ten Penetrations’ wondrous practices.

The *Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture* has long been practiced in Shu, yet the Shu edition still contains errors. Since no one has ever verified the facts and block-printed it, "a character passes through three transcriptions, and a bird becomes a horse." For instance, at the scripture’s opening, the four characters "The Dao speaks: At that time" are the Jade Emperor Dao Lord’s preface. When the Heavenly King expounded the scripture, he began with such causes and conditions—just as Buddhist sutras begin with "Thus have I heard" and the *Analects* with "The Master said." These cannot be omitted; they must be restored. Though I, Qi, may incur the charge of presumption, I do so to preserve the scripture’s intent.

Every scripture comprises three divisions: the introductory section, the main doctrinal section, and the dissemination section. The old edition lacks these four characters, thus omitting the introductory section. The introductory section should begin with "The Dao speaks," the main doctrinal section should comprise the thirty-six chapters, and the concluding passage should serve as the dissemination section. Why has this scripture circulated in Shu? It is because the Primordial Emperor Lord was first born in Haohui—present-day Gusu—where he received this scripture and attained fruition as the deity of Shu. He then propagated this scripture to enlighten humans and gods. The Primordial Emperor was reborn in the dingwei year, when the Celestial Emperor appointed him as the Yang Official of the Southern Dipper, the office governing birth. Thus, those seeking heirs often prayed to him, and it became known that Wenchang was Nanchang, the deity overseeing the nurturing and cultivation of virtue.

According to historical records, at the end of the Jingde era, Academician Le, serving as the Resident Censor of the Western Capital, suddenly dreamed of a man in full court attire who declared, "The Emperor commands your presence." Le followed him and soon beheld magnificent palaces. When he asked the messenger whose they were, the reply was, "This is the Emperor’s abode." Upon ascending, the Emperor said, "You govern those seeking heirs. I have chosen one for you." Shortly after, a man was selected, and the Emperor said, "Those in the Central Plains seek heirs. Go and do not refuse." The man kowtowed three times, begging to be excused, but the Emperor said, "Go!" A courtier standing nearby said, "This is the Barefoot Immortal Li Shouwei of Nanchang." The following year, Emperor Renzong was born. Thus, it is clear that Wenchang governs the office of heirship and prosperity.

Each sentence of this scripture governs a single matter. If one can practice even one sentence, one may ascend as a superior immortal—how much more so for those who recite the entire volume? How could there be no karmic response? Yet in this world, there are Daoist priests who live and die without ever hearing the name of the *Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture*. Some, upon seeing that the scripture does not explicitly discuss the retribution of good and evil, set it aside on a high shelf. Others, though fond of recitation, do not understand its principles. Yet the scripture does indeed speak of good and evil retribution. For instance, it speaks of "delivering one from the five bitter poisons" and "transcending form to reach the Beginning Azure." If one has no sins, how could one fall into the five sufferings? If one has no merit, how could one reach the Beginning Azure? Such examples are numerous.

Other scriptures say, "Recite and uphold this scripture," but what does "this scripture" truly signify? It refers to this very heart. If one cannot guard this heart with care—indulging in deceit, recklessness, perversion, and excess, violating reason and propriety—then in life, one will suffer from grave illness and imprisonment, and in death, one will be cast into ditches, devoured by flies and gnats. How could the gods of heaven and earth spare such a one, consigning them to the Avīci Hell to endure endless torment? As the Buddhist texts say, "Even if the karma one creates over a hundred kalpas does not perish, when the conditions converge, one will still receive the retribution oneself." The tradition states, "Misfortune and fortune have no doors; it is man who invites them." Is this not the retribution of good and evil?

Here, I have appended verified examples to inspire reverence and faith in the reader, that they may cultivate each practice step by step and ascend the gates of the ten immortals. Even those of shallow capacity may attain clarity regarding past circumstances and achieve the Way of *shijie* (liberation through apparent death). There are five types of *shijie*: water liberation (drowning), fire liberation (self-immolation), metal liberation (being cut by blades), wood liberation (transforming while leaning against a tree), and earth liberation (entering mountains or stones). The Mysterious Woman has methods for cultivating the five liberations to escape great calamities, evade yin pursuers, and flee to other realms, where one may seize a womb or take over a body.

The Primordial Heavenly King’s brows emit azure radiance. How vast is the Way of the Sage! Overflowing, it nurtures the myriad things, towering to the heavens. Observing the founding masters of the Three Teachings, who established their doctrines for the world, we see they never adhered to partiality. Yet people forcibly distinguish them, saying Buddhism governs nature, Daoism governs life, and Confucianism governs principle. They do not realize that these three are one. When the Buddha expounded the Dharma, his brows emitted white radiance; when the Primordial One expounded the Dao, his brows emitted azure radiance. Did these two sages manifest different signs of excellence? The white radiance of the Western direction is the qi of metal, which, though it represents nature, encompasses life within it. The azure radiance of the Eastern direction is the yang qi, which, though it represents life, encompasses nature within it. The Way of nature and life mutually constitute the human being. As the *Doctrine of the Mean* states, "What Heaven imparts is called nature; following nature is called the Way."

What Heaven bestows upon me is life; what I receive and embody is nature. When we speak of nature, life is within it; when we speak of life, nature is within it. Thus, the seventh chapter of the middle volume states, "The root of nature and life is firm." What, then, are nature and life? In terms of nature, they are benevolence, righteousness, propriety, and wisdom—the four beginnings, the five constants, and the principles of the myriad things and affairs, all encompassed within. In terms of life, they are *yuan*, *heng*, *li*, and *zhen*—the four seasons, the five phases, and the transformations of the myriad beings, all issuing forth from them. This is the luminous principle of Heaven, yet people obscure it with selfish desires and cannot restore the original purity of their source. Thus, the sages, in accordance with what humans are endowed with, cultivated and clarified moral standards, established teachings for the world, and enabled people to fulfill the Way of utmost sincerity. Then, the original countenance reappears before them. As it is said, "Only the utmost sincerity under Heaven can fully realize one’s nature, thereby assisting Heaven and Earth, and aiding in transformation and nourishment, as if shown on the palm of the hand."

Some may ask, "You annotate Daoist scriptures yet cite Buddhist sutras and Confucian texts. Is this not excessive?" I reply: The sages of the Three Teachings originally aimed to correct human evil and guide all toward the good Way. Thus, it is said, "There are not two Ways under Heaven; the sages do not have two hearts." It is like entering a city—one must pass through its gates. Though the palaces may differ, the destination is the same. If people fully realize their aspirations, where can they not go? Therefore, I have harmonized the classics and pronouncements to elucidate them. What fault is there in this?

The crown revolves with purple qi; the myriad-flowered treasure canopy floats and covers the form. Purple qi arises from the union of yin and yang qi, signifying the origin of life. Within this purple qi, the myriad-flowered treasure canopy takes shape, shading the Dharma body. Above each person’s head, there is also a flower canopy, though they do not see it. The scripture says, "Purple clouds cover the Yellow and the Old," referring to the Three Treasure Lords—this is precisely what it means.

When one cultivates the Dao, even spirits and gods cannot perceive their boundaries—only a radiant red light surges forth, dazzling the eyes. Jade-like brilliance and golden auroras coil and shimmer in resplendent splendor. Like the luminous glow of jade and the iridescent hues of gold, they twist and gleam, flashing before the eyes of heaven and humanity. Such is the light of the Seventeen Emperors, all emanating from within oneself.

The Jade Emperor Dao Lord and the Great Mystery Dao Father bow their heads in reverent anticipation, wishing to hear the profound chapters. Beneath the title of the *Cavern Scripture*, it is recorded that the Great Mystery Dao Father, Master Niu Zi, compiled this text—only here do we encounter the Jade Emperor Dao Lord and the Great Mystery Dao Father. The Jade Emperor is the Numinous Treasure of the Great Mystery; some mistakenly identify him as the Most High, though I, too, once doubted this. Now, in clarifying this, I recall a dream in which, before the hall of an old family estate, a herd of cattle gathered, and one bull charged at me. I warded it off with my staff, striking its left eye, while its hoof struck my face. I bit down on one of its toes and awoke with a start.

One day, I chanced upon the *Veritable Records*, which state: "The Most High transformed eighty-two times into the Dark Warrior, known as the Great Mystery." The *Descent of the Immortals* also says: "The ox is the essence of the Dark Warrior." Only then did I recall the *Book of Rites*, which calls the ox 'the Great Martial of the First Origin.' Thus, I realized that the Great Mystery and Master Niu Zi are none other than the Dark Emperor. The dream was no illusion.

The Dark Emperor was born in the first kalpa of the Heavenly Opening of the Yellow Emperor’s reign, in the first year of the Purple Cloud era, the *jiawu* year, on the third day of the third month. The *True Warrior Scripture* mistakenly records this as *jiachen*. At fifteen, he began studying the Dao and cultivating practice. After forty-two years, he ascended to the Purple Cloud at the age of fifty-seven, on the ninth day of the ninth month of the *gengyin* year. He was then appointed Marshal of the Great Mystery and forever entrusted with guarding the North. During the second kalpa of the Heavenly Dragon era, when King Zhou of Yin ruled with tyranny, demonic spirits ran rampant, harming living beings and sending toxic *qi* surging upward. The Primordial Beginning commanded him to capture them, and for his merit, he was restored to the Kan position and appointed Great General Zhenwu of the Heavenly Dark Warrior. Later, in the third year of the True Transformation era of Heaven—corresponding to the second year of the Jiayou reign—the Three Pure Ones entrusted the Jade Emperor with evaluating his merits. The Three Officials and Four Saints ranked him second only to the Heavenly Emperor. He was then appointed to the Hanlin Academy to compile the jade tablets, and the Great Mystery was elevated to the Dark Heavenly Emperor. Thus, I know this scripture was reissued upon his investiture. Originally comprising one hundred and twenty fascicles, the Great Mystery compiled these thirty-six chapters, which are also the origin of the thirty-six revered scriptures, making them easier to practice—much like the *Supreme Scripture of the Great Cavern*, which differs not from the wondrous first rank.

The term "reverent anticipation" signifies looking upward with devotion, while "wishing to hear" denotes listening with humility, composed and solemn, focused without distraction. One fears only that their reverence may falter or their demeanor may lack propriety—this is what is meant by "solemnity and uprightness suffice to govern." The heart of the Dao Father extends from self to others, embodying the Master’s way of loyalty and reciprocity. How could one not rejoice and sing with delight?

From this point onward, the six roots and six cavern palaces are taken in order to avoid disrupting the main principle.

The Primordial Heavenly King, contented, sings:
*"The Eleventh Jade Chapter of the Great Cavern of Wenchang—*
*The Cavern Vision of the Eye Root, where the Dao Eye first opens.*
*Yiwei, Bingchen, Mingyi, Jiaren."*

The preface recounts how the Jade Emperor Dao Lord narrated the origins and causes of the scripture—this is called the *Preface Section*. The main scripture consists of the Primordial Heavenly King’s proclamation of the luminous sounds—this is the *Orthodox Section*. The conclusion, also by the Dao Lord, summarizes the scripture’s essence—this is the *Circulation Section*.

*"The August One transcends the shadowless—"*

The eye’s relation to form is of great consequence. When the eye sees, the heart desires; when the heart stirs, the spirit wearies. Thus, the spirits of the five viscera all leak through the eye, making it the foremost root. The eye’s aperture connects to the heart, which is the abode of spirit. Once the eye sees, the heart inevitably stirs.

*"August"* means great, and *"above"* means lofty. It speaks of the Dao’s greatness and transcendence, rising beyond the realm of formlessness. Without form or light, it is called "shadowless." In this scripture, the character *"shadow"* appears twenty-eight times across three fascicles:
*"Eight shadows govern constant peace,
Eight shadows harmonize the Cavern Yang,
Eight shadows illuminate the Mud Pill,
The Great Clarity observes the Eight Shadows"*—all convey the same meaning.
*"Within the radiant shadow’s clarity,
The Great One reigns as Shadow King,
Bearing this shadowed person,
Qi emerges from the flower’s shadow,
Ever abiding within the shadow’s transformation"*—another shared meaning.
*"The Supreme Ultimate’s Primordial Shadow King,
The Great Simplicity brushes the ethereal shadow,
The red shadow veils the boundless,
The cavern shadow lodges spiritual penetration,
The Supreme Ultimate’s Mysterious Shadow Youth,
The feathered shadow of the Great Void’s court,
The golden watchtower’s upper shadow qi,
The unified jade shadow qi,
The yellow shadow qi of the morning’s midst"*—all belong to the same category.
*"The August One transcends the shadowless,
The Great Void’s emptiness is shadowless"*—another category.
*"Riding the shadow’s morning radiance,
Driving the shadow to ascend the distant clouds"*—another category.
*"The Emperor’s One ascends the bright shadow,
Brightness gives rise to the Emperor’s shadow"*—another category.
*"The Two Origins ascend the shadow’s thoroughfare"*—another category.
*"The Eight Perfected unite as Shadow Lords,
A thousand shadows arise in solemnity"*—another category.
*"The Three Heavens illuminate the Nine Shadows"*—a distinct meaning, though the character is the same.

Some interpret *"shadow"* as chariots, robes, or regalia; others as banners, pendants, or standards; still others as the colors of light and *qi*; or as the names of gods and perfected beings. In various scriptures and traditions, there are *"shadow-morning radiant aurora crowns,"* *"shadow robes,"* *"shadow standards,"* and *"shadow chariots."* Yet no one knows what these objects truly are. In my humble estimation, they resemble the seven treasures of officials today—crowns, hats, sashes, belts, saddles, and bridles. The *Jade Emperor Scripture* speaks of *"nine auroras streaming shadows"* and *"flying cloud jade chariots,"* which are similar. Here, *"shadowless"* refers to formlessness. If one can withdraw their gaze and turn inward, they will naturally reach the realm of emptiness and non-being.

*"The wheel of the Nine Luminaries halts."*

Some say *"the Nine Luminaries arise,"* but this is surely an error. It means the sun and moon pause their movement, and the Jade Armillary Sphere ceases its rotation. The *qi* of humanity originates in the primordial chaos of the Great Vastness, yet it cannot be preserved and nurtured due to the leakage through the eye root. Now, having realized this and begun cultivation, one transcends the realm of formlessness. Thus, the Jade Armillary Sphere and the Jade Crossbar halt their turning, awaiting the proof of one’s attainment.

In heaven, it revolves the celestial axle, transforming the Nine *Qi* to nurture the myriad things of heaven and earth. Only the Seven Primes of the Northern Dipper circulate day and night—this is what is meant by *"the Jade Armillary and Jade Crossbar aligning the Seven Governors."* Within the heart, the Seven Primes likewise operate, sharing the same ceaseless mechanism as the Nine Primes of heaven. Thus, as humans, we must strive unceasingly, fortifying our will to align with the celestial workings.

*"Luminaries"* refers to the radiance of the eye’s spirit. When the gaze is fixed, the Nine Orifices all come to rest. As the *Book of Songs* says: *"The child cherishes bright virtue, neither loud in voice nor harsh in countenance"*—this expresses the same principle.

*"Revolving wind blends with the Emperor’s Heart."*
The *"Emperor’s Heart"* is the Dao-Heart. *"The human heart is perilous; the Dao-Heart is subtle. Only through refinement and unity can one hold fast to the center."* The heart, as a thing, is serene, pure, empty, and luminous—like a mirror’s void or a scale’s balance. It governs the entire body, encompassing all principles and responding to all affairs. Even spirits cannot fathom its depths. Every movement and every breath is bound to it. Thus, the *Great Learning* teaches that the Way lies in rectifying the heart.

*Laozi* said: *"The five colors blind the eye."* When people are obscured by material desires, they cannot perceive the transformations of heaven and earth. Therefore, the sages established teachings to *"withdraw the gaze and return the hearing,"* making the rejection of cleverness and the abandonment of sagely wisdom urgent tasks. If one can preserve the heart and nurture the nature, then the myriad things of heaven and earth will vividly appear before them.

*Mencius* said: *"There is no better way to nurture the heart than to reduce desires."* If one can diminish desires, they will attain the *"heart-fasting"* of Yanzi’s *"sitting in forgetfulness."* Thus, the sages *"washed the heart and retired into secrecy"* to achieve the perfection of the Dao.

This chapter focuses on cultivation through the eye root. The eye has several interpretations. Buddhist scriptures speak of the *"flesh eye, heavenly eye, wisdom eye, dharma eye, and Buddha eye."* The *"flesh eye"* belongs to ordinary beings—what the world calls the *"vulgar eye."* The *"Buddha eye"* is the *"Dao eye."* By the standards of common people, the vulgar eye observes heaven and earth. The perfected person observes heaven and earth with the Dao eye. Where is the Dao eye? It must be said: in the One Heart. Within, there are the five viscera and six bowels, yet they are separated by the body’s barrier. Without, there are the Five Movements and Six *Qi*, yet they are separated by heaven and earth. If observed with the vulgar eye, none can be seen. But if observed with the Dao eye, one sees through both inner and outer, beyond the Nine Heavens, and even the tiniest speck of dust is illuminated.

*"Revolving wind blends in union"*—the *qi* of heaven and earth intermingle to form the *"Emperor’s One True Dao Samadhi."* Humans are the same: using saliva as the dragon and emptiness as the tiger, the Way of circulation lies in these two things. The *Book of Changes* says: *"Clouds follow the dragon; wind follows the tiger. When the sage arises, the myriad things behold him."* The principles are closely aligned.

Later, the ninth chapter says: *"The Emperor’s Heart is the Great Mystery’s thoroughfare."* Formerly, Yu Linggui of Hejian practiced the *"Great Cavern’s Revolving Wind Blending Dao"* for twenty years. While seated, he could perceive all affairs under heaven, yet he concealed his abilities and appeared no different from others. His countenance remained as that of a man in his thirties, his clothes worn as ever. When asked about events near or far, he answered as if witnessing them firsthand. People revered him, though he would say, *"It is mere happenstance, not something I know."* He never ceased reciting the *Great Cavern Sutra*, sometimes abstaining from grain to drink wine. Later, he suddenly ascended as an immortal, having attained the *"Revolving Wind Emperor’s Heart."* When one turns the light of both eyes inward to reflect, true *qi* follows and gathers in the original palace—this is called *"revolving wind blending in union."*

*"The Eight Sceneries revolve, ever tranquil."*
Some say *"Eight Qi,"* but this is incorrect. The heart is heaven; the kidneys are earth. The distance between heart and kidneys is eight inches and four parts; the distance between heaven and earth is eighty-four thousand miles. The *"spirit wind bellows"* ensures the stability of heaven and earth. For humans, the movement of true *qi* ensures the body’s enduring peace.

The human body’s Three Divisions and Eight Sceneries—from the coccyx to the *Baihui*—are divided into three sections per barrier, totaling twenty-four nodes corresponding to the Twenty-Four *Qi*.

**Upper Division’s Eight Sceneries:**
- Brain Spirit: *Awakened Origin Child*, styled *Dao Capital*
- Hair Spirit: *Mysterious Pattern Florescence*, styled *Dao Balance*
- Skin Spirit: *Penetrating Multitude Second*, styled *Dao Link*
- Eye Spirit: *Void Supervisor Life*, styled *Dao Weight*
- Cervical Marrow Spirit: *Spiritual Model Cover*, styled *Dao Cycle*
- Spinal Spirit: *Beneficial Passage Aide*, styled *Dao Pillar*
- Nose Spirit: *Surging Dragon Jade*, styled *Dao Subtle*
- Tongue Spirit: *Primordial Beam Peak*, styled *Dao Branch*

**Middle Division’s Eight Sceneries:**
- Throat Spirit: *Hundred Streams Release*, styled *Dao Passage*
- Lung Spirit: *Plain Spirit Life*, styled *Dao Level*
- Heart Spirit: *Radiant Yang Prosperity*, styled *Dao Bright*
- Liver Spirit: *Opening Lord Youth*, styled *Dao Azure*
- Gallbladder Spirit: *Dragon Virtue Restrainer*, styled *Dao Release*
- Left Kidney Spirit: *Spring Prime True*, styled *Dao Minister*
- Right Kidney Spirit: *Image Earth None*, styled *Dao Life*
- Spleen Spirit: *Treasure Origin Complete*, styled *Dao Soaring*

**Lower Division’s Eight Sceneries:**
- Stomach Spirit: *Alike Vermilion Nurture*, styled *Dao Morning*
- Intestinal Cavity Spirit: *Omen Soaring Health*, styled *Dao Return*
- Large and Small Intestine Spirit: *Abundant Delivery Stay*, styled *Dao Kitchen*
- Chest Cavity Spirit: *Receiving Prosperity Vigorous*, styled *Dao Spirit*
- Diaphragm Spirit: *Vast Glittering Residence*, styled *Dao Second*
- Flank Spirit: *Opening False Horse*, styled *Dao Achievement*
- Left Yin-Right Yang Spirit: *Supporting Stay Rise*, styled *Dao Jade Tablet*
- Right Yin-Left Yang Spirit: *Embracing Bright Manifest*, styled *Dao Life*

Within humans, the *"Purple River Carriage"* constantly transports the *qi* of true essence upward to the *Niwan*. *"Constant"* means enduring; *"tranquil"* means peaceful—ensuring the body’s perpetual well-being.

Some say the *"Eight Sceneries"* are the *"Eight Gates,"* as employed in *Dun Jia*. Formerly, Shi Cun served Huang Luzi and obtained the *Inner Writings of the Three Sovereigns*, which included the *Eight Gates Dun Jia*. He could perform the arts of *Dun* transformation and illusion, commanding tigers and leopards. In the first year of the Yongkang era of Jin, on the seventh day of the fourth month, he rode a leopard to ascend to heaven, becoming the *"Perfected of Balanced Harmony and Manifest Simplicity."* This is the clear verification of the Eight Sceneries.

Within the vast expanse, the radiant clouds intermingle with the divine heavens. The celestial deities number eighteen thousand, the human deities eighteen thousand—together thirty-six thousand—all in harmonious accord with the workings of yin and yang. As the *Book of Songs* says: *"The divine arrives in thought."* According to the teachings of the Elder of Green City: the hair becomes the Lord of Green City; the head, the Lords of the Three Terraces; the brows, the Lords of the Purple Ultimate; the eyes, the Lords of Mystic Clarity; the left ear, the Lord of Sagacity; the right ear, the Lord of Resoluteness; the nose, the Lord of Heaven’s Wondrous Portal; the mouth, the Lord of the Gate of Teeth; the lips, the Lords of the Jade Portal; the teeth, the Twenty-Eight Primordial Lords of the Extremities; the throat, the Lord Commander; the larynx, the Nine Ministers; the liver, the Lord of the Crimson Palace; the lungs, the Lord of the Florid Canopy; the gallbladder, the Lord of Longevity; the heart, the Lord of the Cinnabar Field; the vessels, the Lord of the Purple Silk; the stomach, the Lord of the Grand Granary; the spleen, the Lord of the Yellow Court; the left kidney, the Lord of the Mysterious Wondrous; the right kidney, the Lord of the Mysterious Origin; the large intestine, the Lord Nourishing Mother; the small intestine, the Lord of Guiding and Conducting; the abdomen, the Lord of the Grand Dao; the Triple Burner, the Lord of the Mysterious Elder; the left foot, the Lord of Thunder and Lightning; the right foot, the Lord of Cloud and Qi. These thirty-six Lords of Vital Qi all correspond within the body, interlinked in form and function, mutually nurturing and operating as one.

The *Book of Changes* states: *"That which is unfathomable in yin and yang is called the divine."* Those who understand the Dao of transformation know the workings of the divine. It also says: *"The divine has no fixed form."* The *Classic of the Yin Talisman* declares: *"Humans know the divine as divine, yet do not know that the non-divine is the very source of divinity."* For the divine, as a thing, is governed solely by intention. Thus, the vast and boundless clouds and mists pay homage to the divine heavens—also named the *"Valley Spirit that never dies."* The *Niwan* is the gathering place of the hundred spirits; the deities within the human body assemble here. Their gathering is neither swift nor slow, neither moving nor arriving—yet they are present. The divine operates concealed within seeing and hearing. If not for the leaks of the eyes and ears, it could be concentrated and gathered. Hence, the *Scripture of Salvation* states: *"Below, it stabilizes the human body’s Niwan and Crimson Palace; within, it governs the five qi, blending and uniting the hundred spirits."* The human body differs not from heaven and earth, sharing the same divine qi.

The Five Thearchs disperse solar essence. Now, the heavens above shine with boundless luminosity, to which the sun, moon, and stars are tethered. Above the divine heavens lie the sun and moon, just as the human head bears eyes. The Five Thearchs—referenced in the annotation on the *"Five Thearchs’ Ever-Preserving City"* in the preceding scroll—are identical here. Chapter Three of this scroll states: *"Within the sun, the five radiance unfold,"* echoing this passage. The Five Thearchs are the qi of the Five Phases: the Green Thearch guards the hun-soul, the White Thearch attends the po-soul, the Red Thearch nurtures qi, the Black Thearch circulates blood, and the Yellow Thearch governs the center. Heaven has the five stars, earth the five peaks, and humans the five viscera—above and below in mutual resonance. Yet when humans indulge in the passions of emotion—joy, anger, sorrow, and delight—stirring within and manifesting without, the local spirits, with their ten eyes and ten hands, observe and point. Thus, calamity and fortune, misfortune and blessing, all respond accordingly. As the saying goes: *"Misfortune and fortune have no gate; they are summoned by man alone."* Solar essence and lunar radiance, if ingested by humans, bestow luminous complexion and robust health. Thus, the preceding scroll states:

*"Auspicious qi nurtures the five clouds,
The five qi congeal in the ten directions,
The five numina transmit talismanic registers,
Filling and replenishing the five viscera,
The Five Elders assist the Jade Root."*

This scroll declares:

*"Blood congeals, the five blossoms level,
Within the sun, the five radiance unfold,
The five viscera plant the Jade Root,
Bowing and rising, they summon the five numina,
The five spirits return to infancy,
Refining and nurturing the five budding pearls,
Drawing forth the five poisons of suffering,
The omen bears the five talismanic registers,
The po-soul lies hidden in the five paths,
The five talismans seal the earth’s knots,
The five talismans weave the Purple Chamber,
The five registers mark the Round Court,
The Five Elders linger in attendance."*

The following scroll says:

*"The five celestial bodies are called the Trigger,
Swallowing saliva generates the five buds,
Gathering the spirit protects the five registers,
Blending within the chambers of the five suns,
The five paths bloom with golden splendor,
The Five Elders transform into youthful innocence,
The Grand Spread unfurls the five talismans,
The five viscera reflect pure serenity,
The five demons strike the six yin,
The five qi govern the central jaw,
The five paths illuminate the Three Heavens,
The Five Elders soar with the Jade Plow,
The Five Peaks respond to the command and arrive,
The Five Peaks open the numinous gate,
The Five Peaks come to the court,
The five clouds thicken in the void,
The Five Elders brandish crimson blossoms,
Grasping the five talismanic registers in the left hand."*

All such instances pertain to the qi of the Five Phases, flowing through the Three Powers as the root of transformation, generation, and nurturance. To *"disperse solar essence"* is to spread the qi of yang harmony, assisting in the creation and nurturing of the myriad things. Humans should constantly regulate the five viscera with the qi of solar essence, preserving and harmonizing the Grand Harmony. This is what is meant by *"The Dao of Qian transforms and each fulfills its nature and destiny."* When the five viscera are in harmony, the Five Constants are complete, and one is not indicted by the five spirits, pressed by the Five Peaks, illuminated by the five stars, or reported by the Five Thearchs. Then the five registers are revised—how could one be bound by the five movements, five paths, or five sufferings? What the noble person cannot attain lies only in what others do not see.

The fluids flow freely within the mysterious membranes.

The character "逸" appears in seven contexts: *Abode of Ease*, *Longevity Ease*, *Purple Ease*, *Void Ease*, *Verdant Ease*, and *Supreme Clarity Ease*.

*Liao* means tranquility, peace, and joy. Heaven and Earth revolve through the water phase in endless cycles, thus never decaying. Humans irrigate the five viscera with fluids, and so do not die; if the fluids dry up, the spirit has nothing to nourish it, and the form must perish. The *Mysterious Membrane* is the hidden water of the northern direction, veiled within a single layer; in the human body, the kidney-water likewise resides within the adipose membranes. When fluids, blood, and qi are constantly full, irrigating and moistening, the body grows strong and the countenance radiant.

The blood congeals into the *Five Florets in Equilibrium*.

Purple, green, and crimson florets are not true colors but external things. Though the eye beholds resplendent wealth and heavenly bliss, these are not to be coveted in the heart. The *Five Florets* are *Azure Floret*, *Cinnabar Floret*, *Pristine Floret*, *Mysterious Floret*, and *Yellow Floret*—speaking of the inner florets that naturally arise. When one nourishes the five viscera with blood and qi, the *Mysterious Pearl* is spontaneously born. As the *Yellow Court Scripture* says: *"Irrigate the Five Florets to plant the numinous root."* Once the Five Florets congeal, they transform into the *Four Numinous Beings*, fully guarding the center.

The *Yu Zhang* Daoist Xiao Weiyi, styled Mianzhi, wandered to Xiangfu Abbey on Mount Lu in Jiangzhou. Delighting in its secluded beauty, he built a retreat there, reciting the *Great Cavern Scripture* daily. One day, with eyes closed, he beheld the Four Numinous Beings standing guard and was suddenly awakened. From then on, his spirit and countenance were utterly transformed, his words extraordinary. He spontaneously composed poetry, and though over ninety, his white hair turned black, and he walked as swiftly as if flying. In the midst of pure qi, he bid farewell to the assembly and sat in transformation. His disciple Xu Qinlin later also departed while seated.

The *Precious Body* reflects the *Luminous Pearl*.

The *Great Cavern Immortal Scripture* is titled *Canghu Jiebao*, though its upper and middle scrolls are not seen—only the lower scroll reveals its meaning. *Bao* (precious) and *zhu* (pearl) are one, referring to the single grain of golden elixir within the body. It is called the *Māṇi Precious Pearl*, the *Grain-of-Millet Pearl*, the *Mysterious Pearl*, the *Dust-Returning Elixir of the Bright Window*, the *Divine Elixir*, the *Jade Flask Elixir*, the *Purple Gold Elixir*, the *Golden Fluid Returning Elixir*, the *Knife-Tip Great Medicine*, the *Sacred Embryo Infant*—a thousand names and ten thousand titles, all referring to the same thing, far beyond the mere external ingredients of metals, minerals, herbs, or trees.

It is formed from one’s own *spirit-water*, *Flower Pool*, *golden essence*, *jade fluid*, *cinnabar*, *quicksilver*, *true lead*, *true mercury*, *dragon liver*, *phoenix marrow*, *crimson woman*, and *infant*, refined and tempered through cultivation. Thus, the upper scroll says: *"The Radiant Great Treasure shines"*; the upper palace says: *"Within the cloud-pearl"*; the middle scroll says: *"Licking and refining the Five Sprout Pearl"* and *"Entrusting and carrying the Moving Pearl"*; the lower scroll says: *"Leading the Canghu Pearl"*, *"Friend of the Precious Red Qi King"*, *"The Canghu’s radiant brilliance"*, *"A single revolution of the pearl in the sun"*, and *"The resplendent Round Pearl gleams"*—all expressing this same meaning.

The Confucian classics speak of the time before Heaven and Earth divided, when form was like a hen’s egg. The word *precious* is not idly attained; its value lies in its infinite responsiveness, fulfilling every desire without fail. As for worldly *wish-fulfilling jewels*, whatever one seeks is granted as the heart desires. The King of Wei possessed a pearl that illuminated twelve carriages before and behind; the *Pearl of Marquis Sui* and the *Uncut Jade of Bian He* were treasured by the world—how much more so the truly supreme and precious treasures of Heaven above, the human realm, the heavenly paradises, the Buddha-lands, the dragon palaces, and the oceanic treasuries?

Now, the *Primordial Beginning* has two precious pearls. The *Scripture of Salvation* says: *"The Primordial Beginning, in the Great Floating Li Land of the Void, suspended a precious pearl, large as a grain of millet. The Primordial Beginning ascended first, followed by the perfected immortals, all entering the pearl’s mouth, never to be seen again."* From this, though the pearl is small, it contains multitudes—how so? The Buddhist teachings speak of *Mount Sumeru fitting into a mustard seed*, of *buddha-lands within a mote of dust*, of *armies clashing on a snail’s horn*. Master Zhu said: *"That which is great has no exterior; that which is small has no interior."* The *Treasure Tower* of *Good Wealth* revealed Maitreya, adorned with countless treasures; yet upon awakening to true enlightenment, all that wealth was found within the pores of Samantabhadra’s body. Vimalakīrti’s room held thirty-two thousand lion thrones. The *Jade Emperor Scripture* says: *"In the heavenly palaces of the ten directions, the Celestial Thearch manifests dharma-bodies to expound the teachings; when the teaching concludes, all return to oneness."* Why should great and small differ, or division and unity be distinct?

Thus, when scattered, it fills the Six Voids; when gathered, it does not fill a handful. The ancients said: *"Reading the entire *Avataṃsaka Sūtra* is not as good as contemplating a single *Gen* hexagram of the *Book of Changes*."* Truly so. When one gathers and restrains the true origin, abiding in stillness, then the myriad things of Heaven and Earth array themselves before one. As *Laozi* says: *"Attain utmost emptiness, abide in profound stillness—then the ten thousand things arise together."* A mote of dust can contain the celestial image; a single truth can respond to ten thousand directions. The vastness of the Six Directions is insufficient to contain one’s body, yet a mustard seed is ample for one’s wanderings.

This *Precious Pearl* is also called *Canghu Jie*, *Perfect Enlightenment*, *Wish-Fulfilling Wheel*, and *Round as a Golden Pellet*, its color like a red tangerine—all names imposed by the sages to guide the unenlightened. Once the fish and rabbit are caught, the trap and snare should be discarded.

Its radiance flows, illuminating the form.

The Dao is not far from humanity, yet people are often admonished with the saying *"to hew a handle"* (learning by analogy). *"Humans can enlarge the Dao"*—one should first reflect on oneself. What is within will manifest without. Thus, one’s brilliance shines forth, the body gleaming with clarity, as it is said: *"Seen on the face, overflowing on the back."* Though hidden, it is as evident as Confucius’ teachings. The subtle becomes manifest; sincerity cannot be concealed. Thus, one who values the Dao, purifies the self, avoids worldly entanglements, conceals traces, and veils light—though seeking no recognition—will naturally be known; though desiring no visibility—will naturally be seen. This is the *flourishing virtue*.

The title is called *Longevity, Ease, and Abundance*—*Longevity, Ease, and Abundance* being the name of the essence of the sun. Within the human body, the radiance of spirit and vitality naturally bestows longevity. As the sutra states: *"If one clings to the notions of self, others, beings, or lifespan, one is no bodhisattva."* Generally speaking, this "longevity" is not the longevity of the mortal world. Humans may live a hundred years, yet those who reach seventy are rare—how can this be called longevity? With such limited understanding, how could one recognize the original, eternal, and indestructible *longevity-nature*? This *longevity-nature* fills heaven and earth, its measure equal to the cosmos, shared with all things and one with all beings. It stands resplendent, vast and unbounded—how could it be confined by numbers or constraints? It is also called *Pavilion of Clarifying the Source*.

To ascend to heights, one must begin from below; to climb a mound, one must start from the plain. This also refers to the division of the left and right eyes. *Pavilion of Clarifying the Source* is the name of the Moon Sovereign, for when the source is clear, its flow is pure. The *pavilion*, in ancient script, resembles a tower or terrace, where immortals gather and abide.

Together, extinguish the mechanisms of the Three Evils. The Three Evils are greed, hatred, and delusion. One who severs these will not fall into the Three Evil Realms and may behold the Three Treasures and Heavenly Lords. *Mechanism* refers to the subtlest movement, upon which fortune, misfortune, regret, and shame depend. Thus, the noble person acts upon perceiving the mechanism, not waiting until the day’s end. The Three Evil Realms are hell, hungry ghosts, and animals—these are the most yin places, from which regaining a human form is difficult. Therefore, one cultivates pure yang to extinguish their pivot. As the scripture says: *"Pray to extinguish the Three Evils, sever the root of earthly bonds."* The same principle applies: the noble person is cautious and vigilant even where unseen, naturally extinguishing the mechanisms of evil.

Open the register and ascend to *Great Clarity*. *Great Clarity* refers to the illumination of the four eyes—some say *Supreme Clarity*, but this is incorrect. Kan-water forever separates one from the realm of Li’s direct illumination. Thus, the sage faces south to rectify the world. The Jade Emperor resides in the *Palace of Pervading Clarity*. When one ascends as an immortal, the celestial register is revealed, and one’s name is inscribed before paying homage to the Jade Emperor. Later, it is said: *"Holding the register, ascend to Great Clarity."* This metaphorically means that for humans, illuminating one’s virtue is paramount. When one’s inherent power is clear and unobscured by sensual desires, one becomes a person of *Great Clarity*—a sage, a true immortal—all of whom take the preservation of their luminous nature as their duty.

Let me safeguard the immortal truth. Only after heaven and earth exist do the myriad things arise. What fills the space between heaven and earth are the myriad things, and among them, none is more spiritually endowed than humans. Yet, failing to cultivate and examine themselves, they fall into the Three Evil Realms. Through the practice of the *Great Cavern Scripture of the Immortals*, one extinguishes these mechanisms and ascends to *Great Clarity*, thereby safeguarding the immortal truth. Some versions say *"enable you to safeguard the immortal truth"*—when a superior addresses a subordinate, it is *"enable you"*; when a subordinate addresses a superior, it is *"let me"*—both are acceptable without harming the meaning. To safeguard one’s own true qi is essential for immortality; one cannot rely on others to preserve it for them.

The immortal sash drapes in emerald green. The Jade Emperor bestows a sash of azure and purple, allowing the adept to wear it when paying homage—a process called *"selecting immortals and recommending scholars."* It is akin to passing the imperial examination in the mortal world, where one is first granted a green robe. In the following passage, it is said: *"Draped in crimson, amidst the green mist"*—both refer to immortal garments.

Dissolve misfortune on the dark paths. Once inscribed in the immortal register, misfortune sinks into the nine depths of the underworld’s shadowy paths. In the mortal world, obtaining an official position brings honor to one’s wife and children, extending blessings to one’s clan—this is but fleeting glory. How much more noble is one who embodies emptiness and tranquility!

Surpass blessings in the morning’s radiance. The officials of the dharma can resolve doubts and disputes. Though they lack cultivation, upon death, they become yin ghosts and are appointed as yin officials, rotating every forty-nine years—a fate shared by all. If one nurtures both inner and outer, cultivating both fortune and wisdom, one attains the immortal Dao. With one’s own true spirit, one receives blessings in the luminous morning above, enjoying boundless joy and freedom.

The term *morning* appears eleven times in various contexts: *"Roaming the golden dawn of the celestial morning," "The sun transforms into three mornings," "The yellow radiance of the morning’s qi," "The high morning reflects Upper Clarity," "Riding the morning’s splendor," "The seven mornings return to the Emperor’s seat," "Jade gates reflect the morning mist," "Surpassing blessings in the morning’s radiance,"* and *"Feathered immortals in the moonlit morning," "Ascending the Hall of Vast Spirit in the morning," "Entering the Chamber of the Heavenly Elder in the morning."* These cannot be uniformly interpreted but must be explained according to the scriptural context. Those who have not studied the canon but rely on transmitted texts to arbitrarily alter the classics are fools who should fear the inescapable karmic retribution—how can they not be warned and cautioned?

Transcend the world and ascend to the Jade Realm. Passing beyond the dust of kalpas, one enters the Jade Realm. Jade symbolizes warmth and harmony. The realm of the Great Yang Dao knows no suffering from heat or cold, where the four seasons are as mild as spring’s qi—thus it is called the *Jade Realm of Great Purity*, where no sun or moon exists, and so there is no day or night, no cold or heat.

The ancestors of countless generations return as infants. The ancestors of past lives—forefathers, grandfathers, and beyond—return to the womb and are reborn in the form of infants. This is called the *Great Cavern Emperor’s* manifestation among humans. Some argue that since these ancestors bear no karmic burden, there is no need for salvation. Yet this scripture provides salvation in sixteen instances, demonstrating that only when one’s thoughts are constantly directed toward elevating one’s ancestors—forefathers, grandfathers, and beyond—is one permitted to ascend oneself. The intent of the Heavenly King is profound indeed!

Here, I categorize them as follows: *"Liberating the roots of the seven ancestors," "Dissolving the accumulated corpses of the seven ancestors," "Breaking the blockages of the seven ancestors," "Returning the seven ancestors as infant immortals," "Severing the dark stagnation of the seven ancestors," "Dispersing the accumulated stagnation of the seven ancestors," "Birthing the seven ancestors in the Hall of Fortune," "Untying the knots to birth the seven ancestors," "The seven mysteries ascend to the Crimson Palace," "The seven mysteries depart the dark burdens," "Dispersing misfortune to pacify the nine mysteries," "The nine mysteries dissolve heavy knots," "Western liberation from accumulated kalpas of misfortune," "The ancestors of countless generations return as infants,"* and *"The ancestors of countless generations shed their karmic names."* These correspond to the *Scripture of Salvation’s* *"Five Sufferings and Eight Difficulties,"* *"Ascension of the Seven Ancestors,"* and *"Deliverance of Souls to the Crimson Mound."*

It is also said: *"For the departed souls of past lives, sever the bonds of earthly servitude."* Those who seek the immortal Dao must first purify body and mind. Purity means being unstained and unattached, neither increasing nor decreasing. Only when one is pure can one perform meritorious deeds, moving heaven and earth to liberate ancestors, broadly delivering all beings, and only then can one deliver oneself—thus feeling no shame.

Within the boundless void of penetrating vision—
*"Penetrating"* means "unobstructed," referring to the ten wondrous practices of perfect clarity. When observed through the mundane eye (read in level tone), or inwardly perceived with mind and gaze (read in departing tone), one gazes upward to the Nine Heavens and downward to the Nine Earths. The middle scroll’s ten chapters are called the *Ten Penetrations*; this is the title of the *Great Penetration*. Thus:

*Penetrating vision in the unobstructed void,*
*Penetrating subtlety in the barrierless mystery,*
*Penetrating emptiness in pure clarity,*
*Penetrating vacuity in serene harmony,*
*Penetrating numen in pure conduct,*
*Penetrating truth in the immaculate body,*
*Penetrating mystery in pure radiance,*
*Penetrating origin in pure light,*
*Penetrating illumination in pure brilliance,*
*Penetrating clarity in dark wisdom—*

These are the *Ten Great Penetrations*, wherein wondrous practice and wondrous fruition reach perfection. Only then does the initial clarity of *hetu-pratyaya* arise.

The *Book of Changes* states: *"Suspended images manifest brightness—none greater than the sun and moon."* As the sun departs and the moon returns, cold and heat arise. Without sun and moon, the Dao’s principles remain unseen; without them, heaven would be an endless night. Thus the character *ming* (明, "brightness") is composed of *ri* (日, "sun") and *yue* (月, "moon"). When the Dao-eye first opens, nothing escapes its sight—even a speck of dust as fine as an autumn hair cannot elude it.

The scripture says: *"The sacred sun and sacred moon illumine the Golden Court."* It is also said: *"The sage combines the brightness of sun and moon."* The great person is inwardly luminous yet outwardly dim, while the common person is inwardly dim yet outwardly bright—thus swayed by circumstances and things.

The *Luminous Pearl in the Black Dragon’s Jaw*—
The sage possesses square pupils; Shun had double pupils. When the human Dao-eye first opens, it is like the pearl beneath the black dragon’s chin—lucid, translucent, and resplendent. For one of thorough attainment, the entire body becomes an eye and hand; wherever touched, it is as if the Thousand-Handed Avalokiteśvara responds.

*Within and without, penetrating illumination and clarity—*
Inside and out, all is brightly revealed, pure and unobstructed—this is heaven’s mirror bestowed upon one. Those who cultivate the *Great Penetration* may gaze upward to the Nine Heavens above and peer downward to the Nine Earths below, comprehending the principles of all things without the slightest concealment.

The *Great Penetration’s* golden elixir requires the gathering of lead and mercury. As the ancients said: *"At the pool’s bottom, the sun’s red glow dispels yin demons; lead is the mountain’s yang qi, the moon’s white medicine sprouts anew; mercury is yang essence."* When yang returns to yang, both eyes become like golden stars, capable of penetrating the Way of day and night. By day, the left eye is used; by night, the right—thus substituting for the brightness of sun and moon.

The above jade verse in celestial script comprises one hundred twenty characters. Above, it governs the *Luminous Ancestral Heaven of Radiant Brilliance*; below, it commands the *Third Tier’s Emperor of Virtue*.

The *Mysterious Covenant* states: *"When the perfected attain penetrating vision and pure clarity, the Dao-eye first opens—unobstructed and barrierless, inwardly and outwardly luminous, perceiving all. They can sever the evil roots of Fengdu Mountain’s *Zhoujue Yintian* Palace, the earthly roots, demonic registers, and ghostly ledgers. Constantly offering celestial blossoms and wafting incense to the Celestial Venerable of Primordial Beginning—who is none other than one’s own indestructible primordial spirit through kalpas, not externally derived—scattering flowers and wafting fragrance, they ascend to the rank of *Human Immortal*."*

The middle scroll’s *Ten Immortals* refer to the *embryo, womb, ethereal soul, corporeal soul, numen, origin, radiance, Mount Hua, viscera, and primordial destiny*. From the first month’s formation of the embryo, they develop in sequence, eventually entering the *Ten Immortal Gates*—as annotated beneath the *Ten Perfected* of the *Subtle Practice of the Mind-Organ* in the middle scroll. Few practitioners may comprehend this, so here, from the *Books of Cultivating Truth*, the *Ten Immortals* are expounded for benefit.

The *Human Immortal* is one whose lifespan exceeds a hundred years, having witnessed countless human generations—such as Laozi at nine hundred years or Peng Zu at eight hundred.

The Celestial Venerable of Primordial Beginning states: *"The twelfth jade chapter of the *Great Penetration of Wenchang*—the ear-root’s penetrating clarity, the sage’s ear attuned to the Brahmā-sound."* [Cyclical years:] *Dingyou, Wuxu, Kui, and Sai.*

The Jade Dawn’s Nine Heavens Controller governs the ear-root—merely hearing sounds, the numinous clarity is stirred, turning with the sound toward good or evil. In an instant, they diverge; a hair’s breadth of difference leads to a thousand *li* of error. Thus, Shun delighted in questioning and examining, Yu heeded good words, Robber Zhi rejoiced in hearing evil, and King Zhou took pleasure in sounds—all through the ear’s listening.

Once, a monk sat in meditation when a crow cawed above him. Someone asked, *"Did you hear it?"* The monk replied, *"I did not hear."* *"Why did you not hear?"* *"Within hearing, there was no hearing."* From this, we see that hearing is not truly unhearing—only that the mind does not cling to it.

The Jade Clarity Numinous Treasure resides above the Nine Heavens. The Nine Heavens comprise three, for from the One *qi* arise the Three *qi*—these are the Three Treasures. From the Three *qi* arise the Nine *qi*—these are the Nine Heavens, the heavens that generate spirits, such as the *Yudan Immeasurable Heaven*. There are also the Eight Brahmā and Nine Heavens: the *Beginning Azure Heaven*, *Great Azure Heaven*, *Beginning Cinnabar Heaven*, *Great Cinnabar Heaven*, *Beginning Plain Heaven*, *Great Plain Heaven*, *Beginning Mysterious Heaven*, *Great Mysterious Heaven*, and *Great Brahmā Heaven*—these too are called the Nine Heavens.

It is also said: the *Exalted Divine Numinous Heaven*. The *South Pole Lord of Longevity*, the *East Pole Lord of Azure Florescence*, the *Nine Heavens Responsive Primordial Thunder Voice Universal Transformation Heavenly Worthy*, the *Nine Heavens Thunder Ancestor Great Emperor*, the *Highest Clarity Purple Tenuity Azure Jade Palace Great Unity Heavenly Emperor*, the *Six Heavens Cavern Abyss Great Emperor*, the *Lord Emperor of the Six Waves Heaven*, and the *Perfected Lord Han of Kě, Nine Heavens Investigator*—these are the Nine Numinous of the Divine Numinous Heaven, wielding the power of life and death, issuing commands, thunder roaring and wind rushing. Thus, the myriad things arise and conclude through them. The *Jade Clarity Dao Lord* presides over them, residing in the human Central Elixir Field.

The *Supreme Great Dao Lord*—the *Dao Lord* is a lord of the Dao. Long ago, the Numinous Treasure descended to be born as the king of *Xina*, bringing great peace to the realm. The people praised him as *"possessing the Dao."* *Dao* means *"to tread"*—who can exit without passing through the door? What can be done without following this Way? It encompasses the affairs of *"illuminating virtue and renewing the people,"* extending from one’s family to the state and thence to the world, all capable of emulation from above to below.

*Laozi* said: *"Cultivate it in the self, and its virtue becomes true; extend it to the world, and it becomes universal."* *The Doctrine of the Mean* said: *"The Way is not far from man."* If one practices the Way yet distances oneself from others, it cannot be called the Way. The great affairs of *"cultivating the self, regulating the family, governing the state, and pacifying the world"*—how can they not proceed from rectifying the self and sincerely aligning the mind, then pacifying and governing the world?

Thus, the man of the Dao devotes himself to benefiting the world and aiding others. When Jie and Zhou were without the Way, the people suffered calamity. Kings Wen and Tang of Zhou rescued the people from water and fire, relieving their inverted-hanging distress. Later generations praised them as lords of the Way.

**Constantly Preserve the Radiant Transformation Within**
The *Jade Scripture* states: *"If the Son of Heaven, kings, or lords uphold it, their states will attain great peace—wealth will enrich the nation, the people will be secure, the army will be strong and victorious, and externally, there will be no harassment from bandits or thieves. The altars of soil and grain will be eternally preserved."* Reciting this scripture is especially for the sovereign, ministers, fathers, and sons to stabilize the land, ensuring the heavens endure long. It is likened to a person whose essence and *qi* are replete, the body robust and strong, free from the encroachment of perverse *qi*, naturally preserving longevity and health. Thus, one preserves within the radiant transformation of creation, preventing its loss or the disturbance of one’s supreme Way by external perversities, the corruption of one’s numinous root, or the theft of one’s supreme treasure. This is *"preserving the radiant transformation."*

**Nine Revolutions, Mirror-Clear**
Nine and ten unite like a mirror’s clarity, penetratingly perceiving all things. The *Jade Emperor Scripture* says: *"Corrupting the numinous root, stealing the supreme treasure"*—this is the failure to preserve the radiant transformation, leading to a mirror that is not empty and a scale that is not level.

Long ago, Chen Yuming attained the Way of the Bright Mirror. After eighteen years of cultivation, he ascended on the first day of the third month in the first year of the *Taikang* era of Jin. During the *Taikang* era, a villager from Xinye, Master Zhang Ruzhen, encountered a divine person descending into his chamber, who transmitted the Way of the *Bright Mirror Penetrating Insight*, saying: *"That which illuminates the principles of things is Heaven; that which reflects the forms of things is the Way. Heaven’s Way is clear; the mirror’s Way is bright. Scrutinized without error, form is fixed here, and things respond there—thus, the shapes of rivers and mountains, the dispositions of ghosts and spirits, have nowhere to hide."*

*"Heaven, through clarity, contains the myriad existences; water, through stillness, reflects all forms. If Heaven is clear and the mirror bright, the mind still and the spirit tranquil, one attains inner and outer penetration—then the supreme Way is achieved. But if externally enslaved by things and internally wearied in spirit, the mind and spirit grow turbid and cannot be stilled, one drifts far from the Way."*

*"This method I received from Lord Changsang; Lord Changsang received it from the Supreme Clarity Heavenly Emperor. If you cultivate it, you will penetrate the mysterious and communicate with the distant, illuminating the eight extremities. Within the *Cavern Reality* methods, there is the Way of the Four Regulations, practiced according to the four seasons—it is the same as this."*

*"The ancients said: 'Empty the chamber, and whiteness arises of itself; settle the mind, and the Way forms of itself.' How true!"* After nine years of cultivation, Ruzhen could see a thousand *li* without a single thing concealed. On the eighteenth day of the eleventh month in the thirteenth year of the *Tianjian* era of Liang, he ascended, styled *Perfected of Complete Truth and Attained Way*. This is the purport of *"Nine Revolutions, Mirror-Clear."*

Each sentence of this scripture governs one affair. If a person practices one sentence, they unite with the Dao and become a perfected one.

**Unbinding the Jade’s Luster in the Chamber**
The *Jade Luster Chamber* is the *Highest Clarity Jade Clarity Palace*, located in the human Central Elixir Field. When the knots of the spirit-chamber are unbound, it shines like jade’s radiance. The *Book of Songs* says: *"Though in your chamber, be not ashamed before the leaking roof"*—fearing even that which is unheard.

**Riding the Plain to Enter the Fourfold Illumination**

Plain is emptiness; as the ear is to sound, so riding the plain and emptiness reaches the fourfold acuity. The *Lung Metropolis Lad* is styled *Plain Illuminer* and *Nameless Flower*—illumination arises from the union of sun and moon, and those who first fashioned written characters knew the workings of creation. **Carrying and Lifting the King Within the Sun**: The *Life-Commanding Lord Within the Sun*, styled *Dao-Spirit*, is carried and lifted without a moment’s abandonment. All references to “sun” in ten phrases—*Five Suns Merged in the Chamber*, *Three Suns Shining on Dark Spread*, *One Pearl Revolving Within the Sun*, *Sun as the Threefold Convergence*, *Five Emperors Scattering Sun-Essence*, *Life-Commanding Lad Within the Sun*, *Sun Unfolding Fivefold Radiance*, *Primal Transformation Unlocking Tomorrow’s Sun*, *Flying Rosy Clouds Dispersing Heaven’s Sun*, *Sea-Sun Rising of Itself in the East*—all denote the true numen of the sun, the essence of Grand Yang. In humans, this is the yang within the *Kan* trigram, the single luminous point between the two kidneys, the *King Within the Sun*, established at the *zi* hour of life-generation. **Joining Wings in the Moon’s Dawn**: The two ears divide yin and yang, hence the *King Within the Sun* and the *Dawn Within the Moon*. As in the *True Formula of Yuji and Jielin* by Ancestral Celestial Master, both govern the spirits of sun and moon. *Carrying and Lifting, Joining Wings* means to constantly lift, reflect, and connect without dullness. Formerly, Master Chen and Yang Taichu encountered the Perfected One Nie Shaoyuan, who transmitted the *High Ascent of the Two Effulgences*, and later attained the Dao and ascended. The *Ancient Poem* says:

*The sage seizes the intent of creation,*
*Grasping sun and moon to set within the furnace.*
*Subtly stirring heaven and earth’s essence,*
*Gathering yin and yang to drive gods and ghosts.*

It also says:

*If you ask me of the practice in the world,*
*I point afar to the sun and moon’s wheel.*

And again:

*When sun and moon unite,*
*There lies the birthplace of the body.*
*The original face is true—*
*I urge you to diligently reflect.*

The Scripture says: *Sacred Sun and Sacred Moon illuminate the Golden Court.* The union of sun and moon is their conjunction on the night of the dark moon—inner elixir is refined and conjoined here. **Grand Unity Summons Heavenly Demons**: As briefly explained in the previous scroll, Grand Unity is the qi transformed from the essence of Water Prime. Before heaven and earth, the number One generates Water to form images; before human birth, the essence of the One Qi is sensed and transformed to form the body. Without Water, heaven and earth cannot stand; without essence and qi, the human body cannot stand. *Laozi* says: *Heaven obtains the One and becomes clear; Earth obtains the One and becomes tranquil; spirits obtain the One and become numinous; the myriad things obtain the One and live.* Thus Grand Unity is the ancestral lord of the myriad spirits, and so can wield talismans to summon and control the great demons of the Six Heavens. In the *Scripture of the Great Cavern*, references to Grand Unity number ten: in the upper scroll, *Grand Unity as the Root of Life’s Mandate*, *Grand Unity Residing in the Purple Chamber*; in the middle scroll, *Grand Unity Summons Heavenly Demons*, *Carrying and Lifting the True Grand Unity*; in the lower scroll, *Grand Unity’s Upper Prime Qi*, *Grand Unity’s Chouqiu Lan*, *Grand Unity’s Yang-Wei Illuminator*, *Lifting the Female Grand Unity*, *Feathered Regalia Commanding Grand Unity*, *Grand Unity as King Within the Effulgence*, and so on. The spirit of Grand Unity unites the Five Spirits into one, and thus the Five Viscera each have their Grand Unity—just as there is no place between heaven and earth without water. In the Great Dao, it is called *Grand Unity Heavenly Venerable*; among the various heavens, *Grand Unity Emperor Lord*; within the Nine Heavens, *Jade Palace Grand Unity Great Heavenly Emperor*, who specially governs Water affairs. In the Dipper, it is called *Grand Unity*; in the Five Fortunes and various earthly realms, *Grand Unity Venerable Spirit*; among the Female Unity Perfected, *Grand Unity Primordial Lady*; in humans, *Grand Unity’s Spirit*—there is nowhere it is not present. Grand Unity resides in the human brain. For human transgressions and blessings, minor matters are reviewed and reported to the Emperor by Grand Unity; greater matters are reported by the Three Corpses; the gravest are recorded by the Three Officials. Thus Grand Unity is the leader of human spirits. Obtain the One, and all affairs are complete. Confucius said: *My Way is threaded through with the One.* Humans obtain the One and live; having already lived, if one can again guard the One, then this Way greatly illumines. Upon completion and wholeness, where is the One? Those who understand should devote their hearts to this. A monk asked: *The myriad dharmas return to the One; where does the One return?* The *Elixir Scripture* says: *Upon reaching completion, even the One is absent*—this urges people to have no attachments. To seek fish and hare, one must rely on traps and snares; once fish and hare are obtained, traps and snares may be discarded. It also says: *To cross the river, one needs a raft; upon reaching the shore, the boat is no longer needed.* The Buddha taught: *Act without abiding, and thereby give rise to the mind.* **The Emperor Lord Surveys the Myriad Essences**: The Emperor Lord, also named *Sevenfold Numen* and *Fengling Fan*, constantly guards above the two brows, wielding talismans and registers to summon and control the great demons of the Six Heavens. The *Golden Book* says: *Grand Unity wields talismans; the Emperor Lord ranks lives*—these are the two Perfected. **Uprooting and Blocking the Qi of Death’s Accumulation**: The *Minor Scripture of Salvation from Suffering* says: *Auspicious smoke seals the gate of death.* The demon kings inspect and survey ghostly essences, blocking the gate of death to protect and recommend immortals. The *Chapter on Generating the Spirit* says: *The Primordial Lady blocks the gate of death.* This is the root of life’s mandate for endless generation. **Transcending the Immortal Yellow Court**: The Yellow Court is the Central Immortal Court, toward which the four directions and eight faces pay homage. In humans, it is the spleen and stomach, governing the Granary Palace. Its spirit is called *Yellow Tranquility Lad*, who disperses and transforms to nourish the Four Numinous Ones. Thus transcending this court is to establish the Three Passes. **The Emperor Stands Above the Three Passes**: The Three Passes are Heaven, Earth, and Water—also Heaven, Earth, and Human. The Upper Pass is the *Muddy Pellet*; the Middle Pass, the *Crimson Palace*; the Lower Pass, the *Sea of Qi*. They are also called the Three Essentials. In the *Book of Changes*, this is the Way of the Three Ultimates. The *Yellow Court* says: *Within the Three Passes are essence, qi, and spirit.* **The Eight Winds Dance the Spirit-Soldiers**: *Zhuangzi* says: *You have heard the Heavenly Flute, but not the Earthly Flute; you have heard the Earthly Flute, but not the Human Flute.* The Eight Winds are the spirit-qi of the eight directions. When the four cardinal and four intermediate directions all arise in harmonious thought, the thousand Perfected and myriad Sages rejoice and dance. When the qi of the human body flows smoothly, the myriad spirits are delighted.

When qi is even slightly disharmonious or a single pulse irregular, the human spirit weeps in sorrow. When the human spirit weeps, it will soon depart the body; when spirit departs and qi is cut off, the person perishes—how could one not be vigilant?

This is the method of the Eight Gates Flying Heavenly Wheel, which circulates essence and qi. On the left, embrace the *Blessed Nectar*: the *Blessed Nectar* is fragrant, exquisite wine, also called *Jade Liquid* or *Elixir of Immortality*. It is the qi-fluid of the entire body, irrigating the root source of the kidneys. Kidney qi ascends to the ears; though the two kidneys reside below, their gate lies above, so when the lower is full, the upper hears with clarity. The *Blessed Nectar* is also called *quicksilver*, *divine water*, *wood-fluid*, *Black Tortoise essence*, *Red Phoenix marrow*, *golden liquid*, *golden flower*, *jade pool*, *golden essence*, and *lead-mercury*—all alternate names for the ingredients of the elixir. Cherish essence to nourish qi, cherish qi to nourish spirit, cherish spirit to nourish emptiness, and the Way of the *Great Cavern* is complete.

On the right, lift the *Vessel of Auspicious Origin*. The *Vessel of Auspicious Origin* is called the *Jade Pool*, *Flowery Pool*, *Recumbent Moon Crucible*, *Suspended Womb Cauldron*, *Mysterious Gate*, *Female Portal*, *Yellow Court*, *True Earth*, and *Golden Tripod*—all implements of the elixir chamber. Neither can be lacking; thus the Dao of the elixir is perfected.

*Penetrating the Subtle without Obstruction*—
Hearing the hidden and minute without hindrance, for *penetrating the subtle* is the wondrous fruit and practice of the sage’s ear. This is one of the Six Penetrations. Through cultivation, one may hear beyond the Nine Heavens and below the Nine Earths.

*Brahmā-Permeation gives rise to Empty Clarity*—
*Empty Clarity* is the heart. From sincerity comes clarity—this is nature. The heart is the dwelling of nature. Attaining the nature of sincerity and clarity, one naturally sees with clarity and hears with acuity. *Brahmā-Permeation* is the sage’s ear, hearing all without exception, no sound escaping it.

*Piercing the Forehead to Hear the Ten Directions*—
The *forehead* is the brow. Above, it reaches the round crown; below, it encompasses the four quarters—nothing is not thoroughly penetrated. The *Ten Directions* are the four cardinal, four intermediate, above, and below—ten in all. When one’s *Brahmā-Permeation* and *Empty Clarity* pervade above and below, the four quarters, nothing is not heard with perfect clarity.

*All Sounds are Liberated*—
Every sound, great or small, resounds clearly, none escaping keen hearing. For like responds to like—there is nowhere one does not hear. Yet the deaf, though thunder shakes the mountains, remain unaware. How could one easily restore their original nature?

When the six roots and six dusts are all purified, one may wield the Six Spiritual Penetrations and attain great freedom. The ear root is governed by the kidneys, but often shaken by sensual desire, dissipating essence and qi, leading early to deafness. One must rely on the *Great Cavern* to summon the true and invoke the numinous, returning to spirit and clarity, dredging and opening the channels to restore the original body. Only then can one realize the wondrous practice of *penetrating the subtle*.

The above jade script of celestial seal, one hundred characters in all, governs above the *Zhuluo Huangjia Heaven* and commands below the *Third Rampart’s Emperor of Virtue*.

The *Mysterious Contract* states: When the perfected attain *penetrating the subtle* and purity, the sage’s ear and *Brahmā-Permeation* become unimpeded, inwardly and outwardly empty and bright, hearing all sounds. They can sever the roots of evil in the *Fengdu Mountain*, the *Tai Sha Liang Shi Zong Heavenly Palace*, and the demonic registers of *Di Gen*.
