Constantly offering elixir fruits to the *Primordial Heavenly King*, they bind the living kernel and ascend to become *Ghost Immortals*.

*Ghost Immortals* are those who, though the body dies, retain undimmed spirit, their presence evoking sorrowful longing and luminous clarity. They can bring fortune or misfortune to humans—such as the city gods, earth gods, *Guan Yu*, and *Zhang Fei* of today’s prefectures and counties.

*Jade Purity, Boundless, Supreme Perfected, Literary Florescence, Great Cavern Scripture of the Immortals*, Scroll Five. ● *(One character appears to be missing here.)*

● *(This passage appears to contain textual errors.)* ● *(This passage contains textual corruption; the cited *Zhuangzi* "Qi Wu Lun" originally reads: "You have heard of the human pipes but not the earth pipes; you have heard of the earth pipes but not the heavenly pipes.")*

*The Jade Purity, Boundless, Supreme Perfected, Literary Florescence, Great Cavern Scripture of the Immortals*, Scroll Six. Annotated by Zhongyangzi Wei Qi of Penglai Mountain in Eastern Shu.

The *Primordial Heavenly King* says: The thirteenth jade chapter of the *Great Cavern of Literary Florescence* states—
*"The nasal root penetrates the empty mystery; the subtle breath of qi flows through."*

*Jihai, Gengzi, Release, Diminution.*

The *Grand Purity* floats beyond the void. *Jade Purity, Highest Purity, Grand Purity*—these are the *Three Clarities*, situated above the *Great Veil* within the *Boundless*. Even celestial perfected sages rarely attain this realm, for nothing is more exalted or revered.

The lower scroll states: *"The Highest Purity ascends beyond the rosy clouds; the Jade Purity resides in the Palace of Ten Thousand Flowers."* The Buddhists speak of the *One Body with Three Aspects*: first *Vairocana*, then *Lokeshvara*, and third *Shakyamuni*. In humans, this corresponds to the *Upper, Middle, and Lower Primal* [elixir fields], all contained within a single body. These three cannot be separated even for a moment. The nose perceives fragrance, the heart craves its desires; the nasal cavity connects to the lungs, and the lungs govern qi, which is inevitably depleted.

Once, a monk in meditation detected the scent of *fragrant accumulations*. His mind thought, *"This must be a vegetarian offering."* At times, he saw celestial immortals inviting him to the heavenly kitchens. The monk would depart in samadhi and return daily. One day, his master observed him and said, *"You have fallen into a latrine."* The monk did not believe him. The master then instructed him to attend the offering again. Upon his return, the master killed a worm from the latrine, and the monk finally understood. From this, we see that the nose’s perception of fragrance can lead one to become a strange being—unlike *Xiangyan the Youth*, who, upon smelling incense, awakened to its origin and immediately attained fruition. The same fragrance of qi leads to delusion or enlightenment; one must be cautious.

The *Grand Purity* immortal realm floats within the void beyond the absolute, corresponding to humanity’s *Lower Primal* [elixir field]. This is called the *Primordial Ancestral Qi*. If one can preserve it, it is called the *Great Elixir*. When the returning wind merges with it, after a hundred days, spiritual communion is achieved. The *Lower Primal*—or *Lower Cinnabar Field*—is the *Sea of Qi*, the lifeline of the body, where spirit and qi gather. If one cherishes and nurtures it, not depleting it through lust and desire, the elixir will form.

*The Three Heavenly Treasure Talismans.*

The *Three Heavens*—*Pure Tenuity, Yu Yu, and Great Scarlet*—are the abodes of the *Three Treasure Lords*. The *Treasure Spirit Talismans* are the most revered of the *Great Cavern’s* sacred chapters, stabilizing heaven and earth. For humans, cherishing the *Three Fields* and revering the *spirit-qi* is essential to preserving form and life.

*"At midday, the Five Radiance open."*

At noon, the *Spirit Youth of the Controller of Destiny* unfolds the chambers of the *Five Spirits*, their luminous brilliance illuminating heaven and earth. This is like the human heart’s spirit—radiant and resplendent, shining through the *Three Fields*, the five viscera, the hundred meridians, and the nine orifices, leaving nothing unseen.

*"The Azure Emperor abides in eternal roundlessness."*

The East belongs to Wood, governed by the *Azure Emperor*. *"Eternal Roundlessness"* is his name. Liver qi ascends to the East, the domain of Jupiter’s influence, protecting the liver and guarding the hun-soul within the *Eight Darknesses*. Humans and all beings equally partake of this qi.

*"Bearing the register, ascending to Great Brilliance."*

The *Great Cavern of Literary Florescence* contains similar passages. The first chapter states: *"Open the register, ascend to Great Brilliance."* Now, *Great Brilliance* emerges from the East, so the *Azure Emperor*, riding the light, bears the immortal register to the *Hall of Great Brilliance* of the *Jade Emperor* to present and review it.

*"Receive the talisman in the Golden Flower Tower."*

Having ascended as an immortal, one must reverently receive the sacred talisman in the *Golden Flower Tower* to enter the celestial register. The *Golden Flower Tower* is the *Twelvefold Tower of the Lungs*, for the nasal qi descends to the lung palace, and lung qi naturally rises from the *Tower*.

*"The five viscera plant jade roots."*

The nose’s perception of odors, when aligned with correctness, harmonizes the five viscera. Heaven’s five phases each possess their roots, and the human five viscera likewise have theirs. Jade is likened to virtue for its warmth and luster. When the root is warm and lustrous, branches and leaves flourish; when the five viscera are warm and lustrous, spirit and essence manifest externally.

*Wang Shuhe’s* *Classic of the Pulse* states: *"The wise can harmonize the five viscera."* The *Yellow Court Scripture* says: *"The nasal spirit, Jade Ridge, is numinous and firm."* The nose is also called the *Mountain Root*, derived from this principle. The upper scroll mentions the *Five Elders assisting the Jade Root*—the *Five Elders* being the spirits of the five viscera, mutually illuminating for clarity.

*"The hun and po likewise congeal in harmony."*

The Scripture states: *"Return the qi of the Upper Heaven to restrain the nine heavenly hun."* The yang-hun is spirit; the yin-po is ghost. Without harmonious qi to bind them, they diverge. In humans, when yin and yang harmonize, the hun congeals and the po gathers, giving life. When yin and yang separate, the hun ascends as spirit, and the po descends as ghost.

The *Book of Changes* says: *"Essence and qi become things; the wandering hun undergoes transformation."* Thus, we know the conditions of ghosts and spirits. On the left are the *Three Hun*; on the right, the *Seven Po*. When each rests in its proper place, they naturally congeal, and their qi flows smoothly through the four limbs. Spirit, essence, hun, po, and intent are the mother of the *Great Elixir*. Is this not why the *Scripture of Salvation* instructs that reciting this scripture on one’s *life-day* results in the hun-spirit becoming pure and upright?

The *Elixir Scripture* states: *"The sun’s hun and the moon’s po—if one recognizes them, one becomes an immortal."* Refine and ingest them for a thousand days, and the body, free of yin, cannot die. The adept should refine the yin-po to assist the yang-hun, making ascension effortless.

*"The empty cavern is pure and mysterious."*

Within the empty cavern, nothing external—no speck of dust—can enter, and nothing internal—no spirit or qi—can escape. Thus, it congeals in purity, mysterious beyond mystery.

The *empty cavern* is the wondrous practice of *nasal contemplation*. One should keep the breath pure and still, untainted by fragrance or stench.

*"Qi flows, giving rise to luminous clarity."*

Among the fragrant scents of myriad treasures, none is as penetrating as musk from the brain. Yet, being an external substance, it is inferior to one’s own *Fivefold True Fragrance*, which, when cultivated, manifests as *non-action and natural purity*. Even this is surpassed by the *subtle, liberated, natural fragrance* perceived by the *Night-Glow Jade Maiden*, which is the most sublime.

In humans, lung qi ascends to the nose, becoming pure and undefiled, free from admixture. Practicing the *True Way of the Imperial Unity of the Great Cavern* to this point, the fragrant qi pervades all, penetrating above and below without exception. All who perceive this fragrance attain liberation.

Stillness and wondrous luminous awareness—once stabilized, it remains unchanging. When harmony pervades the realm of wondrous luminous awareness, the mind of luminous clarity naturally receives the qi of Great Harmony. The dung beetle rolling its ball and the tortoise drawing in qi both attain transcendence—thus does the Buddhist teaching speak of the "wondrous realm of Perfect Awakening" as one with this.

Mysterious breath naturally engenders longevity. The bearing of Highest Heaven is soundless and scentless—how could it be sought through voices, colors, smiles, or appearances? One must strive for utter silence and absence of perception, and true hearing will naturally arise. The Way of nasal contemplation is vast; it is called *embryonic breathing*. The methods of embryonic breathing taught by the various immortals often involve placing a goose feather at the tip of the nose to count the breaths as qi enters and exits—from one to ten, ten to a hundred, a hundred to a thousand, a thousand to ten thousand—until the breath becomes so stabilized that it neither comes nor goes. Some sit at the bottom of deep abysses for days without emerging, thereby forever banishing hunger, thirst, cold, and heat. Those who suffer from hunger, thirst, cold, and heat do so because their primordial qi exits too much and enters too little.

In former times, Xiao Linghu encountered a perfected one who transmitted the method of embryonic breathing. After practicing it, during the Mid-Autumn Festival of the second year of the *Hongdao* era, he underwent a mysterious transformation, his chamber filled with fragrant qi. Many later saw him—though dead, he was not gone. Is this not the Way of long life and enduring vision?

The above jade script of celestial seal, sixty characters in all, governs above the radiant heavens of the *Hall of Empty Clarity* and rules below the Fourth Rampart, moistening the earth and the *Earth Sovereign*. The *Mysterious Contract* states: When the true person attains the empty clarity of the Great Cavern and the mysterious breath flows unimpeded, without obstruction or hindrance, inner and outer become luminously clear. Fragrant qi suffuses the upright qi, pervading above and below, enabling the severing of the baleful qi of the *Mount Fengdu*, the serene illumination of the *Palace of Sinful Qi*, the roots of evil in the *Celestial Palace* and *Earthly Root*, and the demonic registers and ghostly ledgers. One should constantly offer incense of sincerity to the *Celestial King of Primordial Beginning*, emulate the great completion of *King Kui*, and ascend to become a *Water Immortal*.

The *Water Immortal* arises when one falls into water and sinks into the abyss, yet the hun and po do not scatter. Along the banks of rivers and marshes, they appear and disappear, vanish and manifest—such as Qu Yuan, Guo Pu, and Liu Yi. The *Celestial King of Primordial Beginning* said: The fourteenth jade scripture of the *Great Cavern of Wenchang* concerns the *hollow emptiness of the tongue-root*, the mysterious communication of the tongue’s blossom.

*Xinchou*, *Renyin*, *Yi*, *Guai*.

The *Celestial King of the Primordial Radiance of the Supreme Ultimate*:
Discoursing on the mysterious and expounding the Dao, engaging in ornate speech and reckless words, craving and indulging in flavors—all these pertain to the tongue. Thus, the tongue-root is most weighty, and what humans must cultivate. The *Book of Changes* says: "Words and deeds are the hinge and spring of the noble one." One should ensure that words match deeds and deeds match words, not excessively indulging in flavors. Serene magnanimity is supreme, and the true qi of Great Harmony will naturally descend to communicate with the *Crimson Palace*—for the heart connects to the tongue.

Before the Supreme Ultimate divided, the primordial radiance was in profound darkness; after its division, the primordial radiance became luminous. Thus is the primordial radiance honored as king. The scripture says: "The Three Luminaries of Opening Clarity are the root of heaven." Hence, the Supreme Ultimate is king, and every thing possesses a Supreme Ultimate.

The Three Heavens gather the spirit and engender life.
The Three Heavens are *Jade Clarity*, *Highest Clarity*, and *Great Clarity*. "Gathering the spirit and engendering life"—some say "spirit king," but this is incorrect. Only when the three qi harmonize in virtue and the nine qi align in unison is the spirit engendered. Highest Heaven has ten thousand spirits, and thus the human body also possesses ten thousand spirits.

The purple and plain obscure the towering peak.
The *Left Primordial Sovereign of Purple Simplicity*, *Ke Yi Yu Ren*, whose style is *An Lai Shang*, is also known by the alias *Wu Ying*—hence later referred to as *White Simplicity* and *White Primordial*. The qi of purple and plain obscures the towering peak—*ren* means the tip, the summit of a sharp peak. If one can maintain purity and simplicity in guarding the head, this qi will naturally cover it. The third chapter of the preceding upper section says: "Gazing upward to meet the peak without measure," referring to the *Mount Jade Capital*. These three plainnesses—later there is the *Middle Primordial Sovereign of Yellow Simplicity* and the *Right Primordial Sovereign of White Simplicity*—are called the *Three Elder Sovereigns of Simplicity*. The earlier and later passages mutually reveal their meanings, repeated for clarity and analogy.

*An Lai Shang* ascends the *Jade Capital*.
The style of the *Purple Simplicity Sovereign* is *An Lai Shang*, who meets at *Mount Jade Capital*. In the fifth chapter of the following lower section, the name above jade is identical in meaning. The *Celestial King of Primordial Radiance* gathers the hun and engenders the spirit—for *primordial* is the chief of goodness, thus the leader of all spirits.

Uprooting from the realm of the five sufferings:
The five flavors confuse the mouth. The five flavors—sour, bitter, sweet, pungent, salty—those who indulge in them shorten their lives and fall into the realm of the five sufferings. Having already ascended the *Jade Capital*, one must first excel and transcend the three paths and five sufferings. The first chapter of the upper section speaks of uprooting from the *Three Paths Bridge*; the tongue chapter of the middle section speaks of uprooting from the *Realm of Five Sufferings*; the hands and feet chapter speaks of uprooting from the *Five Poisonous Sufferings*; the nature and life chapter speaks of extinguishing the *Three Paths Corpses*; the essence and blood chapter speaks of severing the *Three Paths Sufferings*; the eighth chapter of the lower section speaks of removing the registers of the *Three Lower Paths*; the thirteenth chapter speaks of cutting off the *Three Paths Afflictions*.

The three paths are all errors—how can one change after long delay?
*Tu* means servitude. The *Heavenly Servitude* is tabooed as *Ke Han Ming*; the *Human Servitude* arises from the cycle of life and death; the *Earthly Servitude* involves solitary bondage and displacement. Sever the *Upper Corpse Path of the Heavenly Servitude* at the *Gate of Sensual Desire*, to avoid the servitude of the *Celestial Officials* driving thunder and chasing lightning. Sever the *Middle Corpse Path of the Earthly Servitude* at the *Gate of Love Desire*, to avoid the servitude of the *Earthly Officials* carrying sand and bearing stones. Sever the *Lower Corpse Path of the Human Servitude* at the *Gate of Greed Desire*, to avoid the servitude of the *Water Officials* endlessly drawing from the dark waves.

The five sufferings: Passing through the first, the *Gate of Suffering from Sensual Bondage*, frees one from the suffering of the *Mount Tai Hell*. Passing through the second, the *Gate of Suffering from Love Bondage*, frees one from the suffering of the *Wind Blade Hell*. Passing through the third, the *Gate of Suffering from Greed Bondage*, frees one from the suffering of carrying sand and bearing stones. Passing through the fourth, the *Gate of Suffering from Florid Competition*, frees one from the suffering of filling the sea and digging rivers. Passing through the fifth, the *Gate of Suffering from Bodily Bondage*, frees one from the suffering of swallowing fire, eating coals, and boiling in cauldrons.

In cultivating the *Great Cavern of Wenchang*, one must sever the three servitudes and transcend the five sufferings. The three and five together form the eight difficulties—this is what the upper scripture describes as transcending the five sufferings and eight difficulties.

Returning to the womb of the Seven Primordials’ courtyard.
The Seven Primordials are the *Water Pool*, the abode of the *Potter’s Po*. The *Scripture of the Northern Dipper* governs the netherworld and presides over the sources of water. Beneath the tongue, to the left is *Golden Fluid*, to the right is *Jade Humor*—these flow downward to irrigate the heart. The heart has seven apertures, corresponding to the seven stars of the Dipper.

The Nine Mysteries dissolve the weight of kalpas,
the Seven Mysteries and Nine Ancestors together release the suffering of accumulated kalpas and layered yin.
Cultivating the *Great Cavern of Wenchang* through the *Returning Wind* and *Merging Harmonies* with the *True Dao of the Imperial One*
can resolve ten thousand kalpas of past lives,
dissipate the clamor of lawsuits and summons across a thousand births,
and sever the entangled grievances of karmic retribution.
The names of ancestors burdened by grievances fall away.
The names of forebears across generations, erased from the ledgers of debt,
all ascend to the upper realms,
roaming and feasting in leisure beneath the *Luminous Flowers*—
this is the *Scripture of Salvation*’s *Purple Void’s Fragrant Luminous Palace*,
awaiting the cyclical turning of destiny to ascend and transform.

Roaming beneath the *Luminous Flowers*,
sweet and pungent disperse as yang,
sour and bitter surge and drain as yin.
The two qi bend and stretch beneath the *Flower Canopy* of *Jade Capital*,
as the canopy of flowers covers all heavens.
In the five viscera, the lungs are the *Flower Canopy*.
"Roaming" means leisurely feasting and wandering.

Lowering and raising to summon the Five Spirits.
The Five Spirits are the Five Elders, as noted in the final chapter of the previous scroll.
The ancients said: "Practicing the Dao is not difficult—it lies in the space between lowering and raising."
If one often gazes downward at the five viscera and exhales upward to the true qi,
the primordial spirit will manifest in form.

The body of the adept ascends to the *Jade Hall*.
The *Golden Horse* and *Jade Hall* are worldly honors,
but when your body attains the Dao and ascends to the *Jade Hall*—
the palace of the Jade Emperor, located above the head—
the five qi paying homage to the origin all converge here.
The *Scripture of Salvation* states: "Roaming the Upper Clarity, entering and exiting the *Flower Chambers*," which refers to the same.

The Five Spirits return as infants.
The Five Spirits are: *Left Non-Ultraviolet*, *Right White Prime*, *Great One*, *Controller of Destinies*, *Peach Prosperity*, and *Union of Longevity*.
"Returning as infants" means they all transform into newborns and children.
At this stage of cultivation, it is called the *Great Cavern’s Imperial Venerable* manifesting.

Together they ascend beyond the *Great Vastness*.
Rising into the formless beyond,
the third chapter of the upper scripture also says: "The numinous pass lies beneath the *Great Vastness*."
This means flying beyond the *Empty Vastness* of no traces,
to the land of *Nothing-Whatsoever*,
the expanse of the *Boundless Wilderness*—
thus confirming the earlier *Grand Perfected* without doubt.

Nurturing simplicity to pay homage to the *Perfect Illumination*.
"Nurturing simplicity" means abstaining from meat.
The ancients said: "Fine wine and delicacies are the halberds and spears that harm one’s nature;
lewd sounds and beautiful forms are the axes and saws that break one’s bones."
Those who skillfully nurture simplicity remain tranquil, desireless, and serene,
cultivating simplicity through stillness and non-action.
"Paying homage to the *Perfect Illumination*" refers to the celestial image, round and radiant with luminous brilliance.
Lord Lao said: "If a person can remain constantly pure and still, heaven and earth will all return to them."
This illustrates that if one can be clear, empty, and indifferent,
they will naturally perceive their original nature—heaven’s emptiness, roundness, and numinous clarity.
The *Perfect Illumination* is the *Mysterious Pass*, the single aperture—
not belonging to the heart, kidneys, mouth, or nose.
If one knows this single aperture,
then the winter solstice resides here,
as do the medicinal substances, fire phases, bathing, and womb liberation—all are found here.
The ancients said: "The *Mysterious Pass*, the single aperture, is the great root-source of heaven and earth,
harmonizing with the *Five Thousand Characters* and penetrating the three hundred verses"—
this is precisely it.
It is also called the method of *Silent Homage to the Emperor*.
Formerly, Zhang Tan’yao received from the Heavenly Perfected the *Dao of Internal Nourishment, Primordial Harmony, and Silent Homage to the Emperor*.
After practicing it for twelve years, he ascended lightly.
The Emperor then bestowed upon him the *Liquid of Merging Spirit and Merging Radiance*,
which he ingested, undergoing unfathomable transformations,
and was granted the title *Preserving Light, Inheriting Clarity Perfected*.

The scripture states: "Silent homage to the Emperor leads to ascension in one cycle."
Yet without encountering a enlightened teacher to point out the path of return,
the way of silent homage would also become overgrown.

The *Great Cavern* is empty, clear, and harmonious.
Eating in season, the hundred bones are ordered;
blandness allows the upright qi to settle.
People’s craving for spiciness depletes their true qi,
while craving for salt and fermented sauces shortens their lifespan.
All cravings harm the five viscera—
nothing compares to eating blandly,
for then the spirit is refreshed.
This is the wondrous practice of the *Empty Cavern*.

The *Flower* connects and guides the *Mysterious Illumination*.
Once the tongue’s *Flower* is connected,
it naturally draws the *Mysterious Illumination*’s liquid,
which is swallowed to irrigate the numinous root.
The tongue spirit connects with the *Controller of Life* and the *Upright Order of the Empty Cavern*—
this is the wondrous practice of refining the tongue’s root,
remaining unstained by the five flavors to preserve purity.

Licking and refining the *Five Sprout Pearls*.
The *Five Sprout Pearls* are the essence qi of the five phases—
metal, wood, water, fire, and earth—
the true colors of the five qi: green, red, white, black, and yellow,
the fluids of the five viscera.
When the five qi pay homage to the origin,
they transform into seminal essence,
descending from the brain to the *Crimson Palace*—
this is called the *Five Sprout Pearls*.
The *Yellow Court* states: "Storing and rinsing the five sprouts banishes hunger and thirst."
"Sprouts" signify the beginning of growth,
not yet forming a thicket.
When a person eliminates the five flavors,
they naturally obtain the rich savor of the Dao’s essence.
Nourishing and swallowing the *Great Harmony*
can generate the five sprouts.
The scripture says: "Golden grains and jade nectar—
all sought after—arrive here."

Holding the *Good Flavor* to attain longevity.
The *Traditions* say: "All people eat and drink, yet few truly know flavor."
"Good" refers to water, which is good and benefits all things.
People are without exception good;
water is without exception downward-flowing.
"Flavor" refers to the four seasons: sour in spring, bitter in summer, pungent in autumn, salty in winter,
and sweet in the four transitional periods.
If one can exhale and inhale the flavors of their original viscera in accordance with the seasons,
allowing the fluids to irrigate the spleen and stomach,
then the qi and vessels will flow smoothly.
Holding the blossoms and chewing the petals,
the savor is good, refreshing, and delightful.
The body and countenance become joyful,
the hands and feet light and nimble—
naturally attaining the Dao of longevity and enduring vision.
The method of exhaling and inhaling the five flavors—
*hu*, *he*, *xu*, *xi*, and *chui*—
each corresponds to the four seasons to dispel illness.

The above is the jade chapter of celestial seal-script, ninety characters in total,
which above governs the *Observing Clarity, Upright and Tranquil Heaven*,
and below commands the *Fourth Rampart’s King of Virtue*.
The *Mysterious Contract* states:
"The Perfected attains the *Empty Cavern*, clear and tranquil,
the tongue’s *Flower* connected without obstruction or hindrance,
the internal and external in upright order,
the *Mysterious Illumination*’s pool congealing into butter.
Swallowing the flavor of the *Five Sprout* golden liquid and jade nectar,
they can sever the roots of evil in the *Fengdu* mountain lineage,
the numinous *Seven Non-Heavens* palace,
the *Earth’s Roots*, demonic ledgers, and ghostly accounts.
Constantly offering the Dharma’s food to the *Primordial Heavenly Venerable*,
communicating all flavors,
forming the great rice-pearl,
they advance to become *Earth Immortals*.
*Earth Immortals* appear and disappear at will,
often dwelling in famous mountains, grotto heavens, and blessed lands.
If people suddenly encounter them,
they resemble the people of *Peach Blossom Spring* who fled the Qin,
or the *Hairy Woman of the Mountains*."

The *Primordial Heavenly Venerable* states: The fifteenth jade chapter of the *Great Cavern* of *Wenchang*, "The Root of the Body Caverns the True," reveals the true form where Dao and reality interpenetrate. *Gui-mao*, *jia-chen*, *shen*, and *cui*. The *Peerless True Upper Mystery*—cultivated within the body, its virtue becomes true. For the body receives touch, and the will shifts with it. When the body is cultivated, the Dao is established. Yet people’s attachments—love, pride, sloth, awe, sorrow, or pity—all stray from uprightness. The Master said: "Archery resembles the noble one, who turns inward to seek."

This chapter speaks through the body. The *Peerless* is the *Azure Numinous First Elder* of the East, residing in the human body’s left side and governing the liver. The *Upper Mystery*’s primordial essence is titled *Peerless Duke*, with the taboo name *Mystery Primordial Uncle* and the style *Uniting Talisman Master*. All beings first receive the *Five True Qi* before the *Five Spirits* are born. The *Mystery-Middle Primordial Essence Qi*.

The *Scripture* states: "In heaven’s undifferentiated chaos, the heavenly qi returns to the single body." Thus, the *Primordial Essence Lord Peerless* rides this qi. For the *Nine Primordial Qi* of the *Eastern Primordial King* are born at the *Mysterious Gate*, while yin qi arises from the *Gate of the Female*. The *Great Cavern Scripture* takes qi as its foundation: principle precedes qi, and qi precedes form. Thus, at the *Primordial Beginning*, from the *Hun Dun Supreme Non-Being* of the *Primordial Heaven Treasure Jade Sovereign*, one qi generates three qi, three generate nine qi, and from nine to the ten thousand qi, heaven and earth are established, things are opened, and affairs are accomplished. Heaven, earth, ghosts, and spirits each have their offices, ordered and unconfused.

Humans are the same: from one qi, three qi are born, and from three to the ten thousand qi, the ten thousand spirits are complete—only then is life generated. From infancy to adulthood, from old age to twilight years, returning to the root and restoring life, one remains like an infant. Cultivating this infant, one returns to the One. This is the *Great Cavern*’s method of practice, its beginning and end. Thus, the final verse concludes: "The *Talisman-Transformed Mysterious Qi King*."

The *Book of Changes* states: "Like qi seeks like." For qi of the same kind must merge. Here, the qi terms from the scripture are gathered: In the upper scroll, the *Five Phases* and *Six Qi*, the *Highest Cavern Primordial Qi Ancestor Supreme Non-Being*, the *Auspicious Qi* nurturing the *Five Clouds*, the *Five Qi* knotting the *Ten Directions*, the *Supreme Simplicity Three Flower Qi*; in the middle scroll, the *Crown-Spinning Purple Qi*, the *Dead Accumulated Qi* extracted, the *August Beginning Purple Qi*, the *Mystery-Middle Primordial Essence Qi*, the *Central Yellow Primordial Qi*, the *Azure Essence Upper Flower Qi*, the *Supreme Beginning Nine Primordial Qi*, the *Jade Sovereign’s Qi* congealing into the ten thousand qi; in the lower scroll, the *Nine August Upper True Qi*, the *Heavenly August Upper True Qi*, the *Great One Upper Primordial Qi*, the *White Qi* nurturing upper birth, the *Friend Treasure Red Qi King*, the *Floating Yellow Veiling Spirit Qi*, the *Supreme Center Six Qi* purified, the *Chen-Middle Yellow Radiance Qi*, the *Golden Watchtower Upper Radiance Qi*, the *Five Qi* governing the *Central Harmony*, the *Supreme Mystery Nine Qi*, the ten thousand qi birthing the ten thousand spirits, guarding and sealing the *Dead Qi Pass*, "from now on, dead qi is severed." The ten thousand spirits and ten thousand qi—one qi unites with *Dragon Light*, merging into the *Jade Capital’s Qi*, the *Western Primordial Nine Numinous Qi*, the *Talisman-Transformed Mysterious Qi King*. Initially called *Communing Qi*, there are thirty-four instances of the character *qi*.

The *Great Cavern Scripture* takes qi as its foundation. With qi, one can nourish the spirit; with spirit, one can nourish emptiness. If one can be empty and numinous, one accords with the principle of natural non-being.

*Entrusting Frequency* carries the *Pearl of Circulation*—*Entrusting Frequency* is the *Great One* within the Dipper, constantly turning the *Pearl of the Heart*. It is also called the *Cinnabar Terrace*, *Numinous Terrace*, *Intertwining Pear-Fire Jujube*, or *Night-Shining Pearl*. In truth, the heart spirit is named the *Spirit-Circulating Pearl*, which can be guarded day and night.

*Chaotic Transformation* opens the *Luminous Sun*—the *Nine Souls*’ spirit is named *Chaotic Transformation Return*. Crowned with the *Heaven-Penetrating Crown*, clad in a cyan robe and vermilion shoes, wielding a sword, it constantly rides the *Nine Qi Azure Light*, governing the *Primordial Yang* and opening the *Luminous Sun* to inaugurate the *Azure Yang*’s hall, descending qi as the root of life.

The *Upright One*’s *Left and Right Immortals*—the *Upright One*’s *Left Immortal* is *Emperor Guest*, and the *Right Immortal* is *Jade Harmony*. The two spirits together guard the *E* and *Yin* gates. The *Upright One* is the heart; when the heart is upright, the body is cultivated. Heaven’s sun and moon, earth’s hardness and softness, and humanity’s nature and life.

*Long Guarding the Numinous Void Chamber*—the *Void Bright Numinous Awareness Chamber* is the dwelling of the human heart spirit. To protect it long, preventing external demons from attacking, one must make this body one with the *Great Void*, encompassing the *Dharma Realm*—vast without exterior, minute without interior.

The *Portent* has the *Five Talisman Registers*—all people possess the *Five Qi* and *Five Marchmounts*’ talisman charts and registers. Those with these registers attain the immortal Dao. The *Jade Sovereign Scripture* states: "If one can wear the *Five Directions’ True Writ* and *Five Marchmounts’ Talisman Charts* to enter the mountains and cultivate the Dao, the hundred spirits will be awed and submit."

*Uniting with Immortals to attain the True One*—*True* is the *Sincerity* of the *Doctrine of the Mean*. What practices it is the *One*. The *True One* is the infant, meaning to focus on the One without distraction, sincere and without falsehood. *True* is undivided; *One* is undual. This is the *Undual Dharma Gate of the True One*.

*The Hun souls are born in the Supreme Non-Being*—the *Three Hun* are named *Womb Light*, *Luminous Spirit*, and *Hidden Essence*. Each hun has two attendants, totaling the *Nine Hun*. The *Nine Hun* are born within the *Supreme Non-Being*. The Dao of immortals proceeds from non-being to being, then from being returns to non-being—beginning and end complete.

*The Po souls lie hidden in the Five Paths’ secrecy*—the *Seven Po* are named *Corpse Dog*, *Crouching Arrow*, *Sparrow Yin*, *Swallowing Thief*, *Flying Poison*, *Removing Filth*, and *Stinking Lung*. Together, they are seven. One must nourish the yang hun and subdue the yin po. When the hun are born, the po should be subdued. The five viscera’s evil qi and the roads’ blockages are sealed, never to emerge again.

*Generation after generation, karmic knots are untied*—the *Wenchang Great Cavern*’s *Returning Wind Merging* practice of the *Imperial One True Dao* can untie the myriad kalpas and thousand lives of ancestral grievances, lawsuits, and summons, as well as the entangled karmic debts of parents and clan. All are dissolved and universally liberated.

The Seven Ancestors’ blockages are severed.

Xue Youqi was a native of Baoding in Pu Prefecture. Having passed the imperial examinations in the Kaiyuan era, he was appointed, in his youth, as a magistrate in Ling Commandery. Before his term was complete, stirred by a longing for forests and springs, he cast off his sleeves and entered Mount Shoucheng. He visited the abodes of the Heavenly Masters at Mount Emei and Mount Heming, then journeyed to Mount Nanyue, where he recited the *Great Cavern Scripture*. His disciples numbered in the hundreds, gathering daily at his side as he expounded on the subtle mysteries of the Dao. Emperor Minghuang praised his insights, and he annotated the *Scripture of Numinous Treasure*, devoting himself to refining and delivering the lonely souls of his parents and ancestors. Later, he attained the Dao and ascended in transformation, while hundreds of his disciples achieved liberation through *shi jie*. Was this not because he first delivered his Seven Ancestors before delivering himself?

*The Divine Wind stirs the Womb-Tree*—
The *Scripture of Deliverance* states: *"The Divine Wind is still and silent."* The Divine Wind emerges from the bellows of Heaven and Earth, stirring and animating all life. The Womb-Tree is the root of the womb’s blood and filth. The Divine Wind, as the body’s divine *qi*, can pluck the dead and deliver the living.

*Its roots and branches are utterly severed*—
The root, stem, branches, and leaves of the womb are entirely withered and gone without remnant. Through the cultivation of wondrous practices to this point, relying on the *Returning Wind Merging* Dao, one sweeps away the evil roots and earthly bonds, uprooting the womb’s knots and fetal entanglements at once.

*My kith and kin*—
*The multitude of calamitous ghosts within the womb*—
Within the womb, ghostly spirits abound. The yang spirit desires human life to have something to depend upon, while yin ghosts desire human death to have something to feast upon. Allying with them, the *Lesser Lad of the Great Subtlety* constantly wields banners to summon their souls, descending spirits to spread *qi* and foster their growth into human form. For those not yet born, it is the multitude of ghosts that brings harm. In refining the Golden Elixir, one must also cherish the Sacred Embryo. Formerly, Tang Ruo of Lu Commandery, during the *Pre-Celestial* era, served as a minister and successively governed demanding commanderies. In the Kaiyuan era, he was appointed governor of Runzhou, where his governance was benevolent. His younger brother was a Daoist of Mount Heng, and together they received the essentials of the *Embryonic Valley Spirit*. Often summoned into the palace, Tang Ruo later sought to return to the mountains and was permitted to do so. Upon reaching the Yangzi River, he ascended amidst a five-colored mist and became an immortal. His brother achieved *shi jie*. Those who skillfully nurture the Embryonic Origin are not harmed by ghosts and ascend as divine immortals. The blessings of this scripture for life and death are beyond measure.

*The Five Talismans seal the earth’s knots*—
The Five Talismans are those received by the Five Elders. Heaven possesses Five Talismans to sustain generation and transformation; Earth possesses Five Talismans to maintain tranquility and harmony; humans possess Five Talismans to ensure bodily health and peace. Thus, they obstruct and sever the earth’s stagnant knots.

*Forever as divine perfected immortals*—
Immortals are perfected immortals, divine immortals. There are five kinds of immortals: celestial immortals, terrestrial immortals, aquatic immortals, ghostly immortals, and divine immortals. This chapter focuses on cultivating the root of the body, nurturing the other through the self, and refining the true through the illusory.

*Responding and transforming, they continue for myriad eons*—
Having attained the immortal Dao, one should respond and transform within the world, guiding and delivering all beings. Even the Most Venerable and Noble Lord Lao descended eighty-two times to be born, for he responded to those awaiting deliverance. His thousand transformations and myriad changes far exceed mere continuation for ten thousand eons.

*The Cavern-True purifies the body*—
The root of all under Heaven lies in the body of the One. The five limbs and hundred bones are governed by the master of a single thought. If one loses the power of preservation, calamity and chaos will surely arise. To cultivate the body, first rectify the heart. Once a single thought is rectified, the *ying* and *wei* naturally harmonize. As it is said: *"With a unified will, *qi* moves."* The *Elixir Scripture* states: *"Like a magnet drawing iron, it penetrates barriers unseen. In a single thought, the myriad *qi* and spirits gather as one."* This body is formed of earth, water, fire, and wind. Through cultivation here, a body arises beyond the body. As the ancients said: *"Two [forms] appear identical, yet only when merit is complete does one emerge from the dust."*

*The Dao flows through the natural substance*—
The *Book of Changes* states: *"If it is not the right person, the Dao does not act in vain."* The Dao within the body cannot be separated even for a moment. The Dao flows through the natural substance, which is not the body formed of impure earth, water, fire, and wind. The Buddhist scriptures say: *"Only the Dharma-body abides eternally, unperishing,"* and *"the indestructible Vajra-body."* These are the natural substances, called the wondrous body—unseen when approached, unseen when followed. For it is the profound stillness of true emptiness, pervading Heaven and Earth yet without end, encompassing the cosmos yet without beginning. This is our natural substance.

*The true responds and manifests forms*—
The true and constant nature, still yet responsive, is called the true yang. It manifests forms through transformation, as in the thirty-two marks and eighty excellences of Lord Lao, his thousand transformations and myriad changes, dispersing to answer the prayers of the world, granting all that is sought.

*Abiding unmoved in the Yellow Chamber*—
The true body remains fixed and unchanging; the manifested bodies respond merely to the hearts of people, like the moon reflected in water—one moon in a thousand rivers. As the Buddha said: *"Do not grasp at forms; thusness is unmoving."* The Yellow Chamber is the Yellow Court, the Central Palace.

*The responding and transforming are boundless*—
The responding and transforming bodies are present everywhere, like the moon seen in every river and stream. Even in a thousand vessels of water, the moon is present in each, its size varying only with the vessel’s capacity. So too do the manifestations of the true response vary with the depth of people’s roots and capacities.

Wang Changyu of Shuzhou was a hereditary scribe. Later, in Jiang’an, he encountered a destitute, drunken immortal who called himself the *True Man of the Mysterious and Yellow*. He transmitted to Wang the *Great Elixir of the Red Dragon*. On the Double Ninth Festival of the thirteenth year of the *Great Middle* era of the Great Tang, Wang ascended a parasol tree and departed as an immortal. He was granted the title *Perfected of Preserving Harmony* and appointed Left Minister of the Three Heavens. Later, during the *Zhenghe* era, he transformed into an *Iron Jar Daoist*, selling medicines in the markets of Shuzhou. To his grandson, Wang Daoyuan, he said: *"I am your ancestor."*

The Emperor commanded me to collate the thirty-nine chapters of the *Canon of the Great Cavern*. Now I transmit them to you, along with the three scrolls of the *Secret Register of the Upper Yang’s Inner Prohibitions for Returning Wind, Merging Scenery, Unifying Perfection, and Flying as an Immortal*. Through these, you may understand that once one ascends as an immortal, one must also transform and descend to broadly deliver beings across heaven and earth. Yet the true body remains ever in its celestial position—just as the Jade Emperor divides his form and transforms, never absent from the Golden Tower. So too do the ten thousand qi and ten thousand spirits within the human body: when gathered, they are one; when scattered, they reach the ten directions.

Bone and flesh are as solid as metal and jade. Bone and flesh, like metal and jade, are enduring. For the Dao of *Great Cavern of Wenchang* and *Returning Wind Merging Perfection*, when cultivation reaches its utmost, bone and flesh ascend together. This is because the true fire of the south warms and refines the white tiger’s golden essence to complete the supreme elixir of the Golden Pill—like the hardness of metal and the smoothness of jade. As the transmission says: *"Virtue moistens the body; the heart broadens, and the form flourishes."* In the elixir, the body is lead, and the heart is mercury. When these two substances unite in marriage, they may become as firm as metal and jade. The Buddhists regard this as the *śarīra*, which fire cannot destroy and iron cannot shatter—formed from the undispersed essence and qi of the human body.

The Dao of utmost clarity and true illumination: *"Sincerity in the body has its Dao. Without understanding goodness, one cannot be sincere in the body."* The utmost Dao is the Dao of utmost goodness. Through stillness and the true unity, this perfectly good and beautiful Dao is made luminous. One who can firmly uphold it may become an upper immortal.

Even in extreme old age, this resolve does not change. Though this is spoken for worldly people, it is not the Dao of the upper immortals. The upper immortals attain long life and enduring vision, deathless and unforgetting. For the old endure through kalpas unbroken, their bodies spanning ancient and present time—existing before heaven and earth without beginning, persisting after heaven and earth without end. They stand alone and unchanging, the so-called original substance. The Buddhists speak only of the *dharmakāya* as eternally abiding and indestructible. Most people mistakenly take the four great elements’ temporary union as true reality. Once spirit and qi disperse, it is no better than stinking rot, cast aside—worse than beasts and livestock.

The above jade script in celestial seal comprises one hundred thirty characters. Above, it governs the *Mysterious Brightness and Reverent Celebration Heaven*; below, it commands the *Fourth Rampart and Lord of Virtue*.

The *Mysterious Contract* states: *"The perfected one attains the true, tranquil, and responsive form of the Cavern-Truth, the Dao unobstructed. They eternally abide, transforming into boundless bodies, present without limit. The dharmakāya eternally dwells in the Jade Mountain’s Upper Capital, naturally responding and transforming. In all ten directions, their own body appears, and other bodies attain freedom. They can sever the roots of evil in the Fengdu Mountain’s Daring Bureau, the Linked Winding Heaven Palace, and the demonic registers of the earth’s roots. Constantly, they offer celestial robes and earthly garments to the Primordial Heavenly King, covering above and below, ascending to become divine immortals."*

The divine immortals come and go from grotto-heavens, their transformations ceaseless. Suddenly dwelling among humans, they change their heads and faces—unrecognized by others. These are the *four fruits of arhats* and the *five penetrations of divine immortals*.

The Primordial Heavenly King said: *"The sixteenth jade scripture of the* Great Cavern of Wenchang*: the root of intention penetrates clarity; the great meaning primordially unobstructed."*

*Yisi, Bingwu, Ascending, Distress.*

The nine primordial qi of the Great Beginning: The intention pertains to the central earth, with the spleen and stomach as its dwelling. This is the beginning of the qi of the Great Beginning. The nine primals are the nine yangs, likened to the qi one first receives from father and mother. The character *su* (primordial) appears thirteen times. The upper scroll says: *"Three primordials give birth to the nine muds,"* referring to the Three Primordial Lords—whose taboo names are Han, Zhang, and Boshi—initiating the three primordials. The *qi of the Three Primordial Florals*, the *Three Primordials brushing the distant scene*—these phrases share the same meaning. The middle scroll’s *"riding the primordial into the four luminaries"* differs in principle. *Suqi* initiates Xiao Ren as the name of the White Primordial Lord, the *primordial qi of the Mysterious Center*—referring to *Wu Ying*. The central yellow primordial qi: the Yellow Elder Lord’s nine primordial qi of the Great Beginning, the first sprouting of the nine yang qi. The lower scroll’s *"Great Primordial Brahman Conduct Initiation"* refers to the five great qi before form and substance separate. *"Left-hand escorting the Primordial Lord of the Left Wu Ying"* shares the same meaning as the middle scroll’s *"primordial qi of the Mysterious Center."* *"Great Primordial Cavern-Spirit Numinous"* shares meaning with *"Three Primordial Floral Qi."* *"Three Elders’ Primordial Han Zhang"* shares meaning with *"Three Primordials giving birth to the mud pill."* *Su* means emptiness and purity—all are the true qi of the three fields. The nine primordials differ from the three primordials. The purple primordial, white primordial, and yellow primordial are the qi of the Three Ren Lords, corresponding to the human liver, lungs, and spleen—the coagulation of the green, yellow, and white three qi.

The qi emerges within the radiant scene. These nine primordials emerge from the realm of luminous splendor, likening the qi first transmitted from the parents’ essence and blood. *Jing* (scene) means color and image—the first formation of the embryo, when spirit and essence complete the body, resplendent and flashing.

The *Dharma Enclosure* dances the immortal banner. *Fayuan* is also called *Fatan* (an error), referring to the three enclosures of *Ziwei*, *Taiwei*, and *Tianshi*. It is also called the *enclosure wall* or *city*—the jade city behind the brain. For cultivators, it is the path of silent audience, also the name of the Great One within the Dipper. *Dancing the immortal banner* means using banners and pennants to summon the hun and ling spirits. This chapter focuses on cultivating the root of intention, thus generating wisdom—sincerity of intention precedes the extension of knowledge. The lower scroll’s *"Dharma Enclosure rises in Crimson Empyrean"* shares this meaning. The Great One within the Dipper is the spirit that summons the true and induces the numinous. When one attains it, true spirits descend and divine qi spreads.

Swiftly circling the five venerable elders. *Juanxun* means swiftness—urging the five elders to each spread their true qi and receive the hun and po. The five elders are: *Jade Clarity’s Vast Ultimate Primordial Elder*, *Empty Sovereign’s Numinous Light Origin Elder*, *Mysterious Floral Treasure Heaven True Elder*, *Dewy Vast Numinous Ancestral Elder*, and *Verdant Luxuriant Vast Capital Immortal Elder*—the distinguished guests of the prior five elders, the ancestral qi of the five phases within the Great Ultimate.

When one receives the five qi, only then can form be completed; when the elixir obtains these five qi, only then can the Great Return of Golden Liquor be achieved. As the scripture states: "Heaven and earth receive them to divide and judge; sun and moon receive them to circulate and move."

The Lady Initiate-Pearl—*Hui Feng Hun He Shang Zhen Sheng Mu Zhong Hou Yuan Jun Wang Fu Ren Ming Qi Zhu*—is also called the Lady of the Mud-Pill Palace. The *Yellow Court Scripture* says: "The Lady of the Mud-Pill Palace stands at the center," for she is the spirit of the Feminine One. Some may doubt how the heavens could bear a lady’s name, yet they do not realize that heaven and the human realm are in truth one. In former times, the daughter of Wei Shu, Left Attendant of the Masters of Writing under Emperor Wu of Jin, was named Hua Cun, styled Xian’an. From childhood, she delighted in reading the *Zhuangzi*, *Laozi*, the *Three Commentaries on the Spring and Autumn Annals*, the *Five Classics*, and the *Hundred Masters*. At twenty-four, her parents compelled her to marry, and she was wed to Liu Yi, styled Youyan, a subordinate of the Grand Protector. Though she conducted herself with propriety, the times left her no choice, and she became Liu’s wife. Once her children had grown and Liu’s lineage was secured, she sought to live apart. At the time, Yi served as Magistrate of Xiuwu, and the Lady thereupon cultivated the Way of the Great Cavern’s Imperial One. One night, amidst celestial music, she beheld banners descending from the sky to her chamber, where four perfected ones took their seats: the True Person An Duming of the Great Ultimate, the Great Divinity Fangzhu of the Eastern Flower, the Divine Lord Qingxu of Fusang’s Yang Valley, and Wang Zideng, the Heavenly King of Lesser Existence. The Lady bowed and sought their instruction. After receiving the Dao, she feigned illness and achieved liberation through the corpse, some witnessing the Primordial Sovereign of the Great One arrive in a whirlwind carriage to welcome her. This occurred in the fourth year of Xianhe under the Eastern Jin. She was enfeoffed as the Primordial Lady of Purple Emptiness, overseeing the Southern Office of Life, and later elevated to Lady of the Southern Marchmount, her rank equal to that of an Immortal Duke. She is the ancestral master of the Great Cavern of Supreme Clarity.

Thus we know that the heavens also bear the title of "Lady," a rank equivalent to the third grade, held by female immortals.

**Holding the register, she retreats to the Purple Chamber.**
The Lady takes the register into the Purple Chamber, located behind the brain—also called the Purple Portal—where she presents it to the Jade Emperor, declaring that she has summoned the hun and po and thus achieved transformation. The scriptures often mention the Purple Chamber, or sometimes the Yellow Chamber, referring to the Central Yellow Court.

**The Primordial Father revolves leftward in luminous clarity.**
The Primordial Father of the Upper Mystery is the spirit of intent, governing the Four Symbols. As noted in the fourth chapter of the upper scroll, the scriptures on practice state that the mind should move like a monkey, never resting for even a moment. If one wishes to subdue it, one must recite the Great Vehicle. The ancients said: "Gathering the mind in one place is the bodhimanda of the Way; scattering intent for even an instant casts one into the realm of sentient beings." Intent is the chief of the four spirits among the five viscera, the central ground of upper, lower, and middle equilibrium. If one can day and night observe, examine, and rouse it, preventing its dull accumulation, maintaining constant clarity, then after a hundred days, one will naturally attain numinous communion.

**Merging with the Lad of the Grand Tenuity.**
When the spirit of intent merges water and fire, the Lad of the Grand Tenuity spreads qi and descends the divine to generate our body—this is the spirit that initiates the coagulation of the embryo. In the elixir, when lead first arises, one must gather it with proper method to refine the Golden Liquor Returning Elixir.

**Penetrating wisdom of the Cavernous Clarity.**
The *Scripture of Salvation* speaks of "cavernous wisdom penetrating clarity," while the *Scripture of Spirit Generation* says: "reveling in cavernous wisdom." This refers to the seven awakenings of our wisdom, thoroughly luminous and clear. As it is said: "When things are fathomed, knowledge is attained; with knowledge comes wisdom and prajñā."

**The great intent shines, primordial and unobstructed.**
One version omits "wisdom shines," while another asks: "How could one obtain?" Intent is will, governed by the spleen and issued by the heart. Thus, when the heart is rectified, intent becomes sincere—this is what is meant by "sincere and true intent," without self-deception. The *Avataṃsaka Sūtra* states: "If one wishes to know the Buddha’s realm, one must purify one’s intent like empty space." *Mencius* says: "Will is the master of qi." In the Dao of the elixir, it serves as the Yellow Dame, for it can mediate and unite the qi of the five viscera, gathering them into one. Between metal and wood, without a mediator, nothing can be accomplished. The maiden in blue and the youth in white silk must have their monkey and horse subdued, whereupon the tortoise and serpent will unite.

When the great intent is once attained, it becomes thoroughly unobstructed, luminous and pure, traversing past and future kalpas without hindrance, knowing and seeing all. In the Dao, this is the Ten Penetrations; in Buddhism, the Six Penetrations; among the spirits and ghosts of the middle realm, the Five Penetrations—all inseparable from the Middle Way. In all matters, attaining the mean enables one to be universally perceptive.

**The roots and dusts are all extinguished.**
The six roots are the eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and intent; the six dusts are form, sound, scent, flavor, touch, and dharmas. All illusory delusions instantly dissipate, for with sincere intent, there is no principle of false movement. No person is perfect, yet if even one root awakens, through mutual cultivation and realization, one can extinguish the six cavernous demon-kings and their calamitous thieves, thereby attaining purity of the six roots, harmony of the six palaces, and freedom from the constraints of the six qi. Thus, one with all six desires is a common mortal; one without any is a true immortal. The *Scripture of Salvation* speaks of the coarse dusts first purified, the fine dusts not yet purified—hence one cannot escape the three realms.

**Existence and nonexistence both become empty space.**
The dual views of existence and nonexistence both return to emptiness and quiescence. This is to practice the Way of the Mean, like hating foul odors or loving beautiful forms—this is called self-contentment. The ancient worthies said: "When empty space is pulverized, the complete truth is revealed."

**Wondrous practice fulfills the Ten Perfections.**
When the three thousand wondrous practices of the Great Cavern are perfected, the Way of the Ten Perfections is fulfilled. Unceasing, it endures; enduring, it corrects, ultimately accomplishing both self and others—all emerging from this Way. The *Great Cavern Scripture* regards the cultivation of wondrous practice as supreme. Its concluding verses state: "The Six Pāramitās and Ten Penetrations, with myriad practices perfected." But what are the Six Pāramitās?

The six chapters of the lower scroll provide explanations, and due to their greater length compared to the middle scroll, annotations are appended here. The ninth chapter of the upper scroll, *Mysterious Accord*, states: "Those who have ascended through the six stages have first cultivated the Ten Faiths of the initial mind, then aroused the Ten Goodnesses, next blossomed the Ten Flowers, then perfected the Ten Powers, gradually verified the Ten Immortals, and ultimately attained the Ten Perfections.

1. The Ten Faiths of the initial mind: Awakening the mind of faith, aligning with the mechanism of shared faith, thoughts unwavering in faith, acting through faith, the Five Faiths residing within, inscribing faith in metal and stone, perfecting great faith, good faith enduring to the end, steadfast faith advancing forward—only then is it called true faith.

2. Next, arousing the Ten Goodnesses: The second chapter of the upper scroll states, 'The Ten Goodnesses arise within the mysterious.' Hearing goodness, the Mysterious ascends to the forehead, the Six Dīng radiate luminous light; seeing goodness, the Cinnabar Origin forms square pupils, the Eight Historians illuminate clarity; speaking goodness, life is communicated and the mouth rinsed, the Five Scripts and Kingly Flowers bloom; treading goodness, strength is harnessed and earthly barriers traverse life; contemplating goodness and practicing goodness, utmost goodness knows no transgression; abiding in goodness and preserving peace, settled goodness establishes the foundation. Perfecting the Ten Goodnesses requires but the ten characters of 'goodness.'

3. Blossoming the Ten Flowers: Derived from the seventh chapter of the lower scroll, *The Ten Flowers Observation Gate of Mysterious Accord*. According to the scripture of the upper scroll: 'The Ten Flowers are the wondrous practices of immortals; the Ten Penetrations arise therefrom.' These are the numbers of the *River Chart*. The Five Phases complete generation, the Eight Trigrams array themselves—all heaven, earth, beings, and things are examined thereby to come into being. Once born, they again know and cultivate, esteeming the shedding of the Five Phases' husk and departing from the Eight Trigrams' mechanism, thereby verifying and ascending to wondrous practice, as noted below the title.

4. Next, perfecting the Ten Powers: The eighth chapter of the lower scroll, *Mysterious Accord*, and the sixth scripture of the upper scroll state: 'The Ten Powers first perfect the mechanism.' The eighth scripture of the lower scroll states: 'The Ten Powers proclaim the true script.' Employing power to harmonize with the body, advancing power on level ground, perfecting power in vastness, wisdom-power inwardly purifying, kindness-power emitting light, luminous power blooming in fullness, numinous power universally responding, mysterious power in the Great Square, great power in spontaneity, universal power aiding and embracing.

5. Gradually verifying the Ten Immortals: From the ninth chapter of the lower scroll, *Mysterious Accord*—Womb Immortal, Womb-Enveloped Immortal, Ethereal-Soul Immortal, Corporeal-Soul Immortal, Numinous Immortal, Original Immortal, Flower Immortal, Mountain Immortal, Visceral Immortal, Original-Life Spirit Immortal.

6. Ultimately attaining the Ten Perfections: From the tenth chapter of the lower alley, *Mysterious Accord*. The ninth chapter of the upper scroll states: 'The Ten Perfections ascend to the Purple Chamber.' The tenth chapter of the middle scroll states: 'Wondrous practice fulfills the Ten Perfections.' The tenth chapter of the lower scroll states: 'Wondrous practice ascends to the Ten Perfections.' The eleventh chapter of the lower alley states: 'The Ten Perfections fulfill wondrous practice.' Essence-perfection in the Mysterious Pearl, qi-perfection in Mysterious Power, spirit-perfection in Mysterious Penetration, nature-perfection in Mysterious Unity, origin-perfection in Mysterious Wonder, life-perfection in Mysterious Radiance, form-perfection in Mysterious Wholeness, virtue-perfection in Mysterious Cavern, Dao-perfection in Mysterious Response, command-perfection in the Great Mystery—these six are called the Six Pāramitās and Ten Penetrations. Having ascended through the six stages, wondrous practice is fully accomplished.

This is called the Great Mind’s Spiritual Penetration. The spirit within the mind, when moved, achieves penetration; penetration enables transformation, transformation enables endurance. When the spirit endures, the creations of heaven and earth become manifest before one. All worldly affairs arise from the mind. When the mind’s spirit is penetrated, it does not turn with external things. Sincerity of intent precedes rectitude of mind, leading to universal peace, national stability, and the people’s prosperity. How great is this name! There has never been one who, without cultivating the self, gained early renown throughout the world. The *Book of Songs* says: 'There, they bear no ill; here, they are not detested. Day and night, they strive to perpetuate their glorious reputation as immortals.'

Tradition records: In former times, Liu Yuanqing of Wuchang studied under Master Wang Zongdao, transmitting the registers of the Three Caverns. He constantly practiced the Dao of Returning Wind and Uniting Harmonies, abstained from grains to refine qi, yet drank over a *dou* of wine. At the beginning of the Baoli era, Emperor Jingzong sought Daoist adepts, and the military supervisor Lü Lingcong summoned him. Yuanqing said: 'I have a mountain wife and a concubine west of the pond, for whom beef is life. If I am taken as a master of arts, I fear the general may incur the charge of deceiving the throne.' Thereupon, he requested a pig’s shoulder, sliced it himself, and ate it with garlic sauce. Lü, suspicious, dismissed him. Unable to refuse, he journeyed to the capital and was summoned to the Hall of Administrative Governance, where he was questioned on matters of immortality. His answers were deemed unsatisfactory, and he was sent away. In the third year of Huichang, he was summoned again and responded to the emperor’s satisfaction. Emperor Jingzong bestowed upon him the registers of the Dao, appointing him Grand Master for Closing Court with Silver and Cyan, Chancellor of the Academy of Mysteries, and granted him the title Master of Vast Accomplishment. In the fifth year of Dazhong, in the tenth month, clouds, cranes, and celestial music filled the skies above Luofu. He then underwent liberation by means of the corpse, leaving behind only his staff and sandals. Is this not verification of the Great Mind’s Spiritual Penetration? If one is unwilling to act, those who do act achieve the same.

The Dao is complete, ascending to the Jade Clarity. Wisdom, benevolence, and courage—these three are the universal virtues of the world. Knowing these three, one knows how to cultivate the self. Those born with knowledge, those who practice with ease, and those who achieve success—all are one. The *Cavern Scripture* here may be said to have entered the realm of sages and worthies. Virtue and the Dao are perfectly fulfilled and complete, ascending to the sacred realm of the Upper Jade Clarity. Cultivating to this point, one may release the yang spirit from the Mud Pill Palace.

Some say: 'If the dwelling is ruined...' Confucius said: 'In the morning, hear the Dao; in the evening, die content.' The Upper Realm of Jade Clarity is the Gate of Myriad Wonders within the Mud Pill Palace of humans. Rebirth and union are all entered and exited thereby; human death also departs through it.

The rank of Sage Immortal Duke. The immortal ranks and sacred positions should be called Immortal Duke. Previously, there were the Five Elderly Ones, so it should not redundantly be called 'Duke.' The tenth chapter of the middle scroll takes the eyes, ears, nose, tongue, body, and intent, along with fluids, hands, feet, essence, blood, nature, and life as primary. Thereby, the Four Great Elements—earth, water, fire, and wind—provisionally unite to form this illusory body. One should rely on this illusory body to cultivate and verify the true vehicle, lest the six senses be lured by private human desires, thereby falling into the demonic palaces of the Six Caverns. The body soars beyond the Six Directions, attaining the fruit of Jade Clarity Immortal Duke."

The Buddha explained: "When the Tathāgata speaks of all marks, their fullness is not true fullness—this is called the fullness of all marks. When the Tathāgata speaks of a self, there is no true self, yet ordinary beings take it to be real. Generally, one should not cling to the illusory as the actual, thereby transcending the mundane form and attaining verification of Suchness."

In former times, Master Nie of the Dao, styled Zongwei, was naturally perceptive from birth and served his parents with filial piety. He received the *Great Cavern Scripture* and deeply penetrated its essentials. He encountered the two Perfected Ones, Peng and Cai, and later met the Perfected One Xie Xiutong, who said to him: "Peng and Cai and I have concealed ourselves here for two hundred years. Recently, the Lord of Eastern Florescence commanded us to oversee the Earth Immortals of Jade Bamboo Mountain and the Pavilion of Pure Emptiness. You and I share a predestined affinity with the Dao, so I have come to inform you. You should cultivate diligently, for you are destined for the rank of Immortal Duke." Suddenly, they vanished. Master Nie soon after ascended as a feathered transcendent—was this not verification of the Immortal Duke?

In the Great Yuan dynasty, Gui of Pengzhou Guard in Peng Prefecture practiced the Dao of harmonious union. He constantly recited the *Great Cavern* and *Numinous Treasure* scriptures, and the *Book of Changes* never left his hands. He wandered Peng Mountain and dwelled on Jade Bamboo Mountain, sometimes sitting on a boulder for days. Once, a tiger circled near him, yet he paid it no mind, and the tiger remained at ease.

Another day, as if in a dream, he entered a vast cavern extending several *li* deep. In a luminous space, he saw palaces and was told by someone: "This is no place for you. Depart swiftly." He then ascended the mountain, where pines and bamboos swayed gracefully, deer cried and cranes called. Another voice said: "The time has not yet come. Return for now, and you will be summoned again later." Thereafter, his conduct was extraordinary. On the twenty-eighth day of the fifth month in the *jiawu* year of the Zhiyuan era, at dusk, he heard a voice call: "The Emperor commands your presence. Come swiftly!" He rose abruptly and set out, vanishing midway—was this not his ascent to Jade Clarity and verification as Immortal Duke?

The above jade script of celestial seal, eighty characters in all, governs above the Supreme Jade Heaven of Great Brilliance and rules below the Fourth Rampart, Lord Wang of Virtue.

The *Mysterious Accord* states: "The Perfected One, with profound wisdom of Cavern Clarity, fully comprehends the primordial unity. Root and dust are severed, worldly dharmas extinguished, and the dual burdens of existence and non-existence are utterly stilled. Through the wondrous practice of preserving the True, one attains the great mind and divine penetrations, capable of severing the demonic registers of Fengdu Mountain’s Mingchen Naifan, the evil roots of the Celestial Palace of Wucheng, and the ghostly ledgers of the Earth’s roots. Constantly offering dharma wealth to the Celestial Venerable of Primordial Beginning and bestowing it upon all, one universally fulfills all needs, becoming a Great Wealth King and perfectly advancing to the rank of Flying Immortal in the ten directions.

The Flying Immortal soars through the void, rides clouds and cranes, dwells upon the pillars of flowery banners, rises at dawn in Fusang, and rests at dusk in Xianchi—such as Ding Lingwei and Xu Zizhen.

*Jade Clarity, Boundless, and Supreme Perfected Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture of the Dao*, Scroll Six
● "Head" (*shou*)—likely a misprint for "Azure" (*qing*).
● [Square]—this character is illegible in the original text.

*Jade Clarity, Boundless, and Supreme Perfected Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture of the Dao*, Scroll Seven
Annotated by Zhongyangzi Wei Qi of Penglai Mountain in Eastern Shu.

The Primordial Heavenly King of the Origin spoke: "The seventeenth jade chapter of the *Great Cavern Scripture of Wenchang* states: 'The hands and feet are pervaded by numinous power; the strength of hands and feet is universally penetrating.'

*Dingwei*, *Wu Shen*, *Jing*, and *Ge*.

Within the imperial purple qi of the Primordial Beginning—or as some say, 'humans possess six roots; how then do they also have hands, feet, and the like?'—they know not that when emotions and desires arise, all become root-dust, which is what the Buddhists call the five aggregates, six sense-bases, and twelve sense-fields. The strength of hands and feet lies in the cultivation of qi. When spirit and qi are fully harmonized, one delights in the five destinies, unaware of the hands dancing and the feet leaping.

The Primordial Purple Void Lady of the Imperial Beginning resides within the purple qi—also called the Purple Portal—behind the gate of Jade Capital Mountain. Some mistake 'purple qi' for 'purple origin' due to their similar graphs, leading to transmission errors. The Twelve Bodhisattvas of the human realm say: 'The dung-carrier bears his load with strength.' The strength of the hands denotes courage, vigor, and unyielding progress, unwavering in the face of great adversity. This is what the tradition calls 'choosing the good and firmly holding to it,' and what the Two Teachings call 'steadfast adherence and resolute guardianship'—not the mere act of grasping with the hands. The strength of the feet lies in truly treading and practicing the path.

Radiant light illumines the layered heavens.

Its brilliance shines resplendent above the ninefold heavens. When one’s hands grasp and feet walk, all accords with the correct principle. Thus, purple qi arises in the brain, illuminating it. The character *xiao* (霄) has nine forms: the celestial spirits roam the Golden Heaven; harmonious tones resound beyond the Nine Heavens; the Perfected shines upon the Nine Heavens; the Jade Emperor rides the Vermilion Heaven; the Dharma Enclosure flourishes in the Vermilion Heaven; riding the light, one ascends the Supreme Heaven; the Three Flowers ascend the Heavenly Court; radiant light illumines the layered heavens; and the returning heavens hover over the boundless desert. Though there are nine heavens, their meanings differ. They are not merely heavens but also bear names such as crowns, pendants, chariots, and canopies, each named according to what one perceives.

The Three Heavens illumine the Nine Luminaries.

The Three Qi generate the Nine Qi, forming the Three Treasures and Nine Heavens—all realms of the pure and luminous Dao of the Great Yang. The radiance of the luminaries shines resplendently in the everlasting, undarkened heavens. The head, hands, and feet are named the Three Passes, guarding the nine orifices. One must strive for clarity, brightness, and radiance.

Separation and union give rise to the myriad beings.

Is not Qian and Kun the gate of the *Changes*? Separation and union are opening and closing. The *Book of Changes* states: 'Opening the gate is Qian; closing the gate is Kun.' When Qian and Kun transform and interpenetrate, there arises the principle of ceaseless generation. The Dao’s qi separates and then reunites.

Wearing a vermilion kerchief and a robe of green aurora,

This describes the Primordial Purple Void Lady of the Imperial Beginning: her head wrapped in a crimson kerchief, her body clad in a robe of green aurora. In the third scroll above, it is written: 'The green aurora illumines the golden ramparts'—some say 'Six Auroras,' an error arising from phonetic similarity.

Above, she turns the numinous power of the Cold Youth.

The Cold Youth is the Azure Lad, the domain of the Eastern Green Dragon. The Primordial Purple Void Lady of the Imperial Beginning, fearing stagnation and complacency that would prevent the nurturing of the myriad beings, returns his numinous power to them, allowing each to find its proper place.

Uprooting the five poisons of suffering,

Uprooting the bitterness and toxins of the three evil destinies and five sufferings. The previous passage spoke of 'uprooting the realm of five sufferings'; here it is called 'poisons,' for within the realm of five sufferings, there are yet the five poisons: the qi of the fire cart, freezing ice, severe cold, scorching heat, and acrid bitterness.

Transcending form to surpass the Beginning Azure.

The eight Brahma heavens and nine heavens: the Eastern Beginning Azure Heaven and the Great Azure Heaven. This speaks of one transcending form and spirit, surpassing the Beginning Azure Heaven to reach the Desire Realm, Form Realm, and Formless Realm, then the Four Brahma Heavens of the Seed People, the Nine Heavens of Divine Aurora, and the Supreme Three Heavens. When one meticulously enumerates each heaven, the distances span tens of thousands of miles. Truly, one cannot ascend by steps. Yet the adept, through penetrating understanding, may traverse without crossing barriers or treading shores. In the span of a single thought, one may directly reach beyond the summit.

White Simplicity initiates the towering Xiao,

White Simplicity, the Right Primordial Lady named Initiator of Light, and Xiao Ren, the White Primordial Honored Deity, open the towering Xiao Terrace. Previously, it was called 'Purple Simplicity and Non-Ultimate'—here named the Three Simplicities and Three Peaks, the names of three deities. Some say 'Yellow Simplicity,' which is grossly mistaken.

The Golden Gate is guarded by vermilion soldiers.

The Western Seven Treasures Golden Gate is heavily fortified, its defenses manned by vermilion soldiers. This metaphorically describes the true fire refining true gold, whereby the elixir path is accomplished. Here, it speaks of the White Simplicity Right Primordial Lady stationed above the Golden Gate, its defenses stern and unyielding.

The seven ancestors accumulate corpse-knots,

In the Western Seven Qi Heaven, corpse-knots congeal as yin coagulates. Thus, the spirits of the seven ancestors intertwine, their corporeal roots and impure qi accumulating, unable to disperse until the cyclical movement of the Dao’s qi flows through them.

One transformation topples a hundred evils.

With true fire, one transforms the myriad layers of gold ore, dissolving yin with yang. Through the Dao’s qi, the corpse-knots of the seven ancestors are untied, causing a hundred evils to dissipate at once. Ancestral ties across kalpas are simultaneously reborn.

Receiving blessings in the Eastern Aurora Chamber,

The Eastern Aurora Chamber, also called the Azure Flower Chamber of Everlasting Joy, is where the Great Yang emerges. Benevolent transformation flourishes, and all beings find their proper place—hence 'receiving blessings.' Previously, it was called 'transcending blessings,' akin to Sudhana receiving prophecy in the City of Blessings. The East signifies life.

Returning to the womb of the Vermilion Fire Court.

Though one receives blessings in the Eastern Aurora, one must first proceed to the Southern Cinnabar Vermilion Fire Mansion to refine the body with golden liquid. Only then may one dwell there. The teachings of the Hidden School state: 'Divine immortals and human adepts who do not cross the Southern Palace cannot ascend and transform.' This refers to Mount Heng in the Southern Marchmount.

The numinous and pure practice of the Cavern Spirit—

When one realizes the numinous and pure Dao of the Cavern Spirit, one’s merit and practice become complete. The wondrous practice of the numinous and pure Cavern Spirit demands diligence, free from all attachments. If one clings, the power will not flow.

Power flows freely, naturally illuminating and penetrating.

When one attains the power of qi, it flows freely, thus becoming penetrating, enlightened, resolute, and strong. This is no ordinary power but the power by which the cosmos rests in the hand and the myriad transformations arise from the body—the power of wisdom, benevolence, and courage, which one must cultivate."

The Perfected One’s hands grasp the Dipper,
Pure and utterly true—able to clasp and draw the pivot of the Dipper.
This is not the strength to embrace mountains and leap seas or to lift hooks and shoulder tripods,
but rather the Dao by which one becomes the thief of Heaven and Earth,
stealing qi to offer to oneself, thus attaining great might and vast numinous penetration.

The feet tread upon the Nine Prime Stars.
The two feet may tread upon the Nine Prime Stars of the Northern Dipper.
The Dipper itself has seven stars, with two auxiliary stars, hence called the Nine Primes.
The scriptures say: "The feet tread the Northern Dipper, straddling the *kuigang*."
All lies in the mind’s contemplation, not in literal treading with the feet.

Wielding and grasping the gates of Heaven and Earth,
With qi-power flowing freely, one thus takes hold and bears the gates of Heaven and Earth.
The Celestial Gate and Earthly Axis are the pivot of the Dipper.
Day and night, the jade armillary and balance align the Seven Governors.
The Earth’s axis, three hundred and sixty in number, rotates in succession to turn the Wind Wheel,
driving the square earth.
Of old, Gonggong contended for the world and, in fury, struck his head against Mount Buzhou,
breaking the Earth’s axis—this is the meaning.
Here, "Celestial Gate" is spoken of, not "Earthly Axis," for it is a general term.

The *Yellow Emperor’s Basic Questions: On Heavenly Truth* states:
"The ancient Perfected Ones lifted and carried Heaven and Earth,
grasped and held yin and yang,
stood alone in guarding the spirit,
thus their longevity obscured Heaven and Earth."
This is of the same meaning.

This chapter speaks of the free flow of qi-power.
For power lies in nurturing qi:
when qi is full, power is full;
when qi wanes, power wanes.
Thus, one must value qi and secure its root,
only then can strength be attained,
enabling one to wield and grasp the gates and axes of Heaven and Earth.
The human gate lies in the two qi of yin and yang.

The root of spirit, life, and essence—
Essence is the root of spirit,
qi is the function of spirit,
and form is the dwelling of spirit.
If spirit is overused, it exhausts;
if essence is overly stirred, it depletes;
if qi is overworked, it severs.
Thus, the arising of form depends on spirit,
and spirit’s abiding depends on qi.
When essence is exhausted, qi dissipates;
when qi dissipates, spirit departs;
when spirit departs, form dies.

Compare it to a candle:
when the candle is spent, the flame cannot remain.
Or to a dike:
when the dike breaks, the water cannot stay.
Thus, essence and spirit are the vital connections to life’s pulse—
how can one not be cautious?
