What humans must deeply cherish.

This chapter takes the free flow of power as the wondrous practice.
This power is not the strength of hands or feet,
but the Five Powers and Ten Powers of the Buddha’s teachings:
The Five Powers—faith, mindfulness, diligence, concentration, and wisdom.
The Ten Powers:
1. The power to rightly know what is and is not possible,
2. The power to know the karmic retribution of the three times,
3. The power to know the various meditations, liberations, and samādhis,
4. The power to know the superior and inferior faculties of beings,
5. The power to know the various desires of beings,
6. The power to know the various natures of the world,
7. The power to know all paths to their ends,
8. The power of past-life knowledge,
9. The power of the divine eye to see all,
10. The power of the knowledge of the exhaustion of outflows.
Together, they form the Fifteen Powers,
all recorded in the Buddhist canon—this cannot be denied.

The above Jade Chapter of Celestial Seal, one hundred characters in all,
above governs the Primordial Pillar of the Heavenly Ascension,
below commands the Fifth Mound of the Golden Millet Marshland Earthly Sovereign.

The *Mysterious Contract* states:
"When the Perfected One attains the numinous and pure Dao of the Cavern Spirit,
with hands and feet freely flowing in power,
grasping, wielding, flying, and treading,
coming and going with effortless mastery,
one can sever the evil roots of the Nine Dark Hells,
the earthly roots, demonic registers, and ghostly ledgers.
Ever offering the numinous tea, yellow sprouts, and golden stamens to the Primordial Heavenly King,
circling the Nine Radiant Steps,
one ascends to become a Heavenly Immortal."

The Heavenly Immortal cultivates the inner and outer Golden Elixir,
with merit and practice complete,
soaring through the thirty-six heavens,
surveying the wondrous realms of the celestial palaces,
abiding in bliss and freedom—
such as the Perfected Ones Zhong and Lü.

The Primordial Heavenly King says:
"The Eighteenth Jade Chapter of the Great Cavern of Wenchang—
the Cavern Mystery of Nature and Life, the Numinous Penetration of Primordial Destiny."

*Jiyou, Gengxu, Tripod, Thunder.*
The Central Yellow Primordial Qi—
This scripture establishes the Three Powers following the principles of nature and life.
Thus, the Dao of the Three Ultimates each has its governance.
If one can exhaust principle, fulfill nature, and reach destiny,
then one returns to the Great Dao.

Thus, when the heart arises, nature is extinguished;
when the heart is quiescent, nature appears.
This is called "completing nature and preserving it,"
the gateway of the Way and its meaning.

Yellow Primordial—this is the name of the Yellow Elder Lord.
This chapter speaks of the central intent of nature and life.
Thus, the spleen governs the central earth of *wu* and *ji*,
its color is yellow,
and its qi is also yellow.
The *Scripture of Salvation* states:
"The Yellow Emperor, Central Lord,
whom the myriad spirits cannot surpass,
regulates the five qi,
harmonizing the hundred spirits."
It also says:
"The Yellow Center governs qi,
commanding the Primordial Lords."
Thus, the root of human nature and life lies in the spleen and stomach,
which transform the granary of grains,
nourishing the Four Numinous Ones.
Then nature and life can be long preserved.
In the Dao of the Elixir, this is called:
Earthly Soul, Elixir Mother, Knife Point, Yellow Sprout,
Yellow Flower, Yellow Lad, Yellow Ox, Yellow Court,
Granary, True Earth, Yellow Matron, Earthen Cauldron,
Eight-Trigram Furnace, and the like.
Thus, the Five Prisons—all pertain to earth.

Of old, Xiang Ziwen,
during the Baoli era, served as an official in Hengzhou.
He met Gong Changqing, who said:
"My master, Sima Yinyuan, is a celestial officer of the Weiyu Cavern Heaven.
Human merits and transgressions are all recorded in the Five Marchmounts’ Cavern Heavens
and reported to the Envoys of the Nine Heavens.
My master transmitted to me the Dao of the Central Yellow Great Unity’s silent audience with the Supreme Emperor.
Now I cultivate it."
Ziwen announced his wish to follow and journey south,
but Changqing dissuaded him, saying it was not possible.
Yet, he departed in a flutter.
Thus, it is known that cultivating the Central Yellow Qi
can lead to the Dao of immortality.
This speaks of the Cavern Chapter governed by the Central Primordial Lord of the Round Flower and Yellow Perfection.

Round Flower, also called Yellow Flower,
is the stomach cavity,
also named Jade Longevity Spirit,
the deity presiding over the transformation of the granary of grains.
If one can transform the granary of grains,
then qi becomes harmonious and life endures.
Longevity or premature death—both depend on cultivation and accumulation.

The Supreme Zhang Shang’s Jade Gate,
"Supreme Zhang Shang" is the name of the Yellow Plain Elder Lord.
The Jade Gate is the Jade Emperor’s Palace within the human brain,
where the myriad spirits of the body pay homage,
where the myriad qi gather and converge—
also called the Heavenly Numen, or the Heavenly Valley.

Hidden clouds soar three *ren* high.
Those who exhaust their hearts know their natures;
knowing their natures, they know Heaven.
The "three *ren*" refer to the vast Great Luo Heaven above the Three Realms.
Thus, those who cultivate both nature and life ascend beyond these Three Realms,
and when the Five Clouds are subdued at the tips of the Three Passes,
radiant light shines forth.

The "three *ren*" also denote the clouds of three colors—azure, yellow, and white—
for the Left Primordial Lord of the Purple Plain, Yiyu Ren, is styled "Anlai Shang";
the Central Primordial Lord of the Yellow Plain, Round Flower Yellow Ren, is styled "Supreme Zhang Shang";
and the Right Primordial Lord of the White Plain, Qiming Xiaohe, is styled "Golden Gate"—
these are the Three *Ren*.

The Crimson Radiance veils the boundless,
the Crimson Radiance is the sun, the boundless is yin.
As the moon receives the sun’s light, so is it called the moon.
The incantation says: "Fragrant and veiled in the boundless."
The Sun’s Central Consort is named "Yang within Yin,"
like the Chamber, the Sun, and the Hare—
the hare’s four legs are even, belonging to yin,
while the sun belongs to yang, hence "Yang within Yin."
The moon’s crow has three legs, odd and belonging to yang,
while the moon belongs to yin, hence "Yin within Yang."
They mutually borrow each other’s principles in naming.
This speaks of the Consort within the sun,
just as within the human yang spirit there is a feminine aspect—
yin within yang, yang within yin,
exchanging and intermingling to form the flourishing of culture.

Uphold the Perfected of the Great One.
Constantly uphold the Perfected of the Great One,
for the Great One is transformed from the primordial qi of water,
ever dwelling above the human head,
dispersing true qi to form a canopy of purple clouds,
shading and covering the body’s form.
"Uphold" means to remain ever vigilant and awake.

The Emperor’s Daughter embraces the Stable Mound,
the Mud Pill, the Feminine One, the Emperor’s Daughter—
also called the Central Maiden of the Dipper—
constantly embraces the true yang essence-spirit,
named the Stable Mound.
Reciting the jade scriptures and cloud chapters of the *Great Cavern Immortal Canon*
draws down the true qi flowing from the heavens to give life to the human path.

Chant the *Jade Purity Canon*.
Reciting the jade scriptures and cloud chapters of the *Great Cavern Immortal Canon*,
as Sima chanted the *Cavern Chapters* to give life to humanity,
there is the Holy Mother of the Chamber, the Great Spirit overseeing birth,
with heavenly and earthly deities joining in the chant of jade tones
to supervise the affairs of procreation.

Jade talismans are woven into the Purple Chamber,
the Purple Chamber is in the Heaven within Heaven,
the place where talismanic charts are kept and administered.
As mentioned in the previous section,
this refers to the White Prime Lord, the Venerable Deity of No-Blossom,
who holds talismans and registers, presenting them before the Emperor—
all embodying the same principle, the principle of giving life to humanity.

The Five Registers mark the Round Court.
The talismanic registers of the Five Directions record the names of those who attain immortality.
The Round Court, also called the Heavenly Court Palace,
lies one *cun* above the Bright Hall within the brain,
where the myriad spirits gather.
It governs the soul and spirit to give life to the human path,
and so too does it lead to the attainment of immortality.

The Seven Ancestors return as embryonic immortals,
the Seven Ancestors all return to the womb to be reborn as immortals.
When a person is born, the myriad heavens celebrate,
the ten thousand emperors prepare rites—
only then is one born, for birth is not to be taken lightly.
Yet humans demean themselves, failing to cherish and preserve their lives.

Cut off the Three Paths’ corpses.
The *Scripture of Salvation* eternally delivers beings from the Three Paths, the Five Sufferings, and the Eight Difficulties,
together severing and extinguishing the filth of the Three Paths and Five Sufferings.
The corpses are the Three Corpses—Peng Qiao, Peng Ju, and Peng Zhi—
dwelling within the human body,
constantly reporting sins to the Three Offices.
The Three Corpses reside in the Three Fields of the human body,
each corpse governing three worms, totaling nine worms,
which in turn govern the myriad worms,
gnawing at the body.
As the *Nirvana Sutra* records, each worm has a name,
though the list is too extensive to include here.
Within the eighty-four thousand yang pathways of the human body,
each pore gives birth to a worm.
When a person dies, these worms all fly away,
escaping to distant places and attaching to other things.

The flowing wind severs blood stagnation,
the flowing wind is the mysterious qi,
circulating throughout the body,
thus severing the stagnation of corpse-blood.
When corpse-blood congeals and stagnates,
only by obtaining true qi can it be circulated and dispersed,
preventing coagulation and blockage,
thus enabling the spontaneous transformations of life.

The mysterious work attains the Yellow Tranquility.
The mysterious work of nature and life resides in the Yellow Tranquility,
the name of the spirit of essence and blood.
The Three Births are styled "Yellow Tranquility,"
which is the central spleen-earth.
Earth receives the complete number of Heaven and Earth,
hence the principle of generation and completion ultimately depends on it.

The Cavern Mystery shines with pure light,
when the spleen and stomach are properly regulated,
naturally there is pure and radiant light.
Below, it says that nature and life are the primordial spirit.
The ancients said:
"Constantly call and awaken the master within,
remain vigilant and do not be deceived by others."
One should respond and awaken to this.

The primordial life achieves numinous communion.
The *Scripture of Spirit Generation* says:
"The primordial womb binds long life,
the evil roots dissolve and vanish."
For when the primordial life achieves numinous communion,
it perfects the Great Cavern’s Imperial Lord.

This chapter encompasses both nature and life.
The *Analects* says:
"Nature and the Way of Heaven cannot be heard."
Zilu heard but could not practice it.
This saying is excessive.
Among the three thousand disciples,
Yan Hui, Zeng Shen, Zisi, Ran Boniu, and Zhonggong
were all praised for their virtue—
how could they not have grasped the Master’s teachings on nature and the Way of Heaven?
Later Confucians take this as mere talk,
failing to examine the profound words and subtle principles
of the *Book of Changes* and the *Doctrine of the Mean*,
to explore their ultimate depths.
Instead, they claim that our Confucian school has no such learning on nature and life—
truly a shame.

The *Doctrine of the Mean* says:
"What Heaven decrees is called nature; following nature is called the Way."
The *Book of Changes* says:
"Exhausting principle and fully realizing nature leads to destiny."
How far apart are these teachings?

That which Heaven bestows and we receive at birth—this is it.

The root of nature and destiny stands firm. "One yin and one yang—this is called the Dao." That which completes it is nature. It is also said: "From sincerity comes clarity—this is called nature." Nature is akin to destiny. The *Book of Documents* says: "Able to illumine and exalt virtue." Virtue is nature. What the Buddhist teachings call "blessed virtue" is the firm and unshakable root of the nature school.

Filial piety perfects the enlightened king. The *Analects* says: "The noble person devotes himself to the root. When the root is established, the Dao arises. Are not filial piety and fraternal duty the root of humaneness?" Humaneness is humanity, and loving one’s kin is its greatest expression. In the time of Emperor Shun of Yu, the Supreme One descended to become his teacher, known as Master Yin Shou, instructing the emperor in the Dao of filial piety and fraternal duty. For above in Heaven, there are stars that govern this, and within the Dipper dwells the Perfected One, the Filial and Fraternal King, named Hong Kang, styled Bo Zhong. Long ago, Lan Gong of Qufu attained this Dao and transmitted it to Dame Mei; Dame Mei transmitted it to Grand Scribe Xu, and both achieved transcendence as celestial immortals. Those in the world who cultivate filial piety, fraternal duty, loyalty, and trustworthiness may attain this rank. Thus, the primordial *qi* is the Great Dao, and in the sun it is the Filial Dao Immortal King; the original *qi* is the Supreme Dao, and in the moon it is the Filial Dao Enlightened King; the mysterious *qi* is the Dao of filial piety, and in the Dipper it is the Filial and Fraternal King.

The Dao of the fundamental constants and human relations is naturally so—not imposed from without. Yet when those in authority govern with leniency and gentle instruction, filial piety, fraternal duty, loyalty, and trustworthiness may flourish. But if harsh governance and urgent demands press the people, they will be too preoccupied with mere survival to attend to ritual and propriety. As the saying goes: "Ritual and propriety arise from abundance; banditry springs from poverty." How can this be avoided? If those above act and those below emulate, from the family to the state, then under all Heaven, within the four seas, all will become loyal subjects and filial children. The *Book of Songs* says: "Their demeanor without flaw—this rectifies the four lands." Could this not be what it means?

In ancient times, there was a man named Tian Xuying, styled Liangyi, a native of the State of Qi. Of simple and unrefined nature, he served as an official in Hunan during the Kaihuang era. He attended to his parents with filial devotion and tilled the soil himself to fulfill his duties as a son. After his parents passed away, he received the register and methods of the *Great Cavern Scripture* from the Celestial Master Xue Jichang, reciting it without cease. Later, when Hunan suffered a drought and prayers for rain went unanswered, he was summoned to perform the rites. Liangyi arrived at the prefecture with disheveled hair and tattered clothes, and though he spoke not a word, rain fell. When the rains persisted unceasingly, he merely sat in silence with his headband removed, and the skies cleared. Emperor Xianzong of Tang dispatched envoys to summon him, but he declined and departed through *shijie*. Was this not ascension to immortality through filial piety?

Yuan-era native of Shu, Yao Wenqi, was of a kind and virtuous nature, serving his mother with utmost filial devotion. Though he passed fifty without an heir, while residing in Wuchang and traveling for office in Wuzhou, he encountered the imperial edict of Emperor Renzong, which declared: "Should you recite the *Great Cavern Scripture*, an heir may yet be expected." Later, after Wenqi had recited a thousand scrolls and presented memorials, a son was born to him the following year, named Wenchangbao. Was this not the response to his profound filial piety? For the *Wenchang Scripture* speaks of the Dao of Heaven, Earth, and Humanity as the Three Powers, all rooted in the harmony of yin and yang for the flourishing of life. If yin and yang are disordered, the qi and numbers become perverse, and the root of life nearly withers. *Wen* signifies principle and prosperity.

The root of life attains Great Harmony. The great virtue of Heaven and Earth is called "life." When the root is nourished by the true qi of Great Harmony, this becomes the unceasing foundation of life. The *Yellow Court Scripture* says: "Why not consume the *wu*? The essence of Great Harmony." The *wu* is the universal Dao of the world. "Through non-action, ascend to the Upper Clarity." The *Book of Changes* states: "No thought, no action." This is the principle of spontaneity—the Dao of the Great Elixir, non-action that accomplishes all. Ascending to the realm of Upper Clarity, one beholds the numinous and true Heavenly Worthy. When the qi of the spleen ascends to the Crimson Palace, it is all the qi of Great Harmony.

Generally, the middle scroll employs the six roots as metaphors. The Buddhist scriptures say: "Not entering form, sound, fragrance, taste, touch, or dharma—this is called *Srotaāpanna*. One return and no return—this is called *Sakṛdāgāmin*. No coming—this is called *Anāgāmin*. Truly no dharma—this is called *Arhat*." In Daoism, these are the Four Fruits of Immortality; in Buddhism, the Four Fruits of Arhatship. Before reaching ultimate realization, one does not revolve in the cycle of rebirth, thus temporarily nurturing Great Harmony and wandering in the Upper Clarity, ultimately aspiring to the supreme fruit. Buddhist disciples, ignorant of the *mingzong* (life’s root), glimpse only the nature and dismiss the illusory shell as useless, refusing to cherish it. They merely cultivate stagnant emptiness and torpor, failing to unite nature and life.

The above jade script of celestial seal comprises one hundred characters, governing above the Heaven of Supreme Peace and the Imperial Cliff, and below the Fifth Fortress of the Lord of Human Virtue. The *Mysterious Contract* states: "The Perfected attains the numinous penetration of the pure and primordial mandate of the Great Cavern. From the Heavenly Worthy and Heavenly Emperor to the Perfected, Immortals, and Divine Beings—whether of heavenly, divine, human, or demonic realms—and all sentient beings, the root of life and nature is fundamentally all-pervading, unobstructed, and unhindered. It can sever the earthly roots of the Five Peaks’ hells, the roots of evil, demonic registers, and ghostly ledgers. Constantly offering divine water and numinous fluid to the Celestial King of Primordial Beginning, it nourishes the Mysterious Flower and ascends to the rank of Perfected Immortal."

The Perfected Immortal first refines the elixir and concocts medicines in the human world, saving the poor, reciting spells over water, inscribing talismans, performing rites for orphaned souls, and guiding the departed, ascending in flight like the Immortal Ge. The Celestial King of Primordial Beginning said: "The nineteenth jade chapter of the *Great Cavern Scripture* of Literary Flourish: *The Numinous Fluid and the Fount of the Numinous Fluid*—numinous penetration." *Xinhai, Renzi, Gen, Jian.* The essence of green refined above black qi.

The numinous fluid within the body is like water within things—though seemingly intangible, the ancients said: "Tears, saliva, essence, fluid, qi, blood, and liquid—these seven are all yin substances." Yet without them, there would be no means to nourish the root of life. The Youth of the Mysterious Radiance of the Great Tenuity. Also called *jingjing* (radiant essence), this is the name of the youth of the Great Tenuity. As this chapter takes the numinous fluid as its theme, it employs the youth of the Great Tenuity to disseminate the qi of radiant flourish, unobstructing the hundred passages and preventing the stagnation of fluid and vessels, thereby facilitating ease of life.

The Great Tenuity appears five times in the scripture: the upper scroll says, "The jade tally verifies the Great Tenuity"; the Great Tenuity Heavenly Palace. The middle scroll says, "The Youth of the Mysterious Radiance of the Great Tenuity," merging with the youth of the Great Tenuity. The lower scroll says, "Proceeding to enter the Great Tenuity." Above the Nine Heavens of the divine, there are also the Heavenly Emperor of the Great Tenuity, the Great Emperor of the Great Tenuity, the Great Emperor of the Lesser Tenuity, and the like. The divine transforms within the Jade Chamber. "Exhausting the divine and knowing transformation—this is the flourishing of virtue." The spirit of the body congeals within the dwelling of the heart, enabling one to penetrate metal and stone, enter water without drowning, and walk through fire unscathed. From ancient times to the present, this is the Womb of the Buddha-Mother, also called the Celestial Worthy of Primordial Beginning in preservation.

Master Xujing said: "If you wish the spirit within the body not to depart, do not retain a single thing in the numinous terrace. If things remain in the heart, the spirit is not clear, dissipating true essence and harming sinew and bone. When the spirit departs, swiftly recall it; when the spirit returns to the body, the qi naturally follows. Doing this morning and night, the true embryo of the Red Child will naturally be born." The divine transformation refers to the myriad qi and myriad spirits in metamorphosis. The Jade Chamber is the golden house and jade chamber within the human body. If one can nurture it with celestial harmony, after a thousand days, transformation is possible.

The *Records of Immortals* recount that the Perfected of Pure Yang encountered an elder hosting a gathering. The Perfected said: "I possess a set of music. May I perform a piece to accompany the wine?" The host assented. The Perfected took a gourd from his waist, poured out twelve maidens, each holding a musical instrument. Two maidens bearing banners led the way, playing several melodies with refined elegance, their movements measured and graceful. The Perfected said: "This is the wondrous music of the Highest Heaven, unlike the vulgar music of the human world." The guests laughed and toasted with wine. The Perfected then returned the maidens to the gourd and swallowed it, saying: "These are the spirits of the five viscera and six bowels within the body. When the human qi is harmonious, the spirits are harmonious, thus producing musical sounds."

The immortal traditions further record that immortals often hear musical sounds within their abdomens. When one cultivates the *Wenchang Great Cavern* to this stage, there exists within the body a complete set of music, which those who nurture it well may also perceive. Is this not what the sixth chapter of the lower scroll and the fourteenth chapter refer to as "sandalwood blazing, the tuning of auspiciousness"? When this scripture is gathered, it becomes the precious *Canghu Jie*; when dispersed, it becomes the sound of "sandalwood blazing, the tuning." Only when yin and yang qi harmonize can sound arise—such is the flourishing of the Wenchang Dao.

**Soaring feathers traverse the purple void.**
The regulation of birds lies in qi. Thus, when the spirit-qi is refined and the yang spirit manifests its form, wings naturally grow, allowing one to ascend and delight in the purple void.

Formerly, Xue Jichang, a native of Hanzhou in western Shu, hailed from an official family. Fond of mountains and rivers, he journeyed to Qingcheng. His parents, deeming the distance not too far, accompanied him. Later, he traveled south to Taoyuan, where he encountered the *Zhengyi* Master on Mount Nanyue, who transmitted to him the *Register of the Great Cavern Scripture and Methods*. He delved deeply into its essential truths. Emperor Ming of Tang summoned him to the capital, where his discourse on the Dao and virtue met with imperial approval. The emperor bestowed upon him the title of *Tianshi*. Later, he begged to return to the mountains, and the emperor composed a poem to send him off, earning the admiration of the entire court.

One day, he said to his disciples: "Tonight, there is a gathering on Zhurong Peak, and I have been summoned to attend." Suddenly, he rose into the air and departed, never looking back. This is the *Great Cavern* soaring through the purple void. Lady Wei of Mount Mao once rode the clouds to Mount Nanyue, covering a thousand miles in an instant. When the clouds dispersed, they transformed into stone, which remains on Mount Nanyue to this day.

**The sun forms the triple *jin* junction.**
The character *jin* appears three times: in the first chapter of the upper scroll, it reads, "The dry landscape and radiance together give birth to *jin*"; in the eighth chapter of the middle scroll, "The sun forms the triple *jin* junction"; and in the final chapter of the lower scroll, "Carrying *jin* to the chamber of the Supreme Emperor." All share the same meaning. The *Triple Jin Junction* is the name of the youth of the Grand Tenuity, capable of generating fluids.

It is also said that the *three jin* are the three spirits within the heart: one is the *Spiritual Vermilion Lord*, another the *Spiritual Luminous Lord*, and the third the *Spiritual Yellow Lord*. The sun interacts with them. This aligns with the meaning of "the dry landscape and radiance together give birth to *jin*." The sun is the essence of the great yang, and within it resides the three-legged crow, which in humans corresponds to the *pi*.

**Bearing the talisman, ascend the Emperor’s ramparts.**
Once the youth of the Grand Tenuity interacts with the heart’s spirits, one should bear the talisman and ascend the jade city of the Supreme Emperor. The area behind the brain is called the *Jade City*. The third chapter of the lower scroll states, "Clad in rosy clouds, ascend the Emperor’s ramparts," which refers to the same—namely, the *yu zhen* bone in humans.

**Unlock the passes with the golden tally.**
Only by holding the tally can one unlock the passes. The tally is a symbolic token; when passing through barriers, one must carry it. At the pass, the tally is matched, and even the slightest discrepancy is deemed fraudulent. Tallies may be made of gold, bronze, or bamboo—here, it is called the *golden tally*, signifying its preciousness.

**Close the gates and strike the jade chime.**
The mouth, eyes, nose, and ears are all called windows, doors, and gates. "Closing" means to seal or block them. The *jade chime* refers to the act of striking the teeth: the left is called the *chime*, the right the *qing*, and the center the *drum*. Thus, to subdue demons, one strikes the chime; to pay homage, one sounds the drum.

**Vanquish the demons of the Three Feng wilds.**
The *Three Feng* refer to Fengdu Mountain, as recorded in the *Scripture on Subduing Demons*. Located in the northeast corner of heaven and earth, the *gen* direction, it is the gate of ghosts. Towering ten thousand *li* high, it is divided into three layers. The upper layer, level with the heavens, is called the *Upper Prime Six Cavern Palaces*, governed by immortal officials. The middle layer is the *Middle Prime Six Cavern Palaces*, ruled by the Great Demon King. The lower layer contains thirty-seven hells—thirty-six in the four directions and one central hell overseeing them. Hence, it is named the *Three Feng* after the Three Primes, and its vastness is called the *wilds*. Without the Demon King, the six yin and six cavern grudges could not be controlled. The demons beneath him are the lingering souls of defeated generals and fallen soldiers from past lives, fierce and combative, their killing intent unresolved. They band together, sometimes masquerading as loyal ministers or righteous knights, receiving offerings from humans, or acting as plague emissaries, tormenting living beings. Cultivators must guard against them, lest they harm the Dao. They may transform into beauty to ravage one’s spiritual root or steal one’s supreme treasure. Thus, one holds the talisman and register, strikes the chime, and beats the drum to wage war against the yin demons.

The *Three Feng* reside between the human kidneys, generally an extremely yin realm. As the *Triplex Unity* states: "Only when the host of yin is entirely stripped away does the warmth of yang appear." One must still battle and repel the yin demons before pure yang can emerge, gathering the lightness to ascend and transform, attaining the rank of Perfected.

**Summon the spirits to the Upper Clarity Palace.**
Gather and summon the souls to the true realm of Upper Clarity—namely, the *Crimson Palace* of the Middle Prime. Heaven possesses talismans for summoning the true and attracting the numinous, which can assemble celestial perfected, earthly sages, and the souls of the three realms. With these, congealment comes easily.

**Emerging bright from the Gate of Utmost Yin,**
This is the lower gate, the palace of the kidneys. One must exit this yin gate to ascend to the yang realm—this is the kidney qi paying homage to the heart qi. As the *Alchemical Scripture* states: "When lead encounters the birth of *gui*, swiftly gather it." This refers to the moment when the yang qi of the north stirs, instantly laying the foundation of the elixir.

**Entering the chamber of the Six Harmonies.**
The *Six Harmonies* refer to the space within heaven and earth. The *Commentary* states: "Beyond the Six Harmonies, the sage preserves but does not discuss." The body possessing the six roots is also called the *Six Harmonies*, corresponding to the *Zhouyi*’s "flowing through the six voids." Some say it resides within the human brain, where the spirits of the body gather. When a person dies, the hun and po occupy it, which is why skulls retain their numinosity.

Human essence rides qi through the limbs and bone marrow, hence the strength of the four limbs. During the union of man and woman, spirit and qi gather in the lower prime, and essence, riding qi, also converges there. If one masters the art of secret retention, the essence will gather in the *Six Harmonies* chamber, merging with spirit and qi into a single mass. It then ascends from the kidneys through the double passes of the spine into the *Mud Pill*, which is called "returning essence to replenish the brain." Thus, the eighth chapter of the lower scroll states: "The Peach Lord guards the Six Harmonies, restraining essence to defend the Mud Pill," precisely referring to this.

Many in the world practice what is called the "Art of Riding the Woman," also known as the "Three Peaks and Yellow Valley Method," or the "Bedchamber Arts," or the "Yellow River Reversed Flow Technique." Though these names vary, they all originate from the *Sea Bottom* and *Tail Gate*. There are five types of *Six Harmonies*, as this middle scroll states: "Entering the *Six Harmonies* chamber of essence," while the lower scroll speaks of "congealing radiance in the *Six Harmonies* chamber," "transforming chaos in the *Six Harmonies* sanctuary," "gazing from the *Six Harmonies* court," and "the Peach Lord guarding the *Six Harmonies*." Other texts expand on this, saying: "Restraining demons to generate the Six Lights," "the great center where the Six Qi are purified," "the Five Demons strike the Six Yin," and "fortifying my Six Immortal Palaces." This middle scroll focuses on cultivation through the six roots. If one can purify the six roots, the Six Lights will arise, the Six Qi will be clarified, the Six Cavern Demons will be subdued, and the Six Palaces will ascend to immortality.

Reversing aging to transform into a youthful form can make the body strong and light, preserve a radiant complexion, and restore the appearance of a child. Thus it is said: "Reversing aging to transform into a youthful form." Those whose white hair turns black again or whose fallen teeth regrow—such cases have been witnessed in the world, for cultivation reaches this level of wonder.

Returning to whiteness and reverting to infant youth. Another version reads "returning the po-soul to infant youth," which is surely an error. For when white hair turns black again and fallen teeth regrow, one resembles an infant child. The *Jade Scripture* states: "Those with white heads and wrinkled faces may all be transformed and delivered." By concentrating qi to attain suppleness, one reverts to the nature of an infant.

The Cavern Source is pure and luminous.
The Cavern Source is the deep spring of water, the origin of fluids. When pure and still, it radiates brilliance. Laozi said: "The clear is the source of the turbid." When the source is clear, the flow is long—unceasing and unbroken, day and night, cycling without end.

The fluids possess numinous efficacy.
The method of swallowing saliva: constantly use the Red Dragon to stir the Flower Pool, filling the mouth, then divide it into three swallows. Still, visualize an infant child in the Crimson Palace to receive and guide it downward. One such cycle is called "one passage." Thirty-six passages constitute "lesser attainment," three hundred and sixty "middle attainment," and one thousand two hundred "great attainment." With long practice, spirit and radiance flourish—hence it is said to possess numinous efficacy.

The scripture’s meaning of fluids appears nine times: in the upper scroll, "The body is nimble with myriad fluid waves"; in the middle scroll, "Fluids drift in the mysterious void"; "Embracing the elixir of fortune"; "Fluids possess numinous efficacy"; "Swallowing fluids generates the myriad spirits"; and in the lower scroll, "Swallowing savor generates the Five Sprouts," "The hundred joints receive fluids," and the like—all share the same principle.

Generally, human fluids serve to circulate through the joints and irrigate the viscera. Yet some despise and spit them out, causing the five viscera to wither, spirit to dull, and other ailments to arise, even leading to death.

Swallowing fluids generates the myriad spirits.
The spirit is fundamentally the one heart-spirit alone. Yet it divides into the myriad spirits, for one qi generates the myriad qi. Heaven and Earth are also one, yet within them the sun, moon, stars, wind, rain, thunder, and lightning transform endlessly. Likewise, humans: the eyes see, the ears hear, the mouth speaks, the hands grasp, the feet walk—all undergo countless changes. Thus, when encountering good, there is fortune; when encountering evil, there is misfortune. Nurtured, they endure; abandoned, they perish. Only with fluids do the myriad spirits have sustenance; without fluids, the myriad spirits depart and vanish.

The Flower Pool’s divine water fuses.
The Flower Pool is the mouth; the Red Dragon is the tongue. With the tongue, one stirs and gathers divine water, which naturally arises from the two orifices beneath the tongue: the left is called Golden Essence, the right Jade Fluid. When a person is ill, the tongue withers, the spirit departs, and the person dies.

It surges upward to irrigate and moisten.
Water’s nature is to flow downward, but when forced, it can rise above the forehead. Divine water, born below, surges upward to irrigate the five viscera, making the body’s complexion lustrous and moist—just as water does between Heaven and Earth.

It comes and goes without end.
From below to above, from above back to below, the Three Palaces ascend and descend, circulating ceaselessly. Human fluids are moved by qi: when qi flows, fluids circulate; when qi stagnates, fluids stagnate—thus illness arises.

It unblocks the source of the generative Dao.
Unceasing circulation is called "unblocking." When fluids flow smoothly through the hundred joints, nourishing the entire body, this is called the source of the Dao. Laozi said: "Water benefits the myriad things and thus nearly approaches the Dao." Water’s nature is yielding and compliant, hence it accords with the Dao.

The Heavenly Root is ever lush and abundant.
The Heavenly Root is also called the Spirit Valley or the Mysterious Female. Laozi said: "The gate of the Mysterious Female is called the root of Heaven and Earth." In the human body, the kidneys are the fundamental root—hence the name Heavenly Root. Those who indulge excessively in bedroom arts damage the kidneys; when the kidneys are damaged, essence has no support and leaks away. Excessive leakage scatters qi, and scattered qi leaves the spirit without a master—thus it departs, and the body withers, leading to ruin.

Therefore, those who cultivate the Dao must keep the Heavenly Root lush and abundant, cherishing essence and qi, nurturing them properly. This is the lifeline of the body—hence it is called the Heavenly Root.

The above Jade Stanza in celestial script comprises one hundred and ten characters. Above, it governs the Heaven of Manifest Stability and Ultimate Wind; below, it encircles the Fifth Rampart’s Lord of Human Virtue.

The *Mysterious Contract* states: "The Perfected One obtains the pure and luminous fluids of the Cavern Source, their numinous efficacy surging upward to irrigate the Flower Pool. The divine water circulates endlessly, unblocking the source of the Emperor’s Heart and the One Mystery—this is called the spirit within the true center, the Great Lord of Longevity. To the left, it generates the Peerless; to the right, the White Prime. Though their names differ, they are the Great One, the Controller of Destiny and Numinous Efflux, the Peach and Plum of Health and Longevity. They grasp talismans and hold registers, revere filial piety and uphold the Dao, perfecting wondrous conduct and preserving the true—such is called the Perfected One, whose rank attains to Sacred Immortal."

The Sacred Immortal was once in the world, slaying the wicked and eliminating harm for the people. With merit complete and the Dao perfected, their entire household ascended in broad daylight. Examples include Xu Jingyang and others.

The Primordial Heavenly King said: "The twentieth Jade Stanza of the Great Cavern of Literary Florescence: 'Essence and blood illuminate the Cavern; essence and blood possess numinous efficacy.'" Gui-chou, Jia-yin, Returning Maiden, Abundance. The Great Yang transforms the Three Mornings...

Firmness, centrality, and uprightness—pure and refined essence—are the abode of inherent nature and the root of destiny. In quiescence and immobility, they bear the deepest relation to both nature and destiny; how can they not be prized?

*Chen* is also a name for the sun, for the sun is the Great Yang, and the morning’s radiance is its chariot. In cultivation, the *zi* hour marks the Winter Solstice, corresponding to the *Fu* hexagram, when the first yang stirs beneath the earth. At this time, one should sit in ordered stillness, dispel impurities, halt thoughts, purify the heart, and guard the One, allowing yang qi to gradually arise and grow. By the *chou* hour, two yangs emerge; by *yin*, three yangs—fully forming the *Qian* and *Kun* hexagrams, ascending like a chariot. The Purple Carriage traverses the Mysterious Path.

The Purple Carriage is the solar wheel, where the Purple River Carriage transports yang qi upward into the brain. The Mysterious Path is the Double Passes flanking the spine, ascending to the Jade City Gate and congealing in the Mud Pill Palace. From here, the yang spirit may exit and enter. The Primordial Lord guards the Valley Youth, the name of the coalesced Central Primordial true essence and soul. The Primordial Lord is the Great One Primordial Lord, residing in the head, constantly blocking the Gate of Death and opening the Gate of Life to grant longevity. The Valley Youth is the Yellow Tranquility Youth, dwelling in the stomach cavity, governing the digestion of grain and dispersion of qi, transforming food and drink. Thus, the Great One Primordial Lord guards this as the root of the body. As the common saying goes: "Without root, food comes first; with food but no spirit to govern it, digestion fails." The Primordial Lord is called the Feminine One, for women who attain Daoist transcendence are all titled Primordial Lords, the most exalted appellation. Guard the stomach and seal the Gate of Death.

The Gate of Death is what people fear to enter. Essence and qi are things; the wandering soul is change. Once changed, transformation occurs—how can life return? What has parted cannot be rejoined; how can one not be cautious? The Valley Youth guards the stomach cavity, blocking the Gate of Death. When food is digested, the human path is born. The *Scripture of Attaining the Dao* states: "Still, regulate food and drink, dispel corpse-demons," and so on. Some say the Three Primes of essence and blood—Lord Wang, styled Yellow Tranquility—are the coalesced Central Primordial true essence and soul, the Guardian Valley Youth. Thus, this stanza centers on essence and blood, perfecting wondrous conduct and wondrous fruition.

The Golden Talisman illumines the Northern Splendor. Golden Talismans and Jade Contracts are refined from true yang, treasured by the perfected. Their radiance blazes like northern brilliance, resplendent as glittering jade. The North is one of the ten directions, hence the scriptures speak of the Ten Splendid Wondrous Practices, a sign of lung metal generating kidney water. The Jade Contract delivers the Seven Ancestors.

Some say "unfolds the Seven Ancestors," but this is incorrect. Only by obtaining the Golden Talisman and Jade Contract, congealed from true yang, can the seven generations of ancestors all transcend their kind, ascending to the Vermilion Numinous Fire Mansion to refine their souls and forge their spirits. Only then may they attain immortal transformation.

The Imperial True irrigates the Upper Birth, the name of the Imperial True essence and soul within the node. Also called the Infant, it enables one to be born in the celestial realms. The cinnabar lies in the first stirring of thought as the Imperial True. Thus, the *Chapter on Generating the Spirit* states: "Form the embryo and guard the Yellow Chamber." It is also called the Dark Terrace Birth. Sever the breath and end the Three Wretched Sufferings.

This was already annotated under the "Five Suffering Realms" in the *Tongue Chapter*. Within the Three Wretched Paths and Five Sufferings—amidst the Fengdu, Mount Tai, and the Twelve River Sources of the earth-water realm—countless underworld officials and jailers abound. These are often heroic and resolute figures from the world, bold and courageous, capable of resolving doubts and righting wrongs, greatly benefiting worldly affairs. Upon death, they become efficacious spirits, selected by the Earth Bureau to serve as underworld rulers. In the Three Wretched Paths, Five Sufferings, Nine Dark Hells, Fengdu, and Mount Tai, they act as officials of the netherworld, dwelling in eternal darkness, cut off from the Three Lights, adjudicating disputes and resolving uncertainties. Every three hundred years, they are promoted. This is the fate of those who, in life, neither understood the Dao nor performed good deeds, thus receiving such netherworld posts and severing their roots of rebirth. Those who cultivate the Supreme Imperial One True Dao of the Great Cavern of Literary Florescence distance themselves from such underworld offices.

The Cavern shines with luminous clarity, the original radiance of inherent purity, aided by fluids—all water qi. Thus, it is called the Cavern Mystery, Cavern Source, and Cavern Clarity. The Cavern Source corresponds to the fluid character, Cavern Clarity to the essence character, and Cavern Mystery to the qi character. The Imperial Heart penetrates the Great Mystery.

Attaining the Imperial Heart’s penetration allows unobstructed illumination, akin to the bodhi heart of Buddhism or what Confucians call the innate knowledge and capacity of humanity. By turning inward, gathering the heart-spirit, and congealing emptiness and stillness, one naturally gains insight. As Buddhism says: "Abide thus, thus subdue the heart"—the same principle. The Great Elixir is mercury, which descends into the lead crucible and is refined with civil and martial fire to congeal into golden liquid. Some take the Imperial Heart as the chapter’s theme, but the Seventh-Curve Patriarch’s *Mysterious Contract* designates essence and blood as the theme, so we follow that, for the heart is the mansion of blood.

The wisdom of past lives knows former destinies, kalpas before and after, past and future—all is clearly understood. This is the knowledge of past lives, the foremost of the Buddha’s six penetrations, which other immortals cannot attain. The root and origin lie within the center.

Tracing back to one’s root and origin, all stems from the central path: rectifying the heart, sincerity of intent, investigating things, and extending knowledge—nothing lies beyond. The center is the great root of the world. From center to periphery, purity and wholeness prevail, with the inner as root and the outer as branch.

The future and the minds of others—*The Doctrine of the Mean* states that the Way of utmost sincerity can foreknow. Thus, Buddhism says: "The Thus-Come One knows the myriad kinds of minds of sentient beings." It also says: "The past mind cannot be grasped, the present mind cannot be grasped, the future mind cannot be grasped." The ungraspable means one cannot abide in this state. Only those possessing the six spiritual penetrations can know this.

The so-called six penetrations are: the penetration of the heavenly eye, the penetration of the heavenly ear, the penetration of knowing others’ minds, the penetration of past lives, the penetration of spiritual states, and the penetration of accordant will. Possessing these six penetrations, one may know the karmic causes, powers, and retributions of past kalpas, future kalpas, and the three times—all without obstruction, fused as one. The three realms and the ten directions become unimpeded and unobstructed, merging into a single body. Thus, the *Zhuangzi* states: "The myriad transformations arise within the body." When the cosmos is at peace, radiance issues forth as heavenly light, and therein knowledge and perception arise. It is also said that only after attaining liberation does one gain knowledge and perception.

**Penetrating the Source and Penetrating Clarity**
In the previous section, *Penetrating the Source* spoke of fluids, while this section, *Penetrating Clarity*, speaks of essence and blood—both belonging to the category of water. If one cultivates and verifies these wondrous practices, one may attain the six penetrations in full and realize the fruit of non-retrogression, forever free from the fear of loss.

**The Myriad Ways Arise from Penetration**
The myriad ways and dharmas all arise from water. With penetration, there is nothing unknown; the affairs of past and future become as clear as pointing to one’s palm. Thus, many scriptures state that the ten penetrations arise from this. When the ten penetrations achieve true penetration, transformations occur naturally.

Some may find the meaning intricate and burdensome. Qi replies: When the Heavenly King expounds the scriptures, it begins with the stirring of numinous winds and the resonance of treasure-light forming sound. Collecting the sounds within the light and unfolding them repeatedly, they become profound chapters. The Jade Emperor ordered their sequence, and the Supreme Mystery compiled them. Only after passing through the hands of three sages was the text completed. How could mere discourse presume to match it? Thus, the sagely admonitions are earnest and repeated, lest even a single word among humans and devas fail to return to truth. Therefore, they are reiterated again and again. Those who explain it must follow the phrasing of each sentence. Though the text winds and turns repeatedly, it is only so that if one fails to believe and understand in one passage, one may awaken in the next. What difficulty is there in this?

The above jade chapter in celestial script comprises eighty characters, governing above the Heaven of Filial Purity and Radiance and presiding below over the Lord of Human Virtue of the Fifth Fortress.

The *Mysterious Contract* states: When the Perfected One attains the penetrating clarity of pure essence and blood, the numinous penetration of the *Great Mystery* and the true Dao of the Emperor’s Heart of Penetrating Clarity is born. Past kalpas, future kalpas, the three realms, the ten directions, the roots of self and others, past and future—all are known and seen with sevenfold penetration and eightfold reach. One can sever the waves of the Water Emperor Qi Bo, the winding springs of the Water Tiger, the sources of the Qu River, the earth’s roots, evil roots, demonic registers, and ghostly accounts. Constantly offering the golden liquor of *Penetrating the Source* and the dharma lamp of *Penetrating Clarity* to the Primordial Heavenly King, one generates qi to moisten the roots, achieving luminous wisdom, wondrous enlightenment, and great capacity, advancing to the noble rank of Upper Immortal of the Jade Clarity’s highest grade.

**Upper Immortals**
These are those who, having cultivated and refined the utmost truth in the human realm, ascend in broad daylight to become guardians of the Jade Emperor. They advance to the Great Luo Heaven as attendants of the Three Clarities, such as Heavenly Master Zhang.

The *Jade Clarity Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture* was proclaimed by the Primordial Heavenly King. Some may ask: Is there a difference between the Heavenly Venerable and the Heavenly King? Qi replies: The titles of the Primordial Beginning are manifold. Some call him the Primordial Heavenly Venerable, or the Primordial Heavenly Venerable of Spontaneous Chaos, or the Primordial Heavenly Venerable of Floating Black, or the Primordial Lord of Heaven, or the Primordial Heavenly Emperor, or the Primordial Qi Heavenly Lord, or the Primordial Yang Lord of Heaven. When the various heavens expound the Dao, each celestial being names the Venerable according to their own perception.

The Dao is originally without name and not truly possessed of form. Those who aspire to the Dao and rely on virtue, clinging to names and exhausting words, are not aligned with the Dao. Yet for those who have not yet understood, one cannot conceal it, and thus, out of necessity, it is set down in writing.

Before heaven and earth were separated, the primordial qi began to coalesce, taking the form of a chicken’s egg. Within it, the Being of Chaos was born. Seated at the center, it divided the clear and turbid, the yin and yang qi, above and below. Its head supported the Qian Heaven, its belly enveloped the Kun Earth. Each day, the Being of Chaos grew one *zhang*, and heaven and earth likewise grew one *zhang*. After ninety-nine trillion, nine hundred ninety-nine billion, nine hundred ninety thousand kalpas, the two modes stabilized. From the qi of the nine palaces within its body, the nine heavens were structured above, and the nine earths congealed below. The spirit within the qi reigned over the nine heavens, and the numen within the qi governed the nine earths. Its heart and kidneys became the Kan and Li trigrams, the sun and moon; the true qi of the five viscera became the five stars; the essence of the nine orifices became the Northern Dipper; its breath became the Xun wind; its voice became the Zhen thunder; its fluids, qi, and blood became the Dui marsh; its body became the Gen mountain. The topography of rivers and peaks resembled the form of the Being of Chaos, hence their uneven heights—mountains and cliffs, peaks and ridges, all irregular.

The Being of Chaos ascended and transformed its spirit above the nine heavens, becoming the Primordial Heavenly Venerable of Spontaneous Chaos. The lice and fleas within its body transformed into the twelve earthly branches and twenty-eight constellations—such as *zi* as the rat and *chou* as the ox, or the Horn Wood Tiger and the Neck Metal Dragon. Dwelling within the Kun belly, their light shone upon the Qian head, becoming the stars and constellations. Its hair and whiskers became grasses and trees; its form became earth; its bones became stone; its tears, saliva, fluids, blood, and urine became rivers, seas, and streams. Only the harmonious qi gathered to form humans, their bodies hundreds of *yojanas* in length. Yet the human form was not yet complete—some had human heads and serpent bodies, others ox heads and human bodies—each drawn together by the resonance of their qi. Some flew, others walked the earth, ascending to heaven or descending to earth, going wherever they pleased. Some devoured one another without restraint. Thus, the Three Sovereigns arose in succession to govern them, honoring the Being of Chaos as Master Pan Gu. The Heavenly Sovereign, Earthly Sovereign, and Human Sovereign correspond to the *Cavern of Truth*, the *Cavern of Mystery*, and the *Cavern of Spirit*.

Thus, heaven, earth, humans, and the myriad things are all transformations of the Primordial Beginning’s singular nothingness. Each thing possesses the Primordial Beginning, for all arise from the primordial qi. Hence, it is called the Primordial Beginning. Only humans receive the most numinous of this qi. How great is this!

The form of all humans born today still resembles that of Master Pan Gu. Thus, when Fuxi drew the trigrams, he modeled them upon Pan Gu’s form: *Qian* as the head, *Kun* as the belly, *Xun* as the thighs, *Zhen* as the feet, *Kan* as the ears, *Li* as the eyes, *Gen* as the hands, and *Dui* as the mouth. Had he not depicted them as images but instead taken them as mere characters, it would still be evident that they embody Pan Gu. All are the continuous transmission of a single qi, passed down through his descendants and posterity—how precious is this!

Yet many in the world, through wine, lust, wealth, and strife, ravage the Primordial Beginning and breach the integrity of Chaos. Therefore, the heavenly spirits expound these cavern chapters, that people may chant and recite them, their natures and dispositions resonating to restore the qi’s wholeness. Only then can they reunite with the natural, primordial Heaven of Chaos, attaining longevity if they seek it, immortality if they pursue it, and effortlessly becoming perfected beings by nature.

Zhongyangzi Wei Qi bows in reverence.

*Jade Purity’s Boundless Supreme Perfected Wenchang Cavern Scripture of the Great Dao*, Scroll Seven
*(Note: This line may originally read, “then the qi has nowhere to return and scatters.”)*
*(Note: “Kun” may be a superfluous interpolation.)*
*(Note: “Wang” may be a scribal error for “zhu.”)*

*Jade Purity’s Boundless Supreme Perfected Wenchang Cavern Scripture of the Great Dao*, Scroll Eight
Annotated by Zhongyangzi Wei Qi of Mount Penglai in Eastern Shu

The Dao speaks: At that time, the Dao was truly pure, luminously wondrous, empty yet penetrating, spiritually unobstructed. Before Heaven and Earth divided, before father and mother were born, it stood solitary and alone. Within it, the myriad transformations of Heaven and Earth, the ten thousand affairs and things, were all indistinguishably commingled—myriad distinctions yet one root.

As *Laozi* says: “There is a thing, chaotically formed, born before Heaven and Earth. Silent and void, it stands alone and does not change, circling endlessly without cease.” This is it.

In humans, it is the heart. Its transformations are unfathomable, responding to every affair and circumstance. When still, it is nature; when moving, it is emotion. Emotion follows circumstances and shifts without end, transforming into desire. Heart, nature, emotion, and desire—these four emerge from the same source yet bear different names.

If one can be still and guard the heart, the original nature will naturally appear. But if one follows the flow of emotional desires and forgets to return, one will sink into the bitter sea of birth and death—how then can one escape? This is why the immortals and humans expound scriptures with the words of the Dao. The Jade Clarity Dao Lord unfolds the wondrous sounds of the Primordial Beginning, hence it is called “the Dao speaks.” To guard one’s nature is to be of Jade Clarity.

The Primordial Beginning Heavenly King, with the qi of the Great Cavern’s Highest Supreme, the Chaotic Cavern’s Supreme Non-Being, and the Primordial Heaven Treasure Jade Sovereign, as recorded in the previous scroll under the “Highest Cavern Primordial” passage, condensed it into a single precious pearl, called the Millet Pearl or the Maṇi Pearl, as noted in the middle scroll under the “Embodied Treasure’s Radiant Pearl” passage.

In this second section, once one knows where the Dao resides, one stands like a sheer cliff a myriad fathoms high, letting go with both hands, closing the eyes and leaping—sitting in empty space, neither touching Heaven above nor treading Earth below, vast and boundless, without limit or boundary. Within the chaotic vastness, one naturally attains something. The wonder of this attainment is like illness cured by medicine, like awakening from a dream, like obtaining a foot-long jade disk, like gaining a precious pearl. This is the moment when the Jade Sovereign’s qi gathers to form the pearl—how could it not be joyous!

In the third section, once one knows this place of joy, one permeates it everywhere, the entire body—hands and eyes—without obstruction. Yet upon reaching this point, one must not cling to it as self-satisfaction but must cast it aside. It is named *Canghujie*.

*Cang* is the true color of verdant yang; *hu* means great; the primordial qi is luminous and perfectly great. *Jie* means to rise straight and strong. Thus, the eleventh chapter of the Lower Scripture says: “The five qi govern the center with *jie*,” meaning the Primordial Beginning, with its supremely great and unyielding qi, condenses the precious pearl and names it *Canghujie*.

*Naming* is the mandate of Heaven. The flowing principle of Heaven bestows it upon the myriad things, and what humans receive at birth is called nature. *Canghujie* is the virtue of nature, for it arises from the pure, unadulterated spirit of firmness, strength, centrality, and uprightness.

It says: “I, with this precious pearl, follow the wondrous One of the Dao, generously bestowing the root of life.” The precious pearl has no form—it is the human’s nature and life. As the *Lunyu* says: “Nature and the Dao of Heaven cannot be heard.” How could petty immortals of lower rank be worthy to hear of it? Thus, the Primordial Beginning declares: “I, with this precious pearl, follow the Heavenly One—water’s register—to establish the root, thereby founding Heaven and Earth.”

*Generously* means water generously benefits the myriad things, thus approaching the Dao. Some say: “Follow the Dao’s wondrous goodness, the One that lends the root of life,” which must be an error. The One is the child of the Dao; when the Dao’s qi moves, it generates water, so the One is the root of Heaven and Earth, the eldest of all virtues. As *Laozi* says: “Only the Dao is good at bestowing and completing.” *Bestowing* is merely lending. Heaven and Earth, the myriad things—none do not borrow this to become the root of their generation and completion.

It conceives the Mysterious and divides the Primordial, giving birth to the Beginning and transmitting the True. *Conceiving the Mysterious* means containing the Great Mystery; *dividing the Primordial* means illuminating the Great Origin; *giving birth to the Beginning* means bringing forth the Great Commencement. The three qi of Mystery, Origin, and Beginning transform and give rise to the Three Treasure Lords. Father and son inherit in succession, master and disciple transmit the True—hence it is called *transmitting the True*.

The three qi: the qi of the Great Mystery generates the Blazing Yang’s Three Qi; the qi of the Great Origin generates the August Light’s Three Qi; the qi of the Great Commencement generates the Chaotic Vastness’ Three Qi. Together, they are called the Nine Qi, known as “the three qi uniting in virtue, the nine qi aligning in harmony.”

They transform and give rise to the various heavens. The nine qi each generate ten thousand qi, which in turn generate the Four Brahmā Seed Peoples’ Four Heavens, the Four Formless Heavens, the Eighteen Form Heavens, and the Six Desire Heavens—these are the Thirty-Two Heavens. Below these, they further generate the Eight Brahmā and Nine Heavens, along with the sun, moon, and stars arrayed in the void. The *Scripture of Salvation*’s five texts open and expand, universally planting divine spirits.

As the *Book of Changes* says: “The Dao of Qian becomes male; the Dao of Kun becomes female.” The two qi interact and transform, giving birth to the myriad things. From this point onward, humans and things flourish and multiply in abundance. Among them, humans are the most spiritually numinous and noble, positioned at the center. They should embody the Dao and model Heaven with their divine illumination.

They congeal into the ten thousand qi. This line should precede “transform and give rise to the various heavens.” The Primordial Beginning congeals the qi of its own body, unfolding and transforming it into the ten thousand qi, only then can it give rise to the various heavens. The *Great Golden Book* states: “The Jade Sovereign’s qi comprises ninety-nine thousand nine hundred ninety-nine hundred million qi.”

Great indeed is this supreme treasure—only I alone exist. The Primordial Beginning declares itself, as in the *Book of Changes*: “Great indeed is the Qian’s origin—all things rely on it for beginning. Supreme indeed is the Kun’s origin—all things rely on it for birth.” The words “supremely great” apply only to Qian and Kun. *Alone exists* means to exist uniquely. Now, the *Great Cavern Scripture* stands above the two trigrams Qian and Kun, hence it is called the Non-Ultimate. The Non-Ultimate and yet the Supreme Ultimate. As the *Book of Changes* says: “The Supreme Ultimate generates the Two Modes.” The Two Modes establish their positions, and the Chaos Clan arises—topping Heaven and treading Earth. Chaos grows one *zhang* each day, Heaven rises one *zhang*, and Earth sinks one *zhang*—this is the Primordial Beginning.

Now the Jade Clarity Dao Lord reissues this treasure. As the *Book of Changes* states: “If not the right person, the Dao does not circulate in vain.” The Primordial Beginning long concealed this treasure, awaiting the proper recipient before transmitting it. The Jade Clarity Dao Lord is none other than the Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy, to whom the Primordial Beginning entrusted this great Dao.

This “reissuing of the treasure” refers to the fact that in the first year of the Dragon Han era, the Primordial Beginning transformed and came into being, and in that same year revealed this scripture. Now, the Jade Clarity Dao Lord reissues it—this scripture must have been expounded again and again after the Kaihuang era. The heavens and the earth each hold their fixed positions. As Confucius said: “Heaven is noble, Earth is base; Qian and Kun are thus established. High and low are arrayed, and noble and humble take their places.” This is what the *Book of Documents* means by “the Five Constants in proper order.” The Daoist scriptures say: “I am your root”—this is the same idea. Just as Qian and Kun, Kan and Li, first give rise to the Four Images, and then to the Eight Trigrams, which have been arrayed since antiquity through countless kalpas of dust, until Fuxi emerged, looked up and down, and drew the Eight Trigrams, only then were they made manifest. King Wen doubled the lines, and Confucius appended the commentaries—only after passing through the hands of these three sages was the system made vast and complete, so as to accord with the principles of nature and destiny, and to encompass the Three Powers in their duality. This *Great Cavern Scripture of the Immortals* existed prior to Heaven and prior to Earth. Now the Primordial Beginning reissues it. The Dao waits for its time—how could it be lightly bestowed? The Dao Lord ascended and entrusted it to the Supreme Mystery Dao Father, and only after transmission through three sages did the ghosts and spirits of the Three Realms and the beings of all heavens and worlds come to know the origin of their existence. For from Qian they knew the Primordial Beginning and the One Qi of the Great Origin.

The Heavenly Emperor Kings and the Perfected Great Sages of the heavens gazed in awe at the treasure’s radiance. Its light spread into hundreds of thousands of millions of rays, coalescing into the *Great Cavern Scripture of the Immortals*. The True Immortals lifted their heads to behold the luminous splendor, its brilliance scattering in patterns of light and color—hundreds of thousands of millions of boundless, inconceivable rays—forming the *Great Cavern Scripture of the Immortals*. The *Jade Scripture* also says: “Concealed, it emits radiance,” and speaks of the “seventeen imperial lights,” all of which are the numinous light within one’s own body, enabling the formation of scriptural patterns. Another example is the Five Directions’ True Writings and Jade Chapters, all formed from the condensation of celestial light and divine qi.

The Jade Seal coalesces into clouds and shines forth in scriptural patterns. The Jade Seal is the ultimate treasure. It is said that its precious script coalesces into cloud-seals and its resplendent colors form patterns, illuminating the celestial Han with its revolving light.

The Heavenly Emperor Kings—such as the thirty-two Heavenly Emperors (Buddhists call them Heavenly Kings, while Daoists call them Emperors)—and the Perfected Great Sages of the heavens, upon seeing the cloud-script and jade chapters in the void, each employed their pure, luminous, and penetrating insight to recognize them. With their primordial Dao-eyes, they beheld; with their flowery tongues of mystery and clarity, they discussed. The Heavenly Emperor Kings and True Immortals, with ten thousand mouths as one, joined in chanting the cloud-chapters of the Great Cavern. Their voices resounded through the ten thousand heavens, their echoes flowing through the nine earths. The *Jade Scripture* says: “Echoes flow through the cloud encampments,” and also: “The Six Directions are near, the Three Luminaries are not distant—united in sound, their resonance penetrates the nine heavens and nine earths.”

The first three ranks did not mention the earth, speaking only of the heavenly Dao. Only now do the nine earths appear, for yang precedes yin. The nine earths are the nine layered earthly sovereigns:

1. Yuan De
2. Huang De
3. Di De
4. Wang De
5. Ren De
6. Di De
7. Li De
8. Fu De
9. Chang De

Each layer consists of one stratum of soil, one of water, and one of wind. Each has four Earthly Sovereigns governing the four directions, known as the Thirty-Six Earthly Sovereigns. Each has Earthly Father-Mother, Ancestral Rectifiers, Commanding Ministers, Assistants, Generals, and a bureaucracy of two-thousand-stone officials, all managing affairs with myriad subordinates. Above them, the Five Marchmounts and famous mountains hold the reins of authority. Each layer spans ten thousand *li*, yet the True Immortals in the lofty heights of the heavens chant the Cavern Chapters, and their voices descend to the Earth and Water Bureaus below. Thus all-encompassing, it may be called great—for the Primordial Beginning’s one qi circulates beyond Heaven and Earth, reaching without limit.

In the celestial realms, earthly realms, watery realms, and divine abodes, all spirits, without leaving their seats, beheld the dazzling cloud-chapters and heard the celestial hymns with their ears. The celestial realms are governed by the Upper Prime Heavenly Officials, the earthly realms by the Middle Prime Earthly Officials, and the watery realms by the Lower Prime Water Officials. Each of the Three Primes has its own jurisdiction, overseeing the sins and blessings of ghosts, spirits, and humans. Every year, on the first, seventh, and tenth months, they convene to assess and judge—no small matter. Thus it is said: “The Three Primes ride the morning’s return; the Great One’s Upper Prime qi.” From this, we know the first chapter pertains to the Upper Prime’s Nine Treasuries and Four Bureaus. Only the Great Sages of the heavens could chant the Cavern Chapters; the remaining ghosts and spirits of the Three Realms did not stir from their places. They could only see the cloud-chapters dazzling their eyes and briefly hear the celestial hymns with their ears, awakening to the Great Vehicle. For though the people of the heavens enjoy bliss, they do not awaken to the Dao. Now, upon seeing the Cavern Chapters, their hearts’ longing is fulfilled.

All obstacles from a hundred lives are extinguished; the dust of ten thousand kalpas dissolves. Pure qi forms Heaven, turbid qi forms Earth, and harmonious qi forms humans. Yet humans, since time immemorial, have drifted and circled within, unaware of how many tens of thousands of kalpas of dust have passed—sometimes as heavenly beings, sometimes as ghosts and spirits, sometimes as mortals, sometimes divided into male and female, sometimes entering other species. A thousand lives, ten thousand lives, emerging here and sinking there, rising and diving—who can count or compare? As the scripture says: “A hundred lives, ten thousand kalpas.”

Truly, it is so. Fortunate indeed are we today to regain the divine and wondrous principles of spirit and perception—how dare we not advance in trembling reverence, striving to extinguish the causes of past ignorance and unawareness? Once this heart awakens, all transgressions of past lives and this present existence dissolve entirely. If even ghosts may thus attain liberation, how could humans do otherwise?

As the Buddha teaches: *"All sins are like frost and dew—enlightened sunlight can dispel them."* That enlightened sunlight is the single heart-mind.

The Three Paths and Nine Dark Realms, the ten directions’ evil destinies—*the Three Paths are detailed in the middle scroll, extracted from the Five Suffering Realms below*—the Nine Dark Realms are: the East’s Wind and Thunder, the South’s Fire and Obscuration, the West’s Vajra, the North’s Profound Cold, the Center’s Universal Torment, the Northeast’s Cauldron of Boiling Oil, the Southeast’s Bronze Pillars, the Southwest’s Slaughter, and the Northwest’s Fire Chariots. Together, these are called the Nine Dark Hells of the Underworld.

The true immortals of all heavens and earths, along with ghosts and spirits, each hold their own ranks and duties, their positions fixed and orderly. Yet there are also those who administer punishments and rewards, rectifying good and evil: true immortals are governed by the Flowing Gold Fire Bells and Thunder Gods—termed the "Staff, Straightedge, and Law"—while ghosts and spirits are bound by the Heavenly One’s Northern Prison and the *Nüqing Tiaolü* (Statutes of the Green Maiden). For those in the underworld, merits and demerits are examined through the Three Paths, Five Sufferings, Nine Dark Realms, and the great hells of Fengdu. Thus, the ten directions and three realms teem with fierce and malevolent ghostly realms to carry out these judgments, scrutinizing deeds and retributions.

Yet when the radiance of the Luminous Sound reaches them, all ten entanglements, nine knots, six defilements, and seven dusts dissolve in an instant. The *ten entanglements* are the ten great evil sins: disobedience to parents, disloyalty to the sovereign, irreverence toward the Three Treasures, killing, theft, sexual misconduct, greed, anger, ignorance, deceitful speech, false words, harsh speech, and divisive speech. The *nine knots* are: betraying life, betraying wealth, betraying reproach, betraying trust, betraying others, betraying the nation, betraying whippings, betraying strength, and betraying gratitude and righteousness. The *six defilements* are the six senses—eye, ear, nose, tongue, body, and mind—along with their objects: sounds, scents, tastes, touches, and dharmas. The *seven dusts* are joy, anger, sorrow, happiness, love, aversion, and desire.

All ghostly beings of the three realms rely on the radiance of the Great Cavern’s precious pearl and the resonant music of the *Tanchi Gou*, so that all worldly entanglements and defilements dissolve in that very moment—like seeking three years’ worth of mugwort to cure a seven-year illness.

Taking the human body as an example: the *Cang Hu Jie* (Azure Grain) is the millet of the *Scripture of Salvation for All People*; it is the single spark of numinous light within humans. Those who transform and give birth to the heavens are the five limbs, hundred bones, blood, and qi defenses of the human body. The emperors of all heavens chanting in unison are like the turning and flowing of qi and blood with each thought. The ten thousand heavens and nine earths are the human body from crown to sole. The three realms of Heaven, Earth, and Water are the three elixir fields. The dissolution of obstacles and dust is the harmony and smoothness of the qi-body. The Three Paths and Nine Dark Realms are the passions and desires of the kidneys. "All bearing the Luminous Sound" is the utmost reach of the heart-mind. "Dissolving in an instant" is the exhaustion of all defilements.

The true immortals of the heavens above the middle elixir field are the upper deities of the human body, while the hellish ghosts and spirits below it are the lower deities. If one cultivates clarity, these spirits transform into true immortals; if one is defiled by passions and desires, the corpse and filth become hell. Good and evil do not extend beyond this single body—whether one becomes a ghost or an immortal lies within the turn of a palm.

Thereupon, the Great Mystery Dao Father approached the Terrace of Xiao, bowed deeply, and prostrated himself, seeking to receive the jade scriptures of the *Great Cavern Immortal Canon* formed by the precious pearl.

The Great Mystery Dao Father, yearning and advancing, entreated to receive the cloud-scriptures of the Great Cavern. Know that these writings are transformations of one’s own true qi, capable of nurturing the vast and boundless. They fill Heaven and Earth, circulate through the Six Voids, give life to the myriad things, ascend to the Mud Pill Palace, descend to the Bubbling Spring, steam the joints, and refine the yang tally into jade scriptures. Upon completion, they revert to primordial qi, returning to the natural void.

Thus may they guide and transform the beings of humanity and heaven, sparing them from the ten thousand calamities, dissolving all sins, preventing their sinking into suffering, and uniting them in the One Vehicle. *"Loyalty and forbearance are not far from the Dao"*—the Dao of the Master is nothing but loyalty and forbearance. The Dao Father’s heart seeks to extend the self to all under heaven, making all beings one body with himself—truly a mind of universal intent.

*Dao* here is not the same as *Dao* in "to guide." The Dao Father entreated: *"From this moment onward, may we guide and enlighten the beings of the dusty world, humanity, and heaven, as well as all other beings. The ghostly spirits of the three realms have already heard and seen this truth, yet the beings of humanity and heaven have not. Thus, I specially seek to receive these teachings to transform them. If they but hear this scripture, they will be freed from the ten thousand calamities, thousand obstacles, and all karmic sins. From this day forward, they will no longer sink into evil destinies but will all ascend to the fruition of the One Vehicle. The ghostly spirits of the three realms who originally held immortal offices will all rise one rank, just as in the human world where grace is universally bestowed. Thus, both the hidden and the manifest benefit equally. If one can sweep away all root-dusts, remaining unstained by the ten thousand affairs and things, this is called the purity of a single body. When a single body is pure, many bodies are pure; when many bodies are pure, a single world is pure; when a single world is pure, all infinite worlds are pure—how then could there be any talk of beings’ calamities and sins?"*

With these vast vows, he earnestly entreated. Before the Primordial Beginning, the Dao Father labored diligently, advancing to inquire and receive the precious scriptures. The Three Treasures are most noble, and the true Dharma is rarely encountered—one must perform the utmost rites.

The Primordial Heavenly King commanded the Primordial Spirit Great Sage and the Jade Clarity Dao Lord to assume proper dignity, and with their own hands, bestowed the Azure Grain Treasure upon the Great Mystery Dao Father.

The Primordial Spirit Great Sage—sometimes mistakenly called the Eight Sages—is a gross error. How could one not know the supreme nobility of the Three Treasures? Moreover, at the moment of transmission, heart seals heart, mouth conveys and mind responds; the prohibitions are most solemn—who could presume to share their seat? If the Eight Sages were to intrude upon the assembly of the Three Treasures, they would scarcely escape the hurling of the fire-bells.

The Primordial Spirit Great Sage and the Jade Clarity Dao Lord should be recited as one phrase, for the Dao Lord is the primordial spirit of the Primordial Beginning. It is like the youth Sudhana in the *Avataṃsaka Sūtra*, who is but a transformation of Śākyamuni’s own spirit. If one were to place the Eight Sages above the Jade Clarity, how could the Three Treasures retain their nobility? The Dao Lord and the Venerable Lord would then stand beneath the Eight Sages—such a principle is utterly without basis.

In their full dignity of bearing, the Primordial Beginning, though already manifest as the Dao Lord, responded to the Dao Father’s earnest entreaty. Thus, the Primordial Beginning took his seat and commanded the Jade Clarity to transmit the scripture to the Dao Father. Thereupon, all observed the rites of reverent deference—gazing downward in humility, lifting their eyes in awe. “Majesty” denotes what is to be feared; “demeanor,” what is to be emulated. In their every advance and retreat, bow and gaze, the solemnity was thus. Then the Jade Clarity, with his own hands, bestowed the *Azure Grain Treasure of the Great Cavern Sutra* upon the Great Mystery Dao Father. From this, the successive transmission of the Three Worthies is clearly evident—how could there be any separate Eight Sages?

In human terms: the Great Mystery is the single point of true yang and primordial life between the two kidneys. The previous ascent to the Terrace of Emptiness is the rising to the Central Yellow Court. The seeking of the precious pearl is the union of true yang with the ancestral qi. The Primordial Beginning’s command to the Jade Clarity is the intent that the indestructible primordial spirit, through kalpas unbroken, should gather in the Primordial Palace. The bestowal by hand of the treasure signifies that the elixir is already formed.

From this, it is clear that the cultivation of this scripture is none other than the refinement of the great medicine of the golden elixir. The entire practice must be sought within one’s own body; one must not seek it externally and so incur reproach.
