Virtue is what humanity is endowed with, what resides within the nature. Expressed, it becomes the Four Beginnings; concealed, it becomes the Five Constants—this is what is called “illuminating virtue” and “employing virtue.”

Nature is the Dao’s substance; virtue is the Dao’s function. Thus, it is said: “the virtue of nature,” harmonizing the inner and outer Dao. When one possesses pure and complete virtue, there is no excess or deficiency—this is the utmost impartiality and appropriateness of Heavenly Principle.

Preserve the Child, the Spirit within the Spirit.
The *Scripture of Salvation* states: “Within the true is the spirit.” This instructs the adept to cherish this body as one would a newborn child. Turning the light inward and reflecting, gazing within the heart and eyes, in stillness and stability over time, one naturally sees the spirit within the true, merging with it as one body.

The Primordial Destiny generates the natural.
The previous two chapters state: “The Primordial Destiny generates the Grand Beginning.” When the Primordial Destiny Perfected Person first comes into being, it is naturally so, not through forced human effort. This is the Eight of Earth completing Wood in the Eastern Direction, signifying the Primordial of Destiny.

A person’s destiny is received from Heaven. One should preserve and guard it steadfastly, not allowing dissipation to endanger the Heavenly Mandate. Thus, the sage Confucius ate coarse food and drank water; the worthy Yanzi lived in a narrow alley with a bamboo bowl and gourd ladle. This is what it means to “find joy in the Heavenly Mandate” and “know the Heavenly Mandate and thus have no worries.” Even sages and worthies were thus—how much more should others be?

The above Jade Passage’s celestial seal comprises eighty characters. Above, it governs the Supreme Pristine’s Flourishing Music Forbidden Upper Heaven; below, it commands the Seventh Mound’s Virtuous Lord.

The *Mysterious Contract* states: “The wondrous practice of the Grand Clarity’s Eight Sceneries, the Ten Virtues permeating the form—employing virtue to harmonize with the body, advancing virtue on a level path, accomplishing virtue in vastness, the wisdom-virtue inwardly pure, the wisdom-virtue emitting light, the luminous virtue in perfect bloom, the numinous virtue universally responsive, the mysterious virtue in great square, the great virtue natural, the universal virtue aiding and embracing. When the Three Thousand Practices are complete, the True Writ descends and spreads. Wishes fulfilled, the true is accomplished—principle harmonizes with transformation, virtue harmonizes with the Dao. Preserve the Child, the myriad spirits illuminating the Eight Darknesses. Thereby, the Five Qi blend within, the hundred spirits unite.”

The Primordial Heavenly King states: The Twenty-Ninth Jade Chapter of the Grand Cavern, "Heavenly Nine Completes Gold, Nine Radiances’ Wondrous Practice." *Jisi*, *Gengwu*, *Bi*, *Xiaoxu*.

The Great Void is without scenery,
The Great Void, the vast emptiness—utterly devoid of things,
Without light, without form or image,
Silent, desolate—self and other both forgotten.

Moreover, the Lung Spirit is named Haohua Xucheng, corresponding to the Metal Quarter, for the Lord of Peng Chamber resides within the Great Void. Within the rosy clouds lies Peng Chamber. Amidst the iridescent mists, faintly appears the true abode of the spirit. Within the human body lies the Three Peng Chamber—the Three Corpse Spirits—who, on the days of *Gengshen*, *Jiazi*, and one’s own life-destiny, ascend to heaven to report one’s merits and transgressions. Another name is the Spirit Within.

Nine clouds seal the layered gates—
The nine clouds (in another version, the Nine Numinous) are the wondrous qi of the Nine Yangs, enclosing the gates. This signifies the nine orifices sealed, not a speck of dust entering—like the noble one who retreats into seclusion, gathering his treasures without fault, fasting to illumine his virtue with spirit.

The Lord Emperor abides in stillness and profound secrecy—
The Supreme One Emperor dwells in a place of tranquility and deep seclusion, situated above the human head. Without disturbance or disorder, it remains still. As *Laozi* says: "Attain utmost emptiness, preserve profound stillness—all things arise together." All depends on the work of stillness and concentration.

The Eight Perfected of the Radiant Lord—
The Eight Perfected of the Radiant Lord within the gallbladder commune with the Lung Spirit. Though Metal and Wood are separated, here they merge, and the Golden Elixir begins to form. This spirit’s name is Beitai Xuanjing. One should visualize the Azure-Clad Heavenly Worthy and guard the space within the gallbladder.

Above, she carries the Female Supreme One—
Lifting the Supreme One Immortal Maiden into the Muddy Pellet Palace, also called the Supreme One Primordial Lady—the Female One spirit, as previously noted. The Gallbladder Perfected and the Supreme One unite at the human’s Hundred Meetings point, also called the Gate of Myriad Wonders.

The Female and Male merge in the Jade Chamber—
The Female One, Male One, and Emperor One are called the Three Ones. Guarding them has its method, which one must seek within. The Female and Male are Yin and Yang; merging in the Jade Chamber refers to their union within the Cavern Chamber. As *Laozi* says: "Know the male, guard the female." Some may wonder how immortals could engage in such things, yet they fail to realize that Heaven as Father and Earth as Mother—Sun as Yang and Moon as Yin—unite to generate the myriad things. The *Book of Changes* pairs the Joyous Maiden with the Mountain Man in the hexagram *Xian*, signifying mutual resonance. The *Appended Remarks* state: "Heaven and Earth resonate, and the myriad things transform and are born." Thus, the Way of humanity is established in five relationships. The *Classic* says: "Husband and wife have their distinctions," and again: "Among the five universal Ways of the world, husband and wife are one." If a husband is upright and a wife chaste, this is called "ordering the household." The *Hexagram Household* states: "Man and woman in their proper places—this is the great meaning of Heaven and Earth." The *Commentary* says: "Even the foolish and unworthy among husbands and wives can participate in knowing and practicing." For male and female to dwell together is the great human principle. How could solitary Yin or lone Yang ever fulfill the human Way? Yet one must halt at utmost goodness. The Way of the noble one begins with husband and wife, and at its utmost, it scrutinizes Heaven and Earth. The *Book of Changes* begins with *Qian* and *Kun* and emphasizes *Xian* and *Heng*; the *Book of Songs* begins with *Guan Guan* and warns against lewdness; the *Book of Documents* records the rites of marriage and the great wedding feast.

Immortals have never been without this. Liu and Ruan on Tiantai, Liu Yuan on the island—all encountered immortal maidens. Once, a recluse who sold medicines for a living heard that a musician’s daughter, possessed of beauty, was to be married for five hundred thousand coins. The recluse offered seven hundred strings of cash, took the girl home, and after several years, when the matter was complete, her parents missed her and visited. In the mountains, they found a magnificent towered abode. The girl’s husband welcomed and bowed to them, keeping them for several days. After one meal, they were never hungry again. At parting, he gave them five ingots of gold to take home. Later, when their money ran out, they returned but found nothing—only empty mountains. Were these not immortals as husband and wife?

The *Elixir Classic* says:
"To cast aside one’s wife is to vainly sever Yin and Yang;
To cease eating is to futilely empty the stomach and intestines."
The Ancestral Heavenly Master, Master Ge, and Master Xu—did they ever abandon their wives and children before attaining immortality?

The Way of the Golden Elixir requires the Yellow Dame as matchmaker, the joyful union of the Azure-Clad Maiden and the White-Clad Gentleman. Husband sings, wife follows; Yang intones, Yin harmonizes. After ten months, the sacred embryo is complete, and the Infant and the Maiden of Cinnabar suddenly manifest in form. Only then is the proof of the Female and Male merging in the Jade Chamber made clear—yet this is not the husband and wife of the mundane world.

Nine cycles return to seven—
This refers to the celestial tally of fire and timing. In the eleventh month, at the winter solstice, the hexagram *Fu* is practiced as the first return. In the twelfth month, *Lin* is the second return. In the first month, *Tai* is the third return and first reversal. In the second month, *Dazhuang* is the time for bathing. In the third month, *Guai* is the fourth return and second reversal. In the fourth month, *Qian* is the fifth return and third reversal. In the fifth month, *Gou* is the sixth return and fourth reversal. In the sixth month, *Dun* is the seventh return and fifth reversal. In the seventh month, *Pi* is the eighth return and sixth reversal. In the eighth month, *Guan* is the time for bathing. In the ninth month, *Bo* is the ninth return and seventh reversal—two Yin tallying Yang fire, advancing and retreating, drawing and adding. When the seventy-two periods of the celestial cycle are complete, by the tenth month, practicing *Kun*, one sheds the embryo and transforms spiritually.

One Yang arises at *Zi*, two Yangs at *Chou*, three Yangs at *Yin*—thus three Yangs make three returns, and Yang is already flourishing. Therefore, fire arises at *Yin* as the first reversal. By the ninth month, fire is already entombed, hence the seventh reversal. By the tenth month, fire is extinguished and reduced to ashes. Master Cui says: "Within a year, in the twelve hours, wherever the mind reaches, all can be done." He also says: "I urge you not to seek the winter solstice—within your body, a Yang naturally arises." From this, the celestial tally of fire cannot be absent, yet one must not cling to it. The perfected transmit the medicine but not the fire—one must seek an enlightened teacher.

Dispersing form throughout the Six Directions—
Upon reaching this point in the *Grand Cavern Scripture*, one attains the Yang Spirit, which exits and enters, dispersing its radiant forms to wander and feast beyond the Six Directions—beyond Heaven and Earth. One should practice shedding this illusory shell. When first emerging from the shell, one returns after a mile, lest disorder arise.

The Mud-Pill Palace is easily distinguished. Exiting and entering through the Gate of Myriad Wonders, one discerns departure and return. The ancients said: "If one penetrates the Mud-Pill Cavity, why trouble with the minor refinement of the Great Return?" Departing and returning again, when entry and exit become effortless, one may then seize the womb and usurp the dwelling.

The Supreme Perfected’s Ninefold Radiance Wheel—
Nine is the completion number of Metal. The Supreme August Perfected is the true Yang and upright *qi* of the self, generating a wheel of nine-colored radiance to gather the myriad spirits. This is the talisman of the Nine Lights, which corresponds to the ninefold perfection of Heavenly Metal.

The Tenfold *Quan* Script—
*Quan* refers to the ancient immortal Wo Quan, who in the time of Yao consumed pine nuts until his eyes became square. Having attained the Dao, he achieved what the *Scripture of Salvation* calls "ten revolutions to return the numinous." This is the true script of the Five Directions and Five Viscera, interwoven and intricate. Thus, the *Mysterious Contract* states: "Swilling is the fluid of the Five Viscera." The characters of the *Wenchang Grand Cavern*’s original text must not be altered, just as the *Numinous Treasure Scripture*’s *Danlou Ahui* or the *Sūrangama Sūtra*’s *śamatha, samāpatti,* and *dhyāna* are not to be changed. If they could be altered, translators of scriptures would render them in vernacular Chinese, but one must follow the ancient texts.

Preserve the primordial *qi* and ensure its flow—
Protect the Three *Qi* of Mystery, Origin, and Beginning within the adept’s body, allowing them to circulate without obstruction. The human body’s blood,荣 *qi*, and卫 *qi* must flow freely and harmoniously to ensure well-being, free from deep-seated illness. If stagnation occurs, other disorders arise, and preservation fails.

The Five *Qi* govern the central *Jie*—
The *qi* of the Five Phases—Metal, Wood, Water, Fire, and Earth—coalesce into the *Canghu Jie*. *Li* is the Dao; *zhong* is the Great Root. Together, they form virtue, nature, and life. When expressed externally, they become emotion; when moderated, they achieve harmony. Harmony is the attainment of the Dao, and the Dao and virtue are unified as one. Thus, timely application is fitting. The Five *Qi* governing the center—here the script is suddenly revealed within.

Transformation soars to the Upper Clarity—
One may undergo boundless transformations, unfathomable as yin and yang. With yin *qi* as the Jade Maiden and yang *qi* as the Immortal Youth, dragons and phoenixes of radiant clouds emerge from one’s own body, allowing one to ride them and ascend into the true realm of the Upper Clarity.

Three Thousand Deeds transcend all—
The Three Thousand Meritorious Acts and Eight Hundred Virtues must be perfected and transcended. Even those with great hidden merits—such as saving thousands of lives in a single effort—may achieve this. When the great merit is complete, one stands as a minister attending the Three Realms.

Many dissipate their essence and *qi* in pursuit of wealth, status, and sensual pleasures. When the body and life are suddenly abandoned, even wives, children, and closest kin turn away in disgust. Where then is the love of the bridal chamber and wedding candles? Only the turning of the karmic wheel remains—how can one hope to bear the Ninefold Radiance Wheel and witness the wondrous deeds of the Supreme Perfected?

The above jade script of celestial seal, eighty characters in all, governs above the Supreme Void of the Peerless Constant Fusion Heaven and rules below the Eighth Rampart of the Great Wind Marsh Earthly Sovereign. The *Mysterious Contract* states: "The Supreme Perfected’s Ninefold Radiance and the wondrous deeds of the Tenfold *Quan*—dual cultivation of the dwelling and the embryo, the spirit and the soul, the viscera and the bowels, the numinous and the primordial, the floral and the mountain, the primordial life and the divine—along with the *qi* of Brahma, the Beginning, the Primordial, and the Mysterious, the Dao *qi* governing the center, the perfected transforming into the true and the divine—when the Three Thousand Deeds are complete," the script swills the noble *qi*, naturally revolving tenfold to return the numinous, and the myriad *qi* ascend as immortals.

The Tenfold *Quan* represents the wondrous deeds of the Supreme Perfected: Heaven One, Earth Two; Heaven Three, Earth Four; Heaven Five, Earth Six; Heaven Seven, Earth Eight; Heaven Nine, Earth Ten. The script is the literary composition of the Tenfold *Quan* of Heaven and Earth, the jade fluid of the essence of the Five Viscera and Six Bowels within the human body. Thus, it is called "swilling the noble *xi*."

The Primordial Heavenly Sovereign said: "The *Wenchang Grand Cavern*’s Jade Script, Chapter Thirty: Earth’s Tenfold Perfection, the Ten Illuminations of Wondrous Deeds." *Xinwei, Renshen, Lü, Tai.*

The Supreme Mystery’s Nine *Qi* above—
The Three *Qi* of the Supreme Mystery, Supreme Origin, and Supreme Beginning reside above the Nine *Qi*. The concluding verse states: "The Supreme Mystery initiates the Ten Illuminations; wondrous deeds ascend to the Ten Perfected." It is also said: "The Supreme Mystery’s capital is the auspicious *qi* presided over by the Elder of the Nine *Qi*."

The mist revolves amidst the Supreme Splendor—
The Three *Qi* unite in virtue, and the Nine *Qi* converge as one, forming clouds and mist that revolve within the Supreme Void. *Taihui* is the name of a palace; other versions mistakenly render it as *Taixu* (Supreme Void). Here, the mysterious *qi* emerges above the Nine *Qi*.

The divine radiance shines upon the empty peak—
The divine and precious radiance is the numinous light, formless and intangible, emitting resplendent brilliance beyond the vast emptiness, in the ethereal and indistinct. In humans, the spirit’s radiance shines forth from the eyes. The "empty peak" refers to the head and face.

The Five Paths illuminate the Three Heavens—
The Five Paths are the Five Elders, shining brightly above the Three Heavens, their audience with the Emperor adorned in resplendent crowns. The Great Elixir’s Three Flowers gather at the summit; the Five *Qi* return to the Origin. The Three Heavens above are the Three Fields within the human body.

Riding the light, ascending the Absolute Empyrean—
Mounting the light-chariot to ascend the layered heavens, one reaches the Absolute Empyrean. This describes the Purple River Carriage conveying [essence] to the summit of Kunlun. As previously stated: "Riding the light amidst the morning radiance"—the meaning is the same. The Absolute Empyrean is unbound above and unsupported below.

Riding the wind, sweeping away stagnant spirits—
The immortal’s body is light, clad in a six-*zhu* robe, driving a flying wheel or feathered chariot, all of which can ride the wind and *qi*. "Sweeping away stagnant spirits" refers to the potent winds and vast *qi* within the Three Realms, where the Five Emperors and Great Demons command the demonic hordes of the heavens, blocking the paths. Only when great merit is complete and the Emperor observes and approves, when demon kings welcome and escort, when the Flowing Gold Fire Bell and the Five Elders open the way, may one ascend. Likewise, when the cultivator’s true *qi* is robust and wisdom-power unobstructed, the twin passes of the spine, the Heavenly Pillar, and the Jade City naturally open, leaving no stagnant spirits.

In the midst of the sun revolves a pearl—
Within the Central Palace, the Cinnabar Prime Lord, named Divine Revolving Pearl, ever turns in the Central Palace like the sun’s precious pearl. One tradition holds there is a revolving pearl within; another, that the pearl revolves within the sun—these do not align.

The Queen Mother of the West’s *wogu* method:
Visualize within the heart a sun as large as a *Chongning* coin, revolving with the heat of fire, descending to the Bubbling Spring, ascending to the Mud Pill, passing through the Three Palaces. After a thousand days, one may project the spirit.

The Lord of Life who governs the sun’s center and the Central Elder Lord of Life, together with the Divine Revolving Pearl, all guard the heart’s spirits. Among the myriad spirits of the heart, these are the most essential.

Govern the heart to enter stillness and tranquility.
With right principle govern these heart-mind thoughts, rendering them pure, settled, and undisturbed by phenomena. The *Yuanjue Jing* says: "By clarifying all thoughts, the movements of awakened knowing cease." The *Yijiao Jing* says: "Restrain it to one point, and nothing will remain undone." That one point is the clarified heart-mind.

The preceding speaks of Heaven; this speaks of the heart—for this heart is the Heavenly Heart. Cultivate within, and the without will respond. Without unity within, one cannot govern the without; without order without, one cannot nurture the within. Nurturing within and without in mutual accord, movement and stillness in resonant response—this is the fundamental purport of the *Great Cavern*. The Daoist scriptures only extinguish the moving heart-mind, not the illuminating heart-mind—this is likewise so.

Uniting the Three and Five Palaces:
Metal and Water share a single source, the One and Five; Fire and Wood share a common homeland, the Three and Five. The Central Palace of *wu* and *ji* unites the Three and Five, where the Four Images and Five Phases intermingle.

Formerly, the Daoist adept Xu and Zhang Huiming encountered the Right Radiant Lady of Mount Nanyue, who transmitted the Way of uniting the Three and Five. Both attained liberation through the corpse and became spirit immortals. Those who practice the Way of uniting the Three and Five will naturally escape the Three Wretched Realms and Five Sufferings, ascending to the Three-Five Heavenly Palaces, where they gain the joy and freedom of Heaven. Though they may live for aeons, brushing past stones, they will not cling to such joy, but advance in true cultivation toward the supreme realm.

Transforming through countless millions of years—
Living for countless millions of years, forever without decline, they accumulate the blessings of heavenly beings. Like an arrow shot into empty space, when its force is spent, it falls back down. But those who cultivate the Way of the *Great Cavern* Golden Elixir ascend directly to the ultimate position—how could they ever revolve in the cycle of rebirth?

"Felling the womb-tree’s earthly root"—
This line bears repeating, for the womb and embryo are matters of utmost weight, without which there can be no generation or transformation. Here, earth’s pairing is not in error: the primal yellow qi coalesces as the womb’s root, adhering to the spleen, all governed by earth’s generative number.

"Severing forever the corpse-blood’s root."
The ninefold ancestors and sevenfold forebears are all pervaded by the Dao’s qi, dissolving the karmic knots of past lives’ accumulated obstructions. The womb-tree and blood-root are metaphors for deep-rooted, firmly anchored bonds—yet through the merit of the *Great Cavern’s* precious scripture, all are felled and severed forever.

"The seven ancestors disperse their accumulated stagnations."
When forebears in past generations clashed in conflict, their curses took form as oral spells at spirit altars and temple shrines, entangling descendants in lawsuits, summons, and ancestral grievances. These stagnations, sealed in the hidden chambers of the unseen, could not be undone—until now, upon hearing the *Great Cavern’s* jade scripture, they are instantly released.

"Returning blossoms to the Dark and Mysterious."
The good sprout reverses its course, flourishing anew in the Dark and Mysterious Garden of the north, the land where Heaven’s One gives birth, the origin of the Three Powers. It is as when a person returns to the root in the Lower Prime, for the Sea of Qi governs the entire body.

"From the ten thousand qi, the ten thousand spirits are born."
The human body’s qi number in the tens of thousands—Mencius spoke of the vast qi filling heaven and earth. Yet if one fails to honor and secure the root, indulging in wine and lust, the qi gradually scatters. By middle and later years, it dwindles to mere thousands, leaving the spirits weary and strength exhausted. But if one knows and nurtures it, the ten thousand spirits are reborn.

The *Immortals’ Transmission* records that Master Wang of the Three Ones at Mount Lu’s Great Peace Palace dreamed of a divine messenger who declared: "The Supreme Emperor commands you to dwell in the Golden Flower Grotto-Heaven. He bestows upon you a single elixir pill to restore your spirit and replenish your primordial qi." The next day, he ascended. Thus we know: without the fullness of spirit and qi, one cannot become an immortal.

The *Classic* states: "Body, hair, and skin are received from father and mother—dare one not preserve them? This is the beginning of filial piety." Parents give life whole; a child should return it whole. Yet many, through wine, lust, wealth, and qi, damage their bodies. In the hidden courts of the unseen, they cannot escape judgment—how then can they hope for immortality?

"Equal the immortals, become an immortal king."
See the worthy and think to equal them.

Having walked shoulder to shoulder with the perfected immortals and accomplished the immortal Dao, one is acclaimed and upheld by all immortals—hence the title "Immortal King." Even among immortals, there are those who don the regalia of kingship. The office of Wenchang, the stellar immortal, attains its utmost nobility at this stage.

The Supreme Mystery initiates the Ten Illuminations,
The Supreme Mystery unfolds the Ten Illuminated Wondrous Practices to receive and deliver those with karmic affinity.
The Supreme Mystery is the progenitor of the Three Qi, giving birth to heaven, earth, and the myriad things. Here, the number is complete, and with the fulfillment of the Ten Illuminated Wondrous Practices, one ascends to the Ten Perfected.
The Wondrous Practices ascend to the Ten Perfected.
When the Ten Illuminated Wondrous Practices reach perfection, one attains the rank of Supreme Mystery Perfected.
The Ten Illuminations and Ten Perfected—ten being the number of earth’s completion—are thus made clear. In the *River Chart*, this is the complete number. The six unbroken lines of pure yang form Qian, which pertains to the radiance of metal. Then one perceives all realms and things as illusory, all affairs as dreams, principles and dharmas as eye floaters or empty blossoms, and all conditioned actions as reflections in a mirror. Thus, one regards sounds and sights as enemies, honors and ranks as dung and dirt, and life and death as morning and evening. In responding to matters and engaging with beings, one weighs with emptiness and balances with equanimity—only then does one verify the Supreme Mystery’s Wondrous Practices.

The above jade scripture in celestial seal comprises ninety characters, governing above the Great Release Jade Exaltation Ascendant Heaven and presiding below over the Eighth Rampart’s Lord of Blessing and Virtue.

The *Mysterious Covenant* states: The Supreme Mystery’s Ten Illuminated Wondrous Practices and Ten Perfected are:
Perfected Essence, complete;
Perfected Qi of the Mysterious Pearl;
Perfected Spirit of Mysterious Power;
Perfected Nature of Mysterious Penetration;
Perfected Unity of the Primordial;
Perfected Life of Mysterious Wonder;
Perfected Form of Mysterious Radiance;
Perfected Virtue, complete;
Perfected Dao of the Mysterious Cavern;
Perfected Response, complete.

The Supreme Mystery’s Ten Perfected—wondrous practices and ascetic conduct—are the celestial horizontal script. They firmly root the myriad practices, encircle the six positions, and have ascended to the Wondrous Practices. The Great Complete Form takes shape, qi and essence refine into the Purple Gold of endless life—thus is the Supreme Mystery Perfected.

The Primordial Heavenly King declares: The thirty-first jade scripture of the Great Cavern of Wenchang corresponds to the two trigrams Qian and Dui, whose tone is akin to metal.
*Guiyou*, *Jiaxu*, *Pi*, *Tongren*.
Beyond the Utmost Clarity’s Absolute Radiance...

Above the Grand Clarity lies the Highest Clarity—thus it is called "beyond the Absolute Radiance," which is none other than the Crimson Palace within the human body.

This scripture corresponds to the two trigrams Qian and Dui. Qian’s image stands loftily above, hence "beyond the Absolute Radiance." Qian begins by bestowing beauty and benefit upon all under Heaven, yet it does not speak of the magnitude of its bounty—how vast indeed! The *Great Cavern Immortal Scripture* universally nourishes the ten thousand existences without boasting of its power, whereas other scriptures proclaim that recitation alone yields such-and-such rewards, thereby vaunting their efficacy. Qian’s essence is firm, strong, pure, and unceasing; those who study the Dao must emulate Qian’s ceaseless vigor, preserving it continuously as if ever-present, to achieve eternal completion.

The Eight August Ones revolve through the Nine Heavens.
The Eight August Ones are the eight trigrams; the Nine Heavens are the nine palaces, as seen in the earlier Luo River Diagram’s numbers—here they need not be repeated.

Qian’s primal power employs the nine, yet Heaven’s virtue cannot be made its head. "Primal, prosperous, beneficial, and steadfast" are Qian’s virtues—thus it is said to "revolve through the Nine Heavens," signifying unyielding self-strengthening.

The Eight August Ones—Lord Lao revolving above the Nine Heavens—are the Eight Spirit Kings. "August" and "king" are one. The vastness of Heaven and Earth, how could it depart from the two qi of yin-softness and yang-firmness? The ceaseless revolution of these two qi—how could it stray from the convergence of the One Primal? Thus, the greatness of Heaven and Earth encompasses all principles, yet its essence is but One. The revolution of the One Primal—spring, summer, autumn, winter, crescent, full, waning, and new moons—never errs by even a single breath.

The *Book of Changes* states: "Observe the spirit-like Dao of Heaven, and the four seasons do not deviate. The sage establishes teaching through the spirit-like Dao."

Verily, in the alchemy of the Elixir, it is termed "fire and timing," corresponding to the Great Yang’s yearly revolution through the celestial circuit. With three hundred days of practice complete, one may ingest and refine it.

The Dark and Vast Mysterious Emperor-Son—refer to Chapter Two of the preceding scroll—is the Dark and Vast Profound Void, also called the Dark and Vast Nonexistent. The soul of the August One ascends as the Emperor-Son. These two spirits jointly guard the lower Cinnabar Field. The visualization method: the Dark and Vast Black Emperor-Son is crimson.

They carry the person within this vision. The Dark and Vast and the Emperor-Son, these two, can uplift the person within this vision, symbolizing the indestructibility of one’s Dharma-body through kalpas. By this uplifting, one remains perpetually wakeful and unobscured, free from the veils of selfish desire and the incursions of love and aversion.

At dawn, ascend to the Chamber of the Heavenly Elder. At midnight, the Zi hour, rise to the Palace of the Heavenly Elder. As recorded in the *Seven Stars Spirit Incantation Scripture of the Heavenly Elder Sovereign*, this corresponds to the liver. The incantation: "The sun rises in the east, radiant with great light." This is the Mao hour, when true qi is transmitted to the liver.

At dusk, feast in the Court of Golden Splendor. In the evening, wander and banquet in the Court of Golden Splendor, which is the lungs, representing the Dui trigram. One version reads "Golden Splendor Convenience," which is erroneous. At the You hour, true qi is transmitted to the lungs. At the feast, one drinks golden nectar and jade fluid, consuming intersecting pears and fiery jujubes.

With a feathered standard, summon the Great One. Using a feathered banner as a tally, summon the Great One Sovereign—see prior annotations. The Great One resides in the head, holding the talisman to summon the ten thousand qi and ten thousand spirits of the inner landscape. Spirits follow qi in motion, all gathering and congealing to pay homage to the Great One Sovereign.

With brocade banners, summon the ten thousand spirits. "Spirit" is that which subtly pervades the ten thousand things. Throughout this chapter, brocade banners and flags serve as instruments to attract the true and summon the numinous. Things gather by kind, and beings assemble by group; thus, feathered standards and brocade banners each summon their own kind.

Fortify my Six Transcendent Palaces. The Six Palaces: the large intestine is the Palace of the Minister of State; the small intestine, the Palace of Primal Yang; the gallbladder, the Palace of the Orchid Terrace; the bladder, the Palace of Supreme Harmony; the stomach, the Palace of Supreme Simplicity; and the Triple Burner, the Palace of the Ultimateless. The sage rides the six dragons to govern Heaven. Heaven circulates the six qi to regulate the myriad beings; humans harmonize the six bowels to resist external pathogens. Thus, it is said: "Strengthen the qi of the five viscera and six bowels within the omen-body." When firm, they form the Six Transcendent Palaces; when scattered, they become the Six Cavernous Malevolent Demons, mutually harming and destroying, all due to the disturbances of emotion and desire, which corrupt the Six Caverns and Six Heavens.

Strike down the roots of the womb and embryo. Sever the roots of the womb and embryo, preventing their proliferation. These dead roots must be entirely eradicated. Only when the dead roots are cut off can the living roots grow, flourish, and thrive, becoming a lush forest of merit and success.

Unbind the knots of the seven ancestors, allowing them to ascend to the heavenly halls and enjoy blissful non-action. One version reads "unbind the knots, the seven ancestors live," which is a confused and disordered phrasing. Simply cultivate a mind turned toward goodness, and the seven ancestors will naturally ascend to Heaven.

Dispel calamities and pacify the nine lineages. Dissolve the misfortunes of the nine lineages, bringing them peace. When the six yin are exhausted, the nine yang begin to form. The *Book of Changes* states: "Vigilant as if facing danger, there will be no blame." When one attainment becomes eternal, continuous as if ever-present, calamities will naturally dissipate, sinking deep beneath the nine earths.

The Crimson City and the Elixir Terrace Maiden—some say the Crimson City is the Crimson and Azure Sea Palace of the Sun Sovereign’s Dark Continent, located beneath the Nine Empyreans, called the First Empyrean. The Elixir Terrace and Purple Mansion are the Palace of Yang Brightness, where many jade pavilions of female immortals reside, such as the Silver Palace of Yang the Supreme.

According to the *Classic of Mountains and Seas*, the four greatest mountains in the Eastern Sea—Mount Penglai, Mount Fusang, Mount Fangzhang, and Mount Canglang—have beneath them the Three Islands and Ten Continents: first, the Dark Continent; second, Yingzhou; third, Zuzhou; fourth, Juquzhou; fifth, Yanzhou; sixth, Linzhou; seventh, Liuzhou; eighth, Changzhou; ninth, Yuanzhou; and tenth, Shengzhou. Later in this chapter, it speaks of the Dark Continent’s Three Ferries, the Cang Terrace’s Flying Feather Wheel, and ascending Fusang—all within the Eastern Sea’s domain. Those who attain the Dao inevitably pass through here, shedding their illusory bones, receiving ranks and robes, and then ascending to the heavenly realms to pay homage to the Three Pure Ones.

Support the omen and enter the Golden Gate. Qian resides in the northwest, belonging to Metal, and is the Gate of Heaven—hence, the Golden Gate. This maiden of the Dui trigram assists my body in ascending together through the Golden Gate. One version reads "summon with talismans to enter the Golden Gate," which is erroneous. The gate of the lord of the world is also called the Golden Gate.

The Moon Mother, Numinous Plain Orchid—Dui is the trigram of the moon. The moon goddess is the essence of Great Yin, named Numinous Plain Orchid (or Tranquil Plain Orchid, which is erroneous). The correct Dharma name for the moon incantation is Numinous Plain Orchid. The *Dipper Scripture* states: "She governs the netherworld and presides over the sources of water."

Guard and seal the Gate of Dead Qi. The essence of the moon constantly guards the lower origin, sealing the Gate of Dead Qi. These four lines all pertain to the Scripture of the Feminine One. The Elixir Terrace Maiden, the yang spirit, desires the person’s ascent, while Tranquil Plain Orchid, the yin spirit, can obstruct the Gate of Death for the person, channeling the flow of living qi.

From this day, dead qi is cut off. Having sealed the Gate of Death, dead qi is severed. Confucius said: "Without knowing life, how can one know death?" The Dao of the Great Cavern knows both life and death, just as the *Appended Judgments* of the *Book of Changes* states: "Trace beginnings to their ends, and thus understand the discourse on death and life."

From here, the springs of life extend. The shores of the springs of life may be glimpsed and crossed. The Buddha said: "The patience of non-arising—if there is no arising, how can there be ceasing? If one comprehends non-arising, one must seek liberation, releasing all dharmic bonds, directly attaining purity in the ten thousand conditions, with nothing to be grasped."

The ten thousand spirits and ten thousand qi become immortals. Clouds move and rain descends, shaping the myriad forms. Thus, the ten thousand qi give rise to the ten thousand spirits. The immortals of the ten thousand qi are the ten thousand spirits returning to oneness, as in the Supreme Ultimate Diagram’s generation of the ten thousand things—this is the root of Heaven and Earth’s ceaseless generation.

Ascending beyond, one attains the position of the True King. As the Qian Dao transforms and evolves, each fulfills its nature and destiny. Thus, transcending and surpassing the barrier of life and death, one verifies and ascends to the rank of the Great Cavern True King. The previous chapter spoke of becoming an Immortal King; through further cultivation, one now reaches the position of the True King of Longevity.

The ten perfections of wondrous practice are complete. The "ten perfections" refer to sincerity without falsehood. Sincerity is the Way of Heaven; the pursuit of sincerity is the Way of humanity. With utmost sincerity unceasing, and unceasing thus enduring, one attains the ten perfections of wondrous practice, fully realizing the ten perfections of wondrous practice from the previous chapter.

The Supreme Mystery unites with the luminous yang. Above the nine heavens, yin qi does not intrude; within the nine earths, yang light is forever obstructed. Thus, the Supreme Mystery qi within my body converges with the luminous yang heaven. In a later chapter, the union of my body with luminous yang shares this same meaning.

The Supreme Great Cavern Honored One. Here, one meets the Great Personage. The Great Cavern Emperor Honored One of oneself manifests—this is the noble one of the limitless and supreme rank, equal in glory to Heaven and forever free from decline. All these belong to the Great Brahma Heaven of the formless realm above.

One qi harmonizes with the dragon’s radiance. Qian is a yang entity, hence the dragon serves as its metaphor—terms like "hidden dragon," "manifest dragon," and "flying dragon" all arise from the primordial one qi. If one cultivates the Great Cavern of the self with benevolence, then one’s qi and virtue unite with the strength of Qian, ceaselessly striving. Dui represents joy and delight, an ineffable celebration. Through cultivation to this point, the yin lines are entirely shed, transforming the mortal form into a body of pure yang and purple gold. Spirit embraces qi, and qi embraces spirit; essence and spirit are refined and luminous, qi and pulse harmonious and smooth. Like the joyous union of husband and wife, like the tender attachment of mother and child, one awaits the moment of spiritual transformation.

The above jade verse in celestial script comprises one hundred twenty characters, governing above the Dragon Transformation Brahma Liberation Heaven and presiding below over the Eighth Rampart’s Lord of Vision and Virtue.

The *Mysterious Contract* states: When the essence and qi of one’s body are fully refined into the six positions of purple gold, having ascended to the perfection of wondrous practice and the boundless longevity of the Supreme Mystery Realized One, one turns the light inward to open and deliver the root of the embryo. The seven mysteries and nine ancestors are all released from karmic entanglements, debts and disputes severed, the gate of death sealed. Those of shared qi and shared root are revived, their life-springs nourished, their myriad spirits extended. Together they transcend to the True King, harmonizing the myriad qi, their wondrous practices all complete. All are named the Supreme Mystery’s Heaven of Luminous Yang. I alone ascend beyond, verifying the Great Cavern Honored Emperor of the One Dragon Radiance, styled the Supreme Mystery of the Unsurpassed.

*Jade Purity’s Limitless Total True Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture of the Immortals*, Scroll Nine. (Here, a "Heaven" character may be missing.)

Jade Purity’s *Limitless Total True Wenchang Great Cavern Scripture of the Immortals*, Annotated Scroll Ten
Annotations by Zhongyangzi Wei Qi of Mount Penglai in Eastern Shu

The Primordial Heavenly King states:
The thirty-second jade chapter of the *Wenchang Great Cavern* corresponds to the *Zhen* and *Xun* trigrams, its tone belonging to Wood.

*Yihai*, *Bingzi*, *Dayou*, *Qian*.
The Eastern Florescence emits its first radiance,
The Lofty Morn illumines the Upper Clarity.
The Judgment Office of the Eastern Florescence and the Square Cauldron Palace is also the abode of the Heavenly Worthy Who Saves from Suffering—a land revering benevolence and treasuring life. Here, the Nine Dragon Talismanic Commands deliver the shades of the dead. "Emits its first radiance" refers to the initial arising of the single yang line, like the sun’s ascent. "Lofty Morn" is also called the Azure Lad, named Morning Sun. As the sun ascends high, it must illumine the true realm of the Upper Clarity. This signifies that when human true qi gathers in the heart’s palace, it issues forth from the liver’s viscera, then begins its transmission, reaching the Crimson Palace by midday.

Resplendent, the round pearl glows with misty haze;
The radiant brilliance shines resplendently within the azure-gemmed pearl, its misty vapors thick and luxuriant. All these are metaphors for the qi of the heart-pearl: the spirit’s light, perfectly round and luminous, penetrating the eight chambers, emptying the five aggregates, a treasure of purity and clarity.

Brightly gleams the purple radiance.
"Brightly" means luminous. Sunlight generates purple radiance, shining with clarity. The liver’s spirit, Dragon Mist Containing Brightness Lord, corresponds to the liver—this is Wood’s resonance. Both *Zhen* and *Xun* belong to the East’s Wood, above corresponding to Jupiter, below governing the liver.

The Seven Morns return to the Emperor’s seat;
The sun spirit named Seven Morns Returning ascends to the Heavenly Emperor’s mat, for the Emperor emerges from *Zhen* and is arrayed in *Xun*. Lesser Yang is *Zhen*, ascending in *Xun* to join *Qian*, the position of six yang lines in perfect fullness—hence, the Emperor’s seat.

The Five Elders fly the jade carriage.
When the Most High depart, the Five Elders must open the way, the host of immortals flanking the chariot. True immortals and cultivators are likewise attended—these are the transformations of the five qi.
As the *Scripture of Salvation* states: "The Five Emperors serve as guards; the Three Realms bow in reverence." The same applies here.

The Great One, King within the radiance;
The Great One resides atop the head, sovereign within the radiance—see earlier annotations on the "person within the radiance."
It is also said: "King within the radiance." One should esteem the head as the body’s leader, thus addressing this spirit as king.

The Controller of Destiny gathers the ten thousand spirits.
The flying jade talisman-carriage summons the ten thousand spirits, all riding the *Xun* wind. Thus, to summon spirits is to gather wind. The Controller of Destiny dwells in the heart, governing all spirits—the heart is the master of thunder.
The *Thunder Scripture* states: "If the heart-fire does not flare, Deng Jun does not roar; if the liver-spirit does not rage, Xin Shu does not stir; if the intent-spirit does not arise, the messengers do not move."
For the liver belongs to *Zhen* and *Xun* as Yi Wood, while the heart-fire activates it—this is the image of striking and drumming. Thus, it can gather and command the ten thousand spirits.
Moreover, *Zhen* is thunder, manifesting in humans as sound; *Xun* is wind, manifesting as breath and qi. Hence, the eight trigrams represent the body.

Buoyantly amid the clouds and waves,
Water converges in the southeast’s *Xun* region. This describes how, at this time, true qi steams and vaporizes, essences and fluids irrigate, and one’s original spirit surges upward. The two trigrams oppose each other in the primordial arrangement, their image being "thunder and wind clashing"—thus they stir and animate the myriad transformations.

Silently gazing upon the Mud-Pill Palace.
Following the *Xun* wind, the noble one issues commands and acts, resolutely assuming a stern countenance, standing at the center of the world. Summoning the Three Officials and Five Peaks, the Mud-Pill Palace’s gates stand at the highest summit. "Silently" means without sound; "gazing" means looking back.

Seven revolutions summon the Three Officials;
Seven revolutions of the true talismanic command summon the Three Officials—within the person, these are the spirits of the three fields. Advancing and retreating benefit from martial vigor; human integrity requires awe-inspiring might. If governance is not smooth, only wind and thunder suffice to startle and rouse the myriad beings.

The Northern Lord bows and proceeds.
The North takes precedence, initiating the Five Directions. Following the season, one ascends the original spirit, rising from the kidneys and navel, traversing the five viscera, and mounting to the Mud-Pill. The true spirits of the three barriers and five viscera all attend and ascend together.

The Five Peaks respond to the command and arrive;
The Five Peaks respond to the summons and come—all five qi mutually resonate and assemble. Thunder and lightning wield the power of life and death, the offices of rewarding good and punishing evil. Thus, when thunder moves and wind flies, the myriad spirits gather—how could any delay be tolerated?

Erasing death, inscribing long life.
The Three Officials and Five Peaks all strike out the registers of death, inscribing the character for life. The two images inverted form the *Yi* hexagram. The *Appended Judgments* state: "The noble one, seeing goodness, moves toward it; having faults, reforms them." This is what it means. For humans, it is a matter of putting it into practice.

Three invocations of the *Zhen*-Spirit Talisman;
Heaven possesses the *Zhen*-Spirit Talisman, which commands the qi of life and subdues demonic essences.
Nothing agitates the myriad beings faster than wind; nothing stirs them faster than thunder. Thus, thunder holds the power of life and death: like thunder-water, it can split open the husks of fruits, grasses, and trees—this is its life-giving aspect. When thunder moves and wind races, cutting away calamities and chaos—this is its death-dealing aspect.
Thus, this chapter’s opening and closing lines state: "Erasing death, inscribing long life; mystically dissolving great demonic essences"—demonstrating the handle of life and death. In the earlier "Primordial Beginning and Great Ultimate" chapter, the *Zhen*-Spirit appears three times; see the detailed annotations above.

Mystically dissolving great demonic essences.
The *Xun* Gate is the Divine Empyrean Palace, the source of wind and thunder. It can wondrously dissolve the great demons of the Six Heavens, preventing their disturbances. Those who study immortality must tremble at *Zhen*’s coming—"thunder startles a hundred leagues"—all should fearfully cultivate and reflect.

Seven ancestors born in the Hall of Blessings;
The seven ancestors of the nine mysteries are all born in the great Hall of Blessings in heaven, roaming carefree—this is the fortune of heavenly beings. When their fortune is exhausted, they do not descend to be reborn among strange kinds. Cultivating the *Wenchang Great Cavern* is the supreme Dharma-gate, reaching the Three Clarities’ realm.

The Mysterious Flower Preserves the Yellow Tranquility.
By the Mysterious Flower preserving and nurturing the Yellow Tranquility Child within the spleen and stomach, one ensures it never declines or falls—this is the Way of long life and enduring vision.

The two images unite to form the Hexagram *Heng*. The *Appended Judgments* say: "The sage abides long in the Way, and all under heaven is transformed and enriched." The *Judgment* states: "Heaven bestows, earth produces—together they move with the seasons." Those who cultivate the *Great Cavern* are not bound by time; wherever they dwell, with a single thought unmoving, the qi of heaven and earth arises. Its generation begins at *Fu* and ends at *Kun*; one ascent and one descent make a single celestial cycle. The qi of a full year is refined within a single moment—within the body, heaven and earth’s creative transformations unfold.

The right section contains ninety celestial seal-script characters of this jade chapter, which above stabilize the *Tai Ji*, *Ping Yu*, *Jia Yi*, and Heaven, and below govern the Eighth Rampart’s Lord of Blessings and Virtue.

The *Mysterious Covenant* states: "The seven ancestors and nine mysteries ascend to the heavenly halls; the myriad generations of ancestors and the Mysterious Flower are born together. Within, the Yellow Tranquility is preserved, and all kin ascend, all recorded in the immortal ranks and enrolled in *Nanchang*. The karmic debts of ten thousand generations—clan graves, tomb disputes, and the ledgers of exiled ghosts—are all pacified at once with the *Great Cavern Sutra of Immortals*. The earth’s roots and evil roots are severed and extinguished; the Way is unified, and long life arises naturally."

The Primordial Heavenly King says: "The thirty-third jade chapter of the *Wenchang Great Cavern* manifests the two hexagrams *Kan* and *Li*, the Way of *Ji Ji*. It is transformed by the mysterious qi of the *Tai Qing* immortal realm. The Supreme Thearch’s Nine Elders’ Capital..."

The moistener of the myriad things—none is more moistening than water. Thus, of all the manifold kinds, none does not rely upon it for life. Water flows through the earth’s midst; the Yangzi, Yellow, Huai, and Han rivers all pay homage to the sea, each governed by its appointed overseers. Therefore, the Fusang Great Thearch and the Nine Qi Heavenly Lords of the East jointly administer the Water Palace, which serves as the grand assembly of all watery domains. Now, the origin of water arises in the north: Heaven’s One gives birth to it, Earth’s Six completes it, and it emerges from the *Kan* position. Thus, this chapter is represented by the hexagram *Kan*. The *Book of Changes* says: “Water repeatedly flows into the abyss; the noble one, by constant virtue, practices and teaches affairs.”

**Inspecting Immortals Ascend Fusang.**
When the immortal registers are examined, those who have attained the Dao ascend to Mount Fusang in the Eastern Sea. It is said that human essence-qi is born in the kidneys and transmitted to the liver, then to the heart’s palace. Thus, below it is said: “The divine network and essence-qi within the human body are like water flowing through heaven and earth.”

**Sevenfold Summons to the Heavenly Thearch.**
The Heavenly Thearch is the Jade Thearch, summoned by the mandate of the Primordial Beginning to the Muddy Pellet Palace in the brain’s central palace. All merits and transgressions of the Three Realms’ true immortals and worldly people are presented to the Jade Thearch by the Three Officials and Five Peaks.

**The Controller of Destiny Rides the Divine Network.**
This represents the hexagram *Li*, which in humans is the heart. The heart’s spirit rides its divine network to ascend and pay homage. The heart is the abode of spirit, thus possessing a guiding principle. *Li* is the image of radiant clarity, so the heart-spirit delights in illuminating and discerning affairs.

**The Five Peaks Open the Spirit-Gates.**
The peaks are the face, and the spirit-gates are the eyes, ears, mouth, and nose. Opening them enables control over demons; closing them and losing their numen allows demons to turn one about. When the Five Peaks all open their spirit-locks, they heed the Thearch’s command.

**Transmitting the Decree to the Great Demon King.**
Receiving the Jade Thearch’s mandate to restrain the Great Demon, the navel is the palace of the Northern Yin, the domain where yin and evil prevail. Thus, the decree is transmitted to restrain them, preventing reckless disturbance. The demons are the eyes, ears, nose, tongue, body, and intent.

**Rivers and Seas All Receive Their Duties.**
Even a single ladle of water may harbor soft-shelled turtles, alligators, dragons, fish, and turtles, and yield wealth and prosperity. The lords of rivers and seas—dragons and their kind—receive their duties and heed the commands of Fusang. From Heaven’s One generating water in the *Kan* position to the completion of heaven and earth, the birth of worthies and sages all arises therefrom. The River Earls, Sea Spirits, aquatic deities, and water immortals all receive and fulfill their originally appointed offices. Like Tao Hongjing, who served as Vice Director of Waterways, or Guo Pu, who became the Water Inspector Immortal Earl, and the Four Seas Ladies who govern female immortals in the waters, humans and aquatic beings may intermingle as immortals.

This account describes the jade’s traversal of the water palaces of the Yangzi, Yellow, Huai, and Eastern Seas, and the dragon palaces: westward from the Shu River, southward from Hengtan, and southwest from Yuan and Jing, where the three rivers converge at Dongting, then flow down to the Han River, meeting Dabie, reaching Mount Lu; southeast from Ji and Gan, converging at Pengli, then flowing down to Yizhen, where the Huai and Yellow Rivers meet from the north and south at Zhenjiang, then flow down to Kunlun Mountain and eastward into the sea. From Zhenjiang, passing through Chang and Su, entering the three hundred and sixty expanses of Tai Lake, reaching Wushan to meet the Zhe River; southeast from Fuxin River to meet the Zhe; from Weiyang, sailing upstream through the Huai, passing Lüliang to enter the Ji; from Mount Tai to meet the Ji; from the Ji, sailing upstream to Linqing, entering the Hutuo, northeast to meet Xiaozhigu and enter the sea; from Zhigu, sailing upstream to the capital, observing along the way Qutang, Dongting, Pengli, and Tai Lake—how magnificent the dragon palaces!—and seeing the Three Water Palaces of Madang Mountain, Caishi, and Jinshan. How could they not receive their duties from the sea?

**Establishing the Corresponding Directions for Assembly.**
Stagnant pools have no root to rely upon, but the Yangzi and Han rivers pay homage to the sea, each in its due time. The cinnabar classics say: “Heaven corresponds to the stars, earth to the tides; in heaven, metal is born, and on earth, water is born.” Thus, at each month’s crescent, full, waning, and new moons, the sea’s waters rise and fall accordingly. Each day, a single tide begins in the Eastern Sea, surging like a snow-capped mountain, passing the sea’s mouth and flowing upstream, traversing Zhe to halt at Caishi in the west, at Yanling Shoals in the southeast, and at Xiaozhigu in the northeast. Day and night, their assembly is unerring. Likewise, in the human body, each day and night, the blood and qi make a single circuit to the fontanel. When the tide arrives, one sits in silent stillness, concentrating the spirit and thought, and hears the blood and qi rushing from heel to crown, the rustling sound of their convergence, like a swarm of ants climbing, the turning sounds of the five viscera and six bowels. Inner and outer correspond, manifesting in the four limbs and reaching the auditory organs. After a long while, they gradually disperse, and all becomes silent. This, too, is a great principle of cultivation.

The sage’s transformative work cannot be entrusted to empty words. Through skillful analogies and clear metaphors, making the near taken from the body and the far from things, even if one cannot observe the sea’s tides from afar, one may listen closely to the ebb and flow of the blood’s glory and the qi’s defense—one myriad, three thousand, and five hundred breaths’ tide. Is this not showing people the corresponding directions for assembly?

**Preserving the Talisman Within the Muddy Pellet.**
Wine jars and sacrificial vessels may be offered to kings and dukes or presented in ancestral temples. How much more should the preserved talismanic contracts, all stored in the Muddy Pellet Palace, await Peach Health? Yin talismans and yang fire all gather in the Upper Prime Palace.

**Guarding the Spirit is Called Peach Health.**
Stirred and raised, it may pass over the forehead. Water is born in the kidneys, and when transported by the Dao, it flows upstream to the Muddy Pellet. Peach Health is the spirit within the kidneys, singularly transporting yang essence to the brain’s rear to assist primordial yang and complete the golden elixir.

**Reversing the Name in the Ledger of the Dead.**
Having obtained the root of ceaseless life, one reverses and changes one’s name in the ledger of the dead, leaving no transgressions to be recorded. The ledger of the dead is the Black Register, where all human transgressions, calamities, and deaths are fully recorded.

**Recording the Fire King of the Immortal Uncle.**
Chapter Three of the Upper Scroll states: "Gao Tongsheng, the Fire King of the Uncle." Here it is abbreviated as "Fire King of the Uncle," for this is the scripture of the Primordial One. The Fire King of the Uncle is the Dao Father, exclusively overseeing the ledgers of the immortals, to which all who attain the Dao are appended.

**Severing the Ledgers of the Three Paths of Suffering.**
The *Kan Hexagram* states: "Bound with cords and fettered in thorns." This is the place of imprisonment and reflection on transgressions, like King Wen’s confinement in Youli or Tai Jia’s in Tong Palace. Now, severing the Three Paths and altering the ledger of the dead—does this not embody this very principle?

**Dispelling Misfortune to Give Birth to the Upper Flower.**
The True Fluid Sovereign within the heart, named Feisheng Shangying, governs the blood and fluids. The *Book of Changes* says: "Kan is not full, yet it levels—no blame." For now, misfortune is dispelled but not yet wholly eradicated. Cutting away the root of calamity, one gives birth to the Upper Flower’s splendor.

**The Seven Mysteries Ascend the Vermilion Palace.**
The Vermilion Palace resides atop the *Li* hexagram. The Seven Mysteries and the Nine Ancestors ascend to the Vermilion Numinous Fire Mansion, where refinement occurs naturally. This is the union of water and fire, the dual cultivation of qi. The immortals Ge Xian and Huang Yuyang both attained the Dao through such alchemical rites.

**My Body Meets the Radiant Yang.**
The omen of the body’s audience with the luminous realm of the Great Yang Dao. The *Precelestial Book of Changes* states: "Water and fire do not repel each other." This scripture speaks of the Dao being accomplished through their union. The *Dou Scripture* says: "Water and fire are the true essence of the Dao; without them, generation and transformation cannot be achieved."

**The Upper Friend is Fang Yingzi.**
The Peach Health Lord of the Moon, Fang Ying, styled Yunliang, is befriended above—an affectionate and lingering attachment. The upper and lower spirits interchange, circulating divine qi, nourishing the root of life, fostering supreme harmony, and establishing the Four Greatnesses.

**The Lower Carries Li Weizang.**
The celestial essence-spirit within the womb, named Li Weizang, styled Fayun Zhu, guards the Water Sea of the Small Intestine, distinguishing the clarity and turbidity of its sources, guiding its discharge with the efficacy of Yu the Great. In humans, it is fitting to skillfully guide essence and blood.

**The Left Seizes the Luminous Chariot Lord.**
The Yellow Qi Lord within the womb, named Zu Mingche, styled Shen Wuji, guards the liver alongside the Bright Wheel of the Northern Dipper. Without the circulation of the myriad qi and spirits, the hundred bones, five viscera, four limbs, skin, and flesh would be but a lump of inert matter.

**The Right Assists Gui Shengchang.**
The White Qi Lord within the womb, on the right, named Xuan Guizi, styled Shengchang, guards the lungs. These two spirits, dwelling within the womb, jointly oversee the five viscera. As the preceding chapter states: "The White Qi nurtures Shangsheng," which conveys the same meaning.

**Uniting the Jade Radiance Qi,**
(One version mistakenly writes "Jade Capital.") Here, the left and right yin and yang qi merge, congealing like jade’s radiant essence to form the body’s shape. This qi, when exhaled, can boil tea; when held in the mouth, it can dry mercury.

**Transforming the Omen to Prosperity and Flourishing.**
To transmute one’s qi and substance, bringing auspiciousness and prosperity—this is the attainment of the Dao. Though foolish, one becomes wise; though weak, one becomes strong. The noble person follows it and finds fortune; the petty person turns from it and meets misfortune. This is not bestowed from without; it is inherently ours.

**Returning to the Infant of the Original Destiny,**
Reverting the spirit of one’s aging original destiny to the form of an infant, also called the Original Destiny Perfected Person. Cultivating the Great Cavern’s Dao, refining the myriad qi and spirits, one returns to the singular truth of the infant’s form, then transforms into primordial qi.

**The Sandalwood Blazes with Auspicious Harmony.**
Not the flute’s *Wusheng Melody* nor the stringless zither’s *Taiping Song*:
*"For years, the master has been poor to the bone,
Yet why does he joyfully embrace heaven’s harmony?
Only if one is a true listener should it be played—
Those who know not the tune must not be shown."*

**The Celestial One, Root of the Primordial Immortal,**
The Celestial One Noble Person emerges at the hours of *chou* and *wei*, serving as the primordial root of water. Thus, rivers and seas become the kings of all valleys, receiving waters. Truly, the Celestial One generates water, its source arising here. The meaning of the *Kan* hexagram is thus revealed.

**Abiding in the Wheel of Luminous Freedom.**
The Greater and Lesser Fortunes are the abodes of the sun and moon. The Northern Dipper’s *Qingyang* and *Tuoluo* govern their affairs. Thus, the Northern Dipper resides in the *Kan* palace, named the Lunar Mansion. The revolving luminous wheel aligns with the Bright Wheel of the liver, the radiant wheel of the sun and moon, the water pool and fire marsh.

**In all refinement, first refine the self.**
The heart is the fire of *Li*; the kidneys are the water of *Kan*. The essential task is their union. The method requires this heart to be empty and still, free from the slightest dust, with not a single thought stirring. The two qi merge, transforming into water and fire. The wandering soul, emerging from the left kidney, returns to the marsh to be refined and transmuted.

The above Jade Chapter of Heavenly Seal Script, comprising one hundred and thirty characters, descends from the Great Crimson Heaven, governing the Ninth Layer of the Boundless Abyss, the Realm of the Colorless Rigid Axis, the Earthly Sovereign Lord.

The *Mysterious Contract* states: "At this supreme vehicle’s gate, the adept’s body and ancestral lineage all attain true immortality, enabling the vast compassion to deliver and elevate beings of heaven and earth to realization."

These four chapters of the Perfected Person, the True Immortal King of the Great Clarity and Great Ultimate, correspond to the Four Heavens of the Three Clarities and the Jade Emperor. They transcend hexagrammatic symbols, just as the *Qian* and *Kun* hexagrams lack stems and branches. *Qian* and *Kun* are the great parents, retiring to seclusion, while *Kan* and *Li* are the parents of the myriad things, thus held in esteem. The Three Clarities retire to nonaction, and the Jade Emperor governs affairs—all are revered, dwelling in the realm beyond color, unbound by hexagrammatic symbols.

Humans who cultivate the wondrous practices of the Great Cavern of Wenchang may transcend the Three Realms, directly ascending to the heavens of the Three Clarities and the Jade Emperor, unbound by the Five Movements or the Eight Trigrams.

The Five Movements are the Five Phases and the stems and branches; the Eight Trigrams are also derived from the Five Phases. *Qian* and *Dui* belong to metal; *Zhen* and *Xun* to wood; *Kun* and *Gen* to earth; *Kan* to water; and *Li* to fire. The cultivator sheds the husk and departs the mechanism.

The Celestial King of Primordial Beginning states: "The thirty-fourth Jade Chapter of the Great Cavern of Wenchang corresponds to the *Kun* and *Gen* hexagrams, both of the same sound and belonging to earth."

The Upper Clarity’s true realm is transformed from primordial qi.

The Jade Clarity’s Myriad Flowers Palace—this Myriad Flowers Palace is the abode of the Jade Clarity’s Primordial Beginning, adorned entirely with gold, jade, and precious treasures, no different in splendor from the *Avataṃsaka*’s opulence. As previously stated: "To behold the *Avataṃsaka* is not equal to a single *Gen* hexagram." Now, the Myriad Flowers Palace reveals where one ought to abide. The noble person reflects that his thoughts do not transgress his station; he acts in accordance with his allotted place, finding fulfillment in every circumstance. This illustrates how one should rest content in the constant, abide in the realm of utmost goodness, free from partiality or reckless pursuit, upholding the rectitude of Heaven’s principle. Wealth and honor are the natural course, and all may partake in the Myriad Flowers Palace’s abundance.

The Lofty Immortals conceal the imperial scriptures. The *Kun* hexagram embodies the principle of nurturing and transformation. The *Book of Changes* states: "*Kun* conceals." The Lofty Immortals are where the celestial perfected store their scriptures—thirty-six sections, eighteen thousand scrolls. The Buddhist canon comprises five thousand forty-eight volumes in one collection. Since ancient times, the institutions of emperors and kings have ensured the preservation of maps and books throughout the realm, such as the *Lian Shan* of Shennong, the *Gui Cang* of Xuanyuan, the *Lian Shan* of Yu the Great, and the *Gui Cang* of Tang the Completer. Successive dynasties treasured these as divine instruments. Heaven, too, possesses its own maps and books, stored by the Celestial Emperor to govern the myriad heavens and administer the ten thousand kinds.

The *Chart of the Nine Heavens* presides. *Gen* halts here, marking the Way of Wenchang as perfect in every virtue. The noble person reveres uprightness within, embodies righteousness without, and embraces service to the sovereign—this is the Way of the minister. The Lofty Immortals and Perfected Sages oversee the registers and charts in the Nine Heavens, directing the mechanisms of transformation to nurture the ten thousand things. Among the Nine Heavens is the Eastern Wall Repository of Maps and Books. The *Kui* constellation governs literature, residing in *Xu*; the *Bi* constellation governs maps and books, residing in *Hai*. The Celestial Emperor commanded the August Person of Wenchang, the Mysterious Sage and Dao Lord Confucius, to preside over the *Chart of Wenchang’s Generative Qi*, circulating true qi to engender and transform the ten thousand things, assisting the imperial enterprise. The Emperor bestowed the investiture: Supreme Perfected of the Great Ultimate and Mount Jiuyi, True Lord of the Eastern Sea and Broad Mulberry Mountain, Grand Thearch of Illuminating the Dao and Flourishing the Confucian Age.

Some may question: "Is this not Confucius’ Way? How could a great sage be subsumed into a heterodox teaching?" Yet they fail to realize that in Heaven, he is a constellation; on Earth, a river or mountain; in the unseen, a spirit; and in the manifest, once more a human. This is but the most evident aspect. Moreover, the great sage, in transmitting teachings for the world and establishing a model for ten thousand generations of emperors and kings, has received veneration and sacrifices across successive dynasties. How could he lack a fruition in the midst of Heaven, Earth, and humanity? Here, he is appended to this discourse, awaiting the discernment of the enlightened.

Observe the cavern and nothing gives birth. How sublime is the origin of *Kun*! The ten thousand things rely upon it for life. The birth of humans and things proceeds from nothing to being, receiving *Kun*’s complete qi. Thus it is said: "*Kun*’s thickness bears all things; its virtue unites with boundlessness." The cavern cannot be observed with the eyes; one must inwardly direct the mind’s gaze. From nothing, being arises—not that nothingness is void, but that it abides in serene constancy. One must not seek outwardly or falsely assume existence. As with Sudhana’s visions, all dwelled within Samantabhadra’s body. This Dao is emptiness and spontaneity, beyond grasp or comprehension. One need only turn the light inward to illuminate the self. Thus it is said: "Observe the cavern and nothing gives birth."

Seven revolutions summon the ten thousand perfected. This shares the same meaning as the seven revolutions that summon the Three Officials. The ten thousand perfected are the ten thousand spirits. Heaven possesses ten thousand perfected; humans possess ten thousand spirits. When Heaven’s true qi merges with human spirit, and Heaven’s qi harmonizes with human qi, the Dao is naturally attained. How could this not be precious?

The Five Marchmounts arrive at the courtyard. *Kun*’s expanse and *Gen*’s mountain—among these, the Five Marchmounts are supreme. A pinch of earth bears Mount Hua and stirs rivers and seas; a rolled stone nurtures plants and gives rise to treasures. How much more so when the Five Marchmounts lie within one’s grasp? The golden elixir is called the gathering of the Five Phases.

The Three Officials summon the host of demons. The Three Officials are the Three Passes. When their command is issued, the myriad heavens obey. Where the will leads, qi follows. When the Three Passes are opened, the Three Flowers gather at the crown. Among the Three Powers, only the Three and Five can govern the ten thousand transformations.

The Controller of Destiny examines the presented records. The Three Officials and Five Marchmounts report human fortunes and misfortunes. The Celestial Emperor commands the Controller of Destiny and Controller of Lifespans to reexamine and verify them before determining good or ill fortune.

Long ago, Nie Shaoyuan was fond of reading and studied the works of Zhuangzi and Laozi. One night, he dreamed of entering a city’s palace, where amidst solemnity, a crimson-robed official seated at a desk said: "This is the Office of Destiny. You may open the register and review your life’s affairs." Later, he received the complete register of the Great Cavern and cultivated the Dao of harmonizing and returning. One morning, as he bathed, four cranes alighted upon his roof. Villagers, seeing flames, rushed over, only to find Shaoyuan already transformed. Was this not the verification of the Controller of Destiny’s records?

Extract the register from the winding springs. The winding springs are the twelve river sources, the watery bureaus that govern human life, death, merit, and transgressions. Liu Yuan passed down that the watery bureaus belong to yin, administered by female immortals. In humans, these correspond to the twelve meridians, which are the twelve river sources.

Inscribe the name in the *Shangqing* register. The following lines, according to the Mao Mountain *Jade Scripture*, state: "The seven ancestors’ bonds are untied; impure blood wholly dissipates. Returning to the vermilion fire chamber, one is reborn within the cavern. The scribes and historians guard the divine body, enabling me to preserve yellow tranquility." These six lines continue the preceding, forming a section titled *The Chapter of the Three Primordial Lords*. Though the meaning repeats, the present text follows the Sichuan edition, appending the next fifteen lines to the prior ten, making twenty-five lines in total, preserved as a single chapter. No arbitrary alterations or additions are made to avoid confusing the reader. Proceeding thus, one may also attain the rank of upper immortal.

The Dark Continent severs the three fords. *Kun* is utterly yielding yet moves with firmness; utterly still yet its virtue is square. Thus, within the earth’s expanse lies the Dark Continent’s Crimson City Prefecture, beyond the Eastern Sea. Among the three isles and divine mountains, the Dark Continent is one of the ten continents. The three fords of weak water span thirty thousand *li*, each guarded by ford-keepers no one can overcome. Yet those who cultivate the golden elixir sever these fords, bypassing the passes to arrive home in a single step. As the ancients said: "Breach the fence, and it is your own estate." Cultivating the Way of Wenchang’s Great Cavern, one does not traverse the Three Realms’ myriad heavens or the twenty-five heavens, but instantly transcends to the realm of no outflows. Only then is the matter truly settled.

The Feathered Canopy ascends to the Court of the Great Void. Riding the feathered canopy and ascending in the radiant chariot, the Court of the Great Void lies far above the Formless Realm. As the *Tradition* states: "Virtue is light as a feather, yet even a feather has its measure." The burden of heaven bears all—soundless, scentless. The Feathered Canopy has form; the Great Void is formless.

Wheeling through the skies, it descends like drifting sands. Soaring and returning above the Nine Empyreans, the carriages and brushes of the perfected ones are myriad, grinding away the cloud-paths. Thus, they fly and scatter like desert sands drifting downward. In the time of Yu, a bird came from the Cinnabar Prefecture, exhaling five-colored mists of qi, called the Cloud-Riding Sparrow. It could fly in flocks, bearing green sand-pearls—light and fine—so that when the wind stirred, dust rose, called "pearl-dust," drifting down like desert sands. Those who obtained and ingested it became weightless and deathless. Is this not what is meant here?

The enlightened need not stir their feet; with the arising of a single thought, they ascend directly to the Round Summit. Another version reads *flying across the Milky Way*, the characters being somewhat similar.

Surrendering transformation, they merge with the ten thousand essences.

Embracing vastness and radiating greatness, all things attain flourishing—such is the virtue of Kun. Those who can gather and refine, moving in harmony with the times and merging with the myriad beings as one body, find nothing that does not come to fruition. Surrendering and transforming, they blend into the essence of the ten thousand things.

Five clouds thicken in the boundless void—five directions, five numina, five-colored clouds of qi, billowing and dense within the infinite sky. The qi of the five viscera steams and rises within the heart’s chamber, congealing into a pearl of perfect clarity, its radiant hues mirrored in the resplendent glow of rosy clouds. Thus, the five colors surge and blaze, illuminating the great emptiness.

Seven rosy clouds descend upon perfect clarity. The seven rosy clouds are the seven awakenings; one version reads: *a single numen descends upon perfect clarity*. This single numen is also the void and luminous, for the heart’s clarity is the heart’s spirit. Here, the seven-colored clouds and rosy mists outshine the sun and moon.

The *Scripture of Salvation* says: *The jade pivot and the balanced armillary halt their turning.* These lines describe the moment when lofty immortals gather with the Lords of Destiny, the Recorders, the Three Officials, and the Five Peaks. The throng of chariots and phoenix-borne carriages shines with such splendor—this speaks of one who can condense the myriad qi, allowing the spirit of the primordial numen to ride upon them. From the lower cinnabar field to the muddy pellet, the ten thousand qi congeal and the ten thousand spirits assemble, which is also a descent upon perfect clarity.

Bright and clear, the Recluse of the Profound Void—
The radiant Infant Boy appears below the navel. The two hexagrams unite in virtue; the *Judgment* of *Modesty* seeks to exhaust its meaning. The Way of Heaven diminishes the full; the Way of Earth transforms the full; ghosts and spirits harm the full. Yet modesty is honored and shines—such is the end of the noble one. This speaks of one who conceals their traces and hides their light, abiding in their proper place, unassuming yet manifest.

Thus, they attain the meaning of modest radiance. The noble one, dwelling in seclusion, seeks to fulfill their aspiration and practice virtue to realize the Dao. Naturally, their name resounds above and below. Though the Recluse of the Profound Void is formless and soundless, they shine with luminous clarity—this is what is meant by *though hidden, it is nonetheless evident*.

The flourishing of the numinous heart aids the tranquility of the Yellow Peace. The flourishing numen is the spirit of the heart; the Yellow Peace is the spirit of the spleen. This speaks of using the heart’s blood to nourish the spleen and stomach. The mutual generation and restraint of the Five Phases, when applied within a person, follow the circulation of qi to harmonize them, each according to its proper Way. For example, if the heart is afflicted, one circulates kidney water to aid it—this pattern applies to all five viscera.

Here, the two hexagrams oppose each other as *Splitting Apart*. The *Judgment* says: *The noble one esteems the waxing and waning of fullness and emptiness.* The Yellow Peace is the central palace, the Yellow Center that penetrates principle, rightly positioned within the body. Beauty resides within, spreading to the four limbs and manifesting in one’s undertakings. When a person’s bearing and conduct accord with the mean of the Dao, it is the utmost of abundant virtue.

The Five Elders scatter crimson blossoms—
The Five Elders are the primal ancestors of Heaven and Earth; the Five Elders within a person share the same qi. Thus, the five spirits gather in the Crimson Palace, wielding and scattering cinnabar blossoms. Burning incense and strewing flowers are both acts of the body’s numinous awareness; the crimson blossom and the cinnabar blossom are one.

They carry fragrant incense and jade numina. The Five Elders scatter the five fragrances to steam and nourish the numinous clarity of the five viscera. The *Upper Scroll* speaks of the Jade Longevity Numen, also the spirit of the stomach. To behold this spirit, one must focus the mind single-pointedly, like a cat stalking a mouse, eyes unblinking—thus, they attain condensation.

The golden substance is bathed in the Emperor’s River—
This is the refining of the jade pupils and the swaying of the yellow blossom to transform the form. The impure bones of the mortal body are now transmuted into a golden numen and jade substance. As previously said, *flesh and bones become gold and jade*—this is the true meaning of that golden form and jade quality, washed and cleansed in the river of the Primal Unity.

Green mists billow like flowing jade. Azure-green mists rise thick and dense, as if jade were about to flow. As previously said, *five clouds thicken in the boundless void*—all describe the ascent and descent of perfected immortals, where auspicious mists and propitious hues suffuse and purify the realm of empty vastness, their splendor surpassing all.
