The Master of the Jade Emperor of the Upper Clarity—
The Upper Clarity Palace is the teacher of the Jade Emperor. The Numinous Treasure is the revered teacher of the Jade Emperor. The Jade Clarity, Upper Clarity, and Grand Clarity form the Three Treasures. Below the Three Clarities, the Jade Emperor is supreme. The Jade Emperor is the August Jade Emperor of the Vast Heaven, the Most Honored of the Myriad Heavens, second only to the Three Clarities. The *Scripture of the Heavenly Duke* says: *The Three Clarities retire to non-action; the Jade Emperor governs affairs.*

The Lord of the Great Dao of the Jade Capital—
The Jade Capital is the palace where the Lord of the Numinous Treasure, the Heavenly Worthy, resides—the Upper Clarity Seven Treasures Purple Tenuity Palace, situated above the Grand Clarity and below the Jade Clarity, known as the Middle Primordial Palace. The Three Clarities correspond to the Three Sovereigns in the Confucian classics.

Together with the spirit of the Crimson Palace of the heart—
Master Void-and-Stillness said: *A sudden arising is sickness; not continuing it is medicine. Do not fear the arising of thoughts—only fear delayed awareness.* An ancient worthy said: *If one sits in stillness for a single moment, it surpasses building a seven-jeweled stupa. Though the stupa may eventually crumble to dust, a single thought unarisen attains true awakening.* Thus, when this heart does not give rise to a single thought, one instantly ascends to the sacred realm. Therefore, it is said: *flying to verify the Venerable of the Great Mystery.*

The heart governs the entire body, and its nature is void and numinous, sufficient to comprehend the principles of the ten thousand affairs and things in the world. Though these principles are scattered across the ten thousand affairs and things, their subtle and wondrous function lies nowhere but in the single heart of a person. As a former worthy’s poem says: *The Dao extends beyond the forms of Heaven and Earth; thought enters the ever-changing winds and clouds.* The Numinous Treasure and the heart-spirit are one heart—this is the heart of Heaven, not the fleshly heart. The spirit is the indestructible spirit across kalpas, not the spirits of sacrifice.

The *Book of Songs* says: *If the human heart unites with the heart of Heaven, the inversion of yin and yang takes but a moment.* Thus, it is said: *The Jade Capital and the heart-spirit fly to verify the Venerable of the Great Mystery.* For the heart of Heaven does not depart from perfect impartiality and utmost rectitude, without the slightest self-interest. If the human heart can embody and follow this, acting without partiality and always aligning with perfect rectitude, then one will undoubtedly verify the Great Cavern and the Venerable of the Great Mystery.

Flying to verify the Venerable of the Great Mystery—
Ascending to verify the fruition of the Venerable of the Great Mystery’s position.

Below this, the *Great Cavern* of Mount Mao (alternate version) reads:
*The spirit extricates the accumulated [karma] of the three paths; the immortal embryo entwines the omen of form.*

The two lines above frequently appear, for the Three Perfected of the Great Mystery occupy the most exalted position. Beyond Heaven and Earth lies the realm of *Xuwu* (Vacuity-and-Nothingness), the abode of the Primordial Beginning, styled *Xuwu Ziran* (Vacuous-Natural). It is called *xu* (vacuous) because it is without heart-mind, and *wu* (nothing) because it is utterly empty. Yet vacuity enables it to contain all, and nothingness enables it to transform all. Thus it is called the *Scripture of the Hidden Emperor*. When humans attain vacuity and nothingness, the numinous spirits naturally come; once they come, they remain enduringly luminous. Hence the hexagrams *Kun* (Receptive) and *Gen* (Stillness) are invoked as metaphors for its capacity to contain and endure.

The above Jade Chapter in celestial seal-script comprises one hundred and thirty characters, transmitted from the Heaven of Yu-Yu, governing the Ninth Rampart of the Lord of Flourishing Virtue.

The *Mysterious Contract* states: Upon reaching this stage, one ascends to the rank of Perfected King of the Supreme Clarity and Perfected One of Grand Unity.

The Primordial Heavenly King says: The thirty-fifth Jade Chapter of the Great Cavern of Wenchang elucidates the Dao of the intermingling of the *Kan* (Abysmal) and *Li* (Clinging) trigrams. It arises from the primordial qi of the Sacred Realm of Jade Clarity.

The Three Perfected give birth to Great Nothingness.
The Three Perfected are the Three Qi Heavenly Lords of the Southern Direction, born at the inception of the Vast Emptiness of Great Nothingness. The text below refers to *Nanchang*, which is Wenchang. Today, Mount Heng corresponds to the *Zhen* constellation above and presides over the Southern Palace of *Li* below. It harbors the Grotto-Heaven of Vermilion Mound, the third of the thirty-six grotto-heavens. Only those who refine and transform themselves here are permitted to attain full personhood. Within the human body, this corresponds to the Three Perfected Yuan Lords of Essence and Blood.

Some say the Three Perfected are the same as the Three Perfected of the Great Mystery mentioned earlier; others claim *Taiwu* (Great Nothingness) is a corruption of *Taiyuan* (Great Prime). This is in fact the Jade Chapter of the Great Cavern of the Lord of Great Simplicity within Great Nothingness.

The Jade Gate reflects the morning glow.
The Great Person continues the illumination across the four directions, as night wanes and the sun’s light succeeds it—precisely the moment when the Great Brilliance emerges from the Eastern Direction. The Southern Direction, positioned in the Palace of *Li*, shares its name with the sun. The *Jade Gate* is where the sun-bird’s chariot emerges; *morning* refers to the sun, and its radiance illumines the rosy clouds of dawn—also an allusion to the early court audience. At the summit of Vermilion Sparrow Peak on Mount Southern Prison stands the Sun-Viewing Pavilion. On clear mornings, ascending this pavilion to observe the solar orb’s emergence from the sea reveals its gradual ascent and descent, its hesitation before rising, and then its sudden ascent in a single burst of splendor—all phenomena fully evident here.

The numinous essence of the Grotto of Great Simplicity—
The sun and moon adhere to Heaven, and their radiance must illuminate the Vermilion Heaven’s Grotto-Yang Palace in the Southern Direction. Only those who refine their forms here are permitted to ascend to the Celestial Court.

As stated in the preceding fascicle: *The Three-Flower Qi of Great Simplicity*—the Three-Flower Qi are also the Three Qi of the Southern Direction. Great Simplicity is the Mother of the Three Simplicities, presiding over the work of refinement and deliverance. It is also called *Hanzhang* (Rare and Vast). Mount Heng possesses a blessed site named the Altar of the Grotto-Heaven of Numinous Radiance, among others—all places where superior immortals attain the Dao. Wenchang’s refinement and transformation occur here, which is why this grotto chapter frequently refers to it.

The cinnabar groves flourish with vermilion branches.
The hundred grains and myriad plants adhere to the earth. Because the Southern Direction is associated with the color red, all that grows there are cinnabar groves and vermilion branches. The *Scripture of the Yellow Court* states: *Vermilion and azure, green boughs and jade-like branches.* Medical texts record: *The Southern Mountains abound in numinous mushrooms and auspicious herbs; those who consume them all become immortals.*

Return the spirit to the ninefold palace.
Restore the spirit to the ninefold palace, for the Vermilion Mound’s Fire Palace is formed from the ninefold yang qi of Brahma. Today, the topography of Mount Heng also presents nine fronts and nine backs, corresponding to the yang number. This describes the signs manifesting in the heart’s palace during cultivation.

Nanchang emits jade-like radiance.
Nothing dries and matures the myriad things as thoroughly as fire. Thus, the Southern Direction’s fire virtue augments the Great Yang, adorning all categories of existence so each may fulfill its growth. Nanchang, the Bureau of Refinement, is the place of deliverance—none who attain the Dao fail to pass through it. Named the Grotto-Yang Palace, it contains the Flowing Fire Pool and the Yellow Flower Waters, both of which generate jade-like blossoms of splendor. The *Scripture of Salvation* states: *Those who cultivate and recite this scripture will all receive deliverance and ascend to the Southern Palace*—a parallel to this passage, describing the heart’s palace and spirit’s abode in such magnificence.

Nanchang is Wenchang. The Primordial Beginning refines it with talismanic scriptures and true writings in the Grotto-Yang Palace. Thus it is said: *Within Wenchang resides the deathless spirit, the Lord of Longevity, the True Lords of Life Mandate, Fortune, Lifespan Extension, and Destiny Augmentation.* The *Scripture of Salvation* states: *The Southern Palace and Nanchang are identical to this*—referring to present-day Mount Heng.

The primordial qi ascends to connect with the Fire Star. The Palace of the Scorching Sun is governed by the Venerable Lord of Flame. Within it, the summer qi nurtures and fosters the myriad things. All the gods of the world, on the day of Summer’s Beginning, ascend to this Crimson Stone Jade Tower to pay homage to the Venerable Lord of Flame, receive the Heavenly Mysterious Talismans, and return to their respective directions to enact the summer ordinances.

The Crimson Emperor, Jade Controller Lord, is named Jingdu. If one knows this spirit and contemplates it for nine years, the elixir of longevity will be attained. Cinnabar clouds will fly, descending to welcome the adept’s body, which will then ascend to Jade Clarity.

Though this be so, Mount Heng lies thousands of miles away—how could everyone journey there to behold it? Yet within the human body there is also a Mount Heng. Knowing this, the Bureau of Wenchang’s refinement and transformation is not far off. The Dao is not distant from humanity; it resides within the body. Seek it through personal inquiry and authentic attainment—do not rely on arbitrary conjecture or forced interpretation.

The hundred joints receive the fluid essence.
The world regards water as the moistening element, and thus it is water that engenders and nurtures the myriad things. This perfectly illustrates the *Kan* trigram’s significance.

Humans possess one hundred and eighty numinous joints, three hundred and sixty bones, one thousand two hundred physical forms, twelve thousand essences of radiance, thirty-six thousand root origins, and eighty-four thousand pores. Within these key points, the moistening fluid essence is generated. Without fluid essence, humans wither and perish. Heaven and Earth are sustained by water, and the myriad things are born and completed by it—truly, all is one.

Conceal the mysterious root in the winding vale of the Three Eminences.
Hide the mysterious root within the winding vale of the Three Eminences. Mount Heng is named the Heaven of Lesser Existence within Great Vacuity. An ancient poem states: *Within the Grotto of Lesser Existence grows the Three Eminences herb.*

The lingzhi is precisely this. Mountains bear five sacred fungi, and those who consume the highest of them attain transcendence. The body soars to the Jade Clarity—once one’s own form has verified the rank of Upper Immortal, one may ascend and wander in revelry through the sacred precincts of Jade Clarity, paying court to the Primordial Celestial Sovereign. Many sages of old had kin whose flesh and bone took flight together, yet these physical forms all shed and concealed themselves in famous mountains; only the spirit may depart.

The seven ancestors depart the Dark Gate.
The Dark Gate is the Water Bureau, the winding source of the Yellow Springs. Before one attains the Dao, the seven ancestors remain mired in the Dark Gate; once immortality is achieved, one must first deliver one’s own lineage of ancestors to escape the Dark Gate—this is the Nether Capital governed by the Earth and Water Bureaus.

Eternally preserve beyond the kalpas of termination.
Forever safeguard through the inexhaustible kalpas of dust. The *Great Cavern Scripture* represents the supreme vehicle, far beyond the reach of lesser immortals of inferior rank. Those who cultivate to this stage never regress—how can they be compared with the fruits of celestial beings?

Inherit the immortal lineage for ten thousand generations.
The *Jade Scripture* states: *Generation after generation without end, ever ruling as sovereign; through a thousand myriad kalpas, perpetually succeeding one another.* In the families of Upper Immortals, all the renowned mountains of the world have those of different surnames who inherit the immortal rank. Only the Heavenly Master Zhang’s lineage has endured for forty generations.

The rank is the honored seat of the sagely succession.
Establishing the ultimate principle in accord with Heaven, this rank is the honored seat of the sagely succession. Among humankind, this is the work of the great person—just as the Great Cavern Celestial Honored One governs all spirits, occupying the most exalted and noble position. Few in the world attain this as immortals.

The Jade Clarity Great Cavern Immortal.
The title is *Jade Clarity Great Cavern Spirit*, the most revered and glorious. This is the moment when Kan and Li unite in intercourse and the true body is perfected. There are the Great Cavern Honored One and the Great Cavern Spirit, yet they are fundamentally one—namely, one’s own original destiny and celestial alignment. Fire above and water below possess the Way of intercourse. People merely know that fire flames upward and water moistens downward, yet they do not understand that restraining the heart-fire to ascend the kidney-water is the principle of ceaseless generation. If fire is too parching or water too inundating, death follows. In tranquil serenity, with a single mind and all distractions banished, the purple-golden light transforms, manifesting in the eyes as a sign—this is not achieved through massage or visualization.

The above jade passage of celestial script consists of seventy characters, descended from the Clear Subtlety Heaven and presided over by the Ninth Rampart Lord of Flourishing Virtue. The *Mysterious Contract* states: *At this stage, one ascends to the Jade Clarity Sagely Heaven as the One Sagely Sovereign.*

The Primordial Celestial Sovereign declares: *The thirty-sixth jade passage of the Great Cavern of Wenchang corresponds to the trigram pair Dui and Gen, signifying joy and stillness.*

The boundary of the Maitreya Heaven is transformed by Brahmanic qi.
The Ninefold Numinous Qi of the Western Origin.
This passage corresponds to the trigrams by first taking Dui and then Gen in opposition. Dui is the trigram of the true West, hence the Ninefold Numinous Supreme Wondrous White Jade Tortoise Terrace Golden Perfected Brahmanic Qi Primordial Sovereign—this is the Queen Mother of the West, who governs the female immortals and resides in the highest precincts of the Paradise of Lang. She is formed of the Ninefold Numinous True Qi and has endured for hundreds of millions of years. Those who recite this scripture may pray for the empresses, consorts, and concubines to enjoy longevity equal to the Queen Mother’s and grace matching the years of the Brushing Stone.

The Golden Elixir flows through the Cloud Palace.
The Great Elixir takes gold as its mother. The Cloud Palace enters the Muddy Pellet Palace. The Cloud Palace is also the residence of the Queen Mother. Formerly, Shen Taizhi, styled Guangxiang, was originally from Luoyang. While serving as an official beyond the lakes, his family settled in Changsha. One evening atop the peak of Mount Zhuhong, he encountered a perfected one who transmitted to him the Fire Dragon technique of the Golden Elixir. After years of cultivation, his merit and conduct were complete, enabling him to ride the void and wander as a spirit, appearing and vanishing unpredictably. Emperor Xuanzong of Tang dreamed of him and invited him to serve as National Preceptor. Later, he ascended as a perfected immortal. This is the verification of the Golden Elixir, and thus the *Great Medicinal Elixir Diagram* was established in former times.

Above, it reaches the rotating apex of the luminaries.
The apex is the end, the utmost. The Queen Mother of Kunlun’s Langfeng governs this, for her height equals that of Heaven. Above, it attains the utmost pinnacle of the seven luminaries’ revolving jade mechanism.

Below this passage, according to the *Jade Scripture* of Mount Mao, there are four lines: *Amidst the radiant glory of the great rosy clouds, / Revolving the nine-heavenly wheel, / Serenely sinking the eightfold firm currents, / The chamber holds the Womb Immortal Mother.* These are absent in the Shu edition. For now, they are omitted, awaiting future scholars who may supplement them. Generally, scriptures and registers follow their respective transmitted lineages, and one need not rigidly adhere to uniformity or divergence, nor weigh their abundance or scarcity to seek peculiarity.

Carrying the *jin*, he enters the chamber of the Grand Thearch.
The *jin* of the Great Tenuity is named *Ganjingjing*, also called *Three Jin Intercourse*, and is also known as the *Jin* Child. It is the celestial robe. Lifting the celestial robe, one ascends to the chamber of the Grand Thearch. This is the Great Tenuity Grand Thearch, also one of the nine souls’ names—namely, the Central Yellow Court.

The Mysterious One’s numinous time gives birth.
The Mysterious One, Laozi Lin Xufu, styled *Lingshi*, guided the Dao to convey the mysterious qi, enabling numinous transformation and change.

The *Knot Scripture* states: *First is the conveyance of qi—this is the qi of the Great Mystery. It is precious to cause the nasal breath’s mysterious qi to congeal and settle.*

The Three Elders rarely display their forms.
The Three Primordial Elders are named *Hanzhang*. In the second chapter of the upper scroll, it states: *The Three Primordials give birth to the Muddy Pellet; the Elder Lord Hanzhang ascends above.* This is of the same meaning. The *Yellow Court Scripture* states: *The Three Elders sit together, each with their companions.* This also shares the same meaning as the Three Elders of the court.

On the left, he grasps the registers of the Five Talismans.
It speaks of the Three Primordial Elders. On the left, they hold the divine writs, talismans, charts, and registers of the Five Numinous Ones and Five Elders, as well as the incantations and mandates that rebuke inauspiciousness and open the Yellow Path. All perfected ones who wander in revelry and immortals who have attained the Dao rely on the Five Elders to initiate their journey.

On the right, he carries the lineage of the ten thousand spirits.
Dui signifies joy—accord with Heaven and response to humankind. The former people faced hardship, yet the people forgot their toil and death. This is the ultimate principle of humanity. When a person attains the Dao, left and right are raised and supported, and the ten thousand spirits all return to one’s grasp, ready to be commanded at will.

Together, they ascend the Dragon-Gem Gate.
The *Book of Changes* states: *The six positions are timely and accomplished; riding the six dragons, one governs Heaven.*

The *Great Cavern Scripture* here calls this the "Six Perfections Fully Realized," where together with the multitudes, one ascends the palaces of Dragon and Phoenix, of gem and jade—this is called "Selecting Immortals and Promoting Adepts." Bowing one’s head to the Jade Clarity Chamber. At the Upper Prime Mud-Pill Palace, cultivation having reached this stage, the Golden Elixir is already formed. One ought to shed the womb and change the cauldron, the spirit transforming naturally. Bowing one’s head, one pays homage and audience to the King of Clarity ● and the Primordial Beginning within the Cavern Chamber, requesting to receive immortal ranks and fill the offices of immortals.

One attains the Most Revered in the Sacred,
verifying the rank of the Great Cavern Heaven’s First Emperor Revered—this is the most exalted position in the sacred realm, forever immune to decline. Such is the station of the Golden Portal’s attending ministers before the Three Supreme Realms, a state incomparable to the conditioned causes of the Three Realms.

The talisman transforms into the Sovereign of Mysterious Qi.
Gen signifies "stillness"—stillness at the place of utmost goodness and ultimate perfection. The tradition states: *The workings of Highest Heaven are soundless and scentless.* When a person’s cultivation reaches this point, all dust is shaken off and exhausted, returning to the ○ Limitless.

The talisman is the Yin Talisman, refined by the yang fire’s minute transformation into Mysterious Qi, verifying one’s rank in the Jade Clarity. First, essence and qi nurture the spirit, forming the Infant; then the Infant is refined into the Yang Talisman, and the talisman transforms into Mysterious Qi—this is what is meant by ascending into formlessness and uniting with the Dao in truth.

The Śākya tradition states: *All phenomena with form are illusory.* It also says: *The Tathāgata cannot be seen through a fully embodied form.* And further: *If one seeks me through form or sound, that person walks the deviant path and cannot see the Tathāgata.* The Tathāgata is the self; if obscured by sound and form, one cannot perceive the original true Buddha. Generally, this scripture aims at knowing destiny and seeing nature as the ultimate attainment—its essence lies in steadfast practice.

The above Jade Inscription of Heavenly Seal comprises sixty characters, descending from the Míluó Heaven to govern the Ninth Rampart’s Lord of Flourishing Virtue.

*The Mysterious Covenant* states: When the Dao is perfected, one ascends to the rank of Sacred Venerable. The form transforms into cloud talismans, the talismans disperse into Mysterious Qi, the qi gathers into true form, and the qi conceals itself as true qi. Gazing upon it, one sees the Jade Talisman; listening, one hears the Jade Tone. It is inconceivable, its merit vast and profound—visible yet unseen, audible yet unheard, tangible yet unattainable. Such is the profound and ultimate Daoist lineage, the *Great Cavern Immortal Scripture*, which here attains great penetration.

**Conclusion of the Scripture**

The Jade Palace Dao Lord said: My master, the Celestial Venerable of Primordial Beginning, bestowed upon me this *Great Cavern Immortal Scripture*, its purport profoundly mysterious.

The Numinous Treasure Heavenly Worthy said: My master, the Celestial Venerable of Primordial Beginning, bestowed upon me this *Great Cavern Immortal Scripture*, its purport profoundly mysterious. The Numinous Treasure especially emphasizes its mystery—how could it be easily known? Without dual cultivation of inner and outer, without natural concentration and stillness, and without unobstructed insight, how could one explore its depths, probe its secrets, and reach its farthest truths? This scripture conceals the hidden truths of celestial perfected beings, shared alike by gods and humans.

**The Wondrous Gate of Daoist Cultivation:**

The wondrous practice of Daoist cultivation begins with upholding precepts, then proceeds to meditation. Once precepts and meditation are established, one practices qi to gather spirit and brightness. When breath is stilled and qi congealed, spirit and brightness naturally arrive. With their arrival, wisdom-light arises—this is the ultimate attainment.

**Initial Meditation and Breath Unification**
*The Sutra of Perfect Enlightenment* states: *Unobstructed pure wisdom arises from meditative concentration.* If one is not still and settled, how can wisdom-light shine forth? *The Lotus Sutra* says: *In a secluded place, gather the mind and dwell unmoving like Mount Sumeru.* It also says: *When the waters of meditation are clear, the pearl of the mind appears of itself.* The ancients said: *To seek the pearl, the waves must be still—stirring the water makes retrieval difficult.* Thus, meditation and concentration.

The Confucians say: *Only after stillness can there be concentration; only after concentration can there be contemplation.* The heart must be still to concentrate, then to contemplate. These three teachings converge in principle.

**Embryonic Breathing Method**
Eat sparingly, speak little, silently count within the mind, and focus on the breath at the nostrils. A thousand breaths of Great Harmony—if a single thought stirs, it cannot be called Great Harmony. Disharmony breeds other afflictions. Only when not a single thought moves can it be called harmony. Count the breaths to a thousand for one cycle; a thousand cycles complete the Great Harmony.

**Inner Observation and True Transformation**
Within inner observation, one can transform one’s true self—ascending to heaven, descending to earth, coming and going without end. "Inner observation" means internal vision. When merit and practice are complete, one can inwardly perceive the five viscera and outwardly gather the ten thousand spirits, enabling transformation.

**Detachment from Phenomena and Dissolution of Dust**
This body has no relation to the other; the other is the other, the self is the self—this is what is meant by departing from all extremes. The Śākya tradition states: *If one fills three thousand great thousand-worlds with the seven treasures to offer in charity, it does not compare to upholding this scripture, even four lines of verse—this merit surpasses the former.* According to *The Diamond Sutra*, there are two four-line verses: the first says, *If one seeks me through form...*; the latter says: *All conditioned phenomena are like dreams, illusions, bubbles, shadows, like dew and lightning—thus should they be contemplated.*

*Laozi* says: *The greatest image is formless.* And: *The great Dao is formless.* Confucius said: *The spirit has no direction, change has no form—silent and unmoving, yet responsive and penetrating.* Carefully examining the teachings of the three sages, though their methods differ, their essence is one.

This scripture is this mind. If one thoroughly investigates its four-line verse, this body is but an illusory aggregation of conditioned phenomena, all empty constructs. If one pursues this path to perceive the original source, one must let go of both ends and engage in a fierce battle on the precipice. Only when the root of life is suddenly severed is one truly home—this is what is meant by detachment from phenomena and dissolution of dust.

The ancients said: *The body of the ten thousand phenomena does not cling to a single thread.* Truly, these words are apt.

**Five Thousand Cycles of Primordial Union**
Gather the Great Harmony to complete five thousand cycles. Though the number is vast, it begins with one—like grinding a brick into a mirror or sharpening a pestle into a needle. Only here does one see the work accomplished, complete and lacking nothing. As the saying goes: *Without sufficient effort, the elixir will not form.*

**Sitting in Stillness, Standing in Oblivion**
Sitting, there is existence; standing, there is none—returning to the boundless, the indistinct, the soundless, the scentless, the thoughtless, the effortless. Where are voices and laughter to be found? The *Daoist Scripture* says: *Sitting in liberation, standing in oblivion*—like the monk Pǔhuà, who shook his bell and ascended to heaven.

**Great Concentration and Complete Perfection**
When the heart’s qi is in great concentration, never wavering, there is no disturbance from hunger, thirst, cold, or heat. Weapons cannot harm, venomous creatures cannot sting, water cannot drown, fire cannot burn. Sight does not see, hearing does not hear, what is near is not perceived before, what follows is not seen behind. Only then is it called *sitting in stillness, standing in oblivion, great concentration, and complete perfection*. Even heaven and earth, ghosts and spirits cannot fathom it. To this day, many ancient worthies in the world sit in meditation without wishing to emerge from concentration—such as Dīshuǐ of Jìnyún in Shu and Pǔ’ān of the Fourth Patriarch in Jiangnan, who were seen in the world yet dwelled in the Dao. This is great concentration and complete perfection.

**Marvelous Practice and Spiritual Penetration**

Marvelous Practice refers to the *Ten Immortals and Ten Gates* of the upper scroll, the *Ten Caverns and Ten Roots* of the middle scroll, and the *Ten Flower-Contemplation Gates* of the lower scroll, along with the wondrous fruits of the *Eight Trigrams and Six Positions*—all termed the *Great Cavern Marvelous Practice*. Spiritual Penetration arises when Marvelous Practice is cultivated to perfection, naturally attaining profound spiritual communion.

First is *Penetration of Qi*. At the outset, one learns *embryonic breathing*, regulating the inhalation and exhalation of qi until their count is known. When the breath is held for 1,200 cycles, this is called *Great Embryonic Breathing*. The method of Great Embryonic Breathing by the ancient Ge Zhichuan corresponds to the *Sūrangama Sūtra*’s *discernment of thought-counting*.

Next is *Penetration of Spirit*. When one’s primordial spirit merges with the myriad spirits and true qi harmonizes, the spirit’s transformations become unfathomable. This does not mean communing with external spirits—such are demonic illusions that corrupt virtue and must never be engaged. Let them depart of their own accord.

Finally is *Penetration of Spirit*. Master Cheng Yi of Luoyang, in his commentary on the *Doctrine of the Mean*, speaks of *foreknowledge*: "Even figures like Dong Wujing of Shu Mountain possess it, yet this is but a minor attainment. At its utmost, a single point of numinous clarity becomes as limpid as a mirror, reflecting the workings of heaven and earth, the auspicious and inauspicious, regret and remorse—all manifest within it. Good and evil are known in advance, for this is the *Way of Utmost Sincerity* in the *Doctrine of the Mean*, what the Buddhist scriptures call *liberated knowledge and vision*, and what the Confucian classics describe as *the extension of knowledge through the investigation of things*."

Its beauty resides within, yet flows through the four limbs, manifesting in one’s undertakings. All arises from the self’s spirit and qi attaining spiritual penetration—nothing comes from without.

**The Ten Penetrations Culminate in Perfection**

In a former dream, I was gored by an ox—this was none other than my own original destiny-star. Master Weishan said: "Dwelling at Weishan for twenty years, I have tended but a single water-buffalo. If it strays into the grass, I lead it out; if it tramples the crops, I strike it. Now, I see it clearly in the open, and though I chase it, it does not flee." For over thirty years, I too have guarded the pen, and only now have I glimpsed the ox. The labor was not easy. From the initial stabilization of breath to the perfection of the Ten Penetrations, no stage may be neglected. When one is penetrated, all are penetrated. Ghosts and spirits possess the Five Penetrations; buddhas possess the Six Penetrations; celestial immortals possess the Ten Penetrations.

**The Dao Complete, Ascending to the Celestial Court**

When merit is fulfilled and the Dao complete, one ascends to the Purple Court, sheds the mortal frame, and the true spirit soars aloft. Though the ancients spoke of *ascending with one’s dwelling*—flesh and bone together—such impure, turbid forms cannot appear before the Emperor. They must be concealed in famous mountains or cast into distant seas. Only the singular true spirit, riding qi in flight, may traverse the Three Realms and ascend to the Jade Capital. The Buddhist teaching that *the fully endowed physical body cannot behold the Tathāgata* expresses the same principle—like the Dark Emperor concealing his golden bones on Mount Wudang.

**Traversing the Three Realms, Wandering the Three Clarities**

The Three Clarities lie above the Three Realms, within the boundless *Daluo Heaven*. Though lofty, they may be traversed. Those who cultivate the *Great Cavern* transcend the Three Realms entirely.

**Attaining the Rank of the Great Cavern, the Celestial Sovereign of Heavenly Unity**

The Celestial Sovereign of the Great Cavern presides above all heavens, the rank to which the adept ascends. *Heavenly Unity* is the *Great Mystery*, the realm attainable by the highest immortals and perfected beings.

**The Six Perfections and Ten Penetrations, Myriad Practices Perfected**

The Six Perfections and myriad practices, the Six Positions and Ten Penetrations, are brought to perfect completion, flawless and whole. Each barrier and ford must be broken through one by one before true suchness is revealed.

**A Thousand Harmonies, Ten Thousand Unions—Naturally Attaining Perfection**

The *Scripture of Salvation* states: "The Dao of *revolving wind and blending union* values harmony above all. If one can achieve a thousand harmonies and ten thousand unions, the Dao of true immortality is naturally attained."

In the preceding three ranks, "true" denotes *sincerity without falsehood*. If one can *turn inward and be sincere*, there is no greater joy. For what is bestowed upon humanity is the *heavenly perfection of complete virtue*. Yet as years advance, it is obscured by worldly desires, the original source eroded, like flowing water rushing ever onward without return. Thus, the Primordial Heavenly King, the Jade Court Dao Lord, and the Great Mystery Dao Father—the Three Masters, father and sons—awakened good causes and established this dialogue to deliver beings.

Yet this scripture embodies the profound mysteries of the Three Treasures, its principles subtle and recondite, difficult to fathom. I have ventured, in the course of its verses, to append my humble insights, unworthy though they be. Drawing from a lifetime of learning—transmitted heart-to-heart and mouth-to-mouth—I have appended them here. Though the text’s expressions vary, now direct, now circuitous, revealing both nature and destiny, its great principle may be summed in six words: *settle heavenly principle, guard one’s fundamental duty*.

Some may say: "To reveal secret teachings is a grave transgression." I reply: "I would rather accept the consequences, for my wish is that beneath the round canopy of heaven, within the four seas, all who see or hear may cultivate and realize the *Great Cavern Immortal Scripture of Wenchang*, thereby above aiding the sage’s boundless longevity, continuing the legacy of Yao, Shun, the Yellow Emperor, and Xuanyuan; and below blessing the common people across the eight wilds, transforming all lands into realms of Yu, Ji, Yan, and Zeng. May all people share in virtue, and all things partake in benevolence—this is my aspiration. What should I fear?"

I, Qi, bow twice and respectfully inscribe this.

The *Mysterious Concordance* states: "The *Great Cavern Immortal Scripture* was expounded by the Primordial Heavenly King for the Jade Court Dao Lord, revealing the primordial, unfolding the ultimate, and bridging the celestial and human, that all might attain immortality. It is the true essential text. When scholars recite it, they awaken and ascend as immortals; when ghosts and spirits recite it, they awaken and ascend as perfected beings; when ordinary people recite it, they awaken and attain longevity; when wandering souls hear it, their souls and spirits revive, forever escaping mortal peril and ascending to heaven. The withered, aged, and infirm who hear it extend their years; infants and divine youths who hear it gain wisdom. Superior adepts who obtain it ascend to the Jade Clarity, attain the rank of sage, and unite with the Dao."

The Jade Clarity Boundless Perfection, Supreme Writs of the Wenchang Great Cavern Immortal Scripture, Scroll Ten

● "秀" is likely a miswriting for "流."
● "玉清" is an error for "玉清."
